<a id="src-00039"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_metzia/70.txt`

Bava Metzia 70 - When Interest is Allowed (Finds)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjlxdlWdnkdAi4rVotkohrwu03S3sWbCb6mx7N_7sZc3DDcr_xJEoVqwAJo7Po2PKXbC0t4M2L5_pyhE_qdQkhWLStE15nTt_RkUnVzjyj9D_7UKecARmQlaPyxcP1DTpGOA_vruDm7msRp/s1600-h/Bartolom%C3%A9+Esteban+Murillo+-+Young+Beggar.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5354814374078994146" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjlxdlWdnkdAi4rVotkohrwu03S3sWbCb6mx7N_7sZc3DDcr_xJEoVqwAJo7Po2PKXbC0t4M2L5_pyhE_qdQkhWLStE15nTt_RkUnVzjyj9D_7UKecARmQlaPyxcP1DTpGOA_vruDm7msRp/s320/Bartolom%C3%A9+Esteban+Murillo+-+Young+Beggar.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 320px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 246px;" /></a><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">One is not allowed to invest in a business venture in which he shares in profits but not losses or in which his proportionate share of profits is greater than that of his losses. The guaranteed part of the investment is then a loan, and its profit is a form of interest prohibited by the Sages.</span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">However, one is allowed to invest the money of orphans where they stand to gain more than to lose by a court appointee.</span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">One is allowed to loan on interest to a non-Jew. In fact, there is nothing wrong with charging interest, but the Torah wants all Jews to behave like family members.</span></div><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">Art: Young Beggar by Bartolome Esteban Murillo</span></div><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><br /></div>
<div>
</div>

---

### content/bava_metzia/71.txt
<a id="src-00040"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_metzia/71.txt`

Bava Metzia 71 - Taking Interest from Non-Jews is also Prohibited (Finds)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEii9AY16F7tgLdUW6UVWIRvSVEFKBR8yrLppd-TzZg-pfOfw5J2CGTm0E_qQYPCtwfIZ49VcuZLAskJNJ2dxwZ8_ZplUFIj3DGYT2QYzTrDVJybP81u-KwNvoENhIrKfWnx7eBAQap_mhSG/s1600-h/Simeon+Solomon+-+King+Solomon.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5355011131014500226" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEii9AY16F7tgLdUW6UVWIRvSVEFKBR8yrLppd-TzZg-pfOfw5J2CGTm0E_qQYPCtwfIZ49VcuZLAskJNJ2dxwZ8_ZplUFIj3DGYT2QYzTrDVJybP81u-KwNvoENhIrKfWnx7eBAQap_mhSG/s320/Simeon+Solomon+-+King+Solomon.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 320px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 274px;" /></a><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">King Solomon and his court prohibited taking interest from non-Jews, as it says in Proverbs, "</span><a href="http://bible.cc/proverbs/28-8.htm"><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">One who increases his wealth by interest collects it for he who favors the poor</span></a><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">"- and who will distribute the interest to the poor after the usurer's demise. </span><br />
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div>
<div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">This prohibition is because if the financier becomes used to taking interest, he may come to take it from Jews, too. Excluded are cases of minor interest, "enough to live on," and Torah scholars who know the law and will not come to take interest from the Jews. Later on, taking interest from non-Jews became permitted since it was not possible otherwise.</span></div><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">Art: King Solomon by Simeon Solomon</span></div>

---

### content/bava_metzia/72.txt
<a id="src-00041"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_metzia/72.txt`

Bava Metzia 72 - Guarantor and Loan Assumption (Finds)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiCKj5ep3t5OADfpbQ-3XwTrTgSWJfPAKOKt7VmgyLMtw2otZkZ4UefxxbyPZMHRLdSeiKaTKJtDx8rBFxnfeVUVQb8viBOKYU3tTIayykfk3BU06U9h3H3_GLZ9oDZnbwXBOTm-OlsAesC/s1600-h/Rudolph+Ernst+-+A+Hard+Bargain.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5355438125110226050" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiCKj5ep3t5OADfpbQ-3XwTrTgSWJfPAKOKt7VmgyLMtw2otZkZ4UefxxbyPZMHRLdSeiKaTKJtDx8rBFxnfeVUVQb8viBOKYU3tTIayykfk3BU06U9h3H3_GLZ9oDZnbwXBOTm-OlsAesC/s320/Rudolph+Ernst+-+A+Hard+Bargain.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 224px; margin: 0px 10px 10px 0px; width: 320px;" /></a><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">One may act as a guarantor for an interest-bearing loan advanced by a non-Jew to a Jew, structured so that there is no interest payment if the borrower pays back to the guarantor.</span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">One may assume an interest-bearing loan given by a non-Jew to a Jew, but the non-Jew must agree, for otherwise, one would, in fact, be paying interest to the first borrower, who would then be paying it to the lender.</span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">If a non-Jew lent money on interest to a Jew and then converted, he may still collect interest if, before his conversion, he establishes it as a new loan, in the amount of principal plus interest.</span></div><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">Art:&nbsp;Rudolph Ernst - A Hard Bargain</span></div>
<div>
</div>
<div>
<br /></div>

---

### content/bava_metzia/73.txt
<a id="src-00042"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_metzia/73.txt`

Bava Metzia 73 - Forward Contracts with High Risk (Finds)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjOY69X6IdzfujU7n-yYUErUj_iy-XkDR9m3q1P0bM8bH5HTDCMjK1JGTP2kn6tQaodwIHbGKvn4eRtk2pry9cRc98-ByPLAhuHkmc851V7ZsTR6mhB1PdeE3ouakNMl0vZklavPOrP9SPd/s1600-h/John+Frederick+Lewis+-+Figures+and+Animals+in+a+Vineyard.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5355811070326901458" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjOY69X6IdzfujU7n-yYUErUj_iy-XkDR9m3q1P0bM8bH5HTDCMjK1JGTP2kn6tQaodwIHbGKvn4eRtk2pry9cRc98-ByPLAhuHkmc851V7ZsTR6mhB1PdeE3ouakNMl0vZklavPOrP9SPd/s320/John+Frederick+Lewis+-+Figures+and+Animals+in+a+Vineyard.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 255px; margin: 0px 10px 10px 0px; width: 320px;" /></a><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">Before the grapes ripen, a buyer can pay in advance for the wine yield of a vineyard. He pays much less than the estimated value of the wine. </span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">Rav forbids it: since the wine will be worth much more in the future, it resembles a "reward for waiting," or interest. Shmuel permits it: sometimes a misfortune can befall the vineyard, and the reduced price is due to accepting risk. And Rav? – The slight chance of loss does not justify the significant price reduction. The law follows Rav. But Rav agrees to Shmuel, where harvesting is done with the aid of oxen because of the high risk to the oxen.</span></div>
<div><br /></div><div>Art: Figures and Animals in a Vineyard by John Frederick Lewis</div>

---

### content/bava_metzia/74.txt
<a id="src-00043"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_metzia/74.txt`

Bava Metzia 74 - Commodity Loans (Finds)
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: 130%;"><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiZOKngsbygOyQS8jRC6j1K_yGmzpYIJGYAiP79CmnoGew6h8sm2nO5ZXFV286KB6ciInYBbtbO4CaLOvbmHNpjeOq4ZYizN3zFB5Tg5SIiEUXFSb6ftjhISLlUpzAlUqZ4OZ6sV5cpFWdw3pIc47thS4DQymJz08SGeF8scCEMzybzKI0JgD9aHuHgmYFf/s600/Vincent%20Van%20Gogh%20-%20Still%20Life%20With%20Two%20Sacks%20And%20A%20Bottle.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" data-original-height="444" data-original-width="600" height="237" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiZOKngsbygOyQS8jRC6j1K_yGmzpYIJGYAiP79CmnoGew6h8sm2nO5ZXFV286KB6ciInYBbtbO4CaLOvbmHNpjeOq4ZYizN3zFB5Tg5SIiEUXFSb6ftjhISLlUpzAlUqZ4OZ6sV5cpFWdw3pIc47thS4DQymJz08SGeF8scCEMzybzKI0JgD9aHuHgmYFf/s320/Vincent%20Van%20Gogh%20-%20Still%20Life%20With%20Two%20Sacks%20And%20A%20Bottle.jpg" width="320" /></a></div>Commodity loans - such as a loan of a bag of wheat to be repaid with a bag of wheat later - are generally prohibited. If the price of the commodity increases in the interim, the lender will receive back more value than he lent, which constitutes interest. The correct way to give such loans is to estimate the value of the bag when it is given and later return the amount of wheat of equal value.</span><br />
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: 130%;"><br /></span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: 130%;">Nevertheless, a person may lend his sharecropper wheat to be used as seeds to repay the same amount of wheat after the harvest. In this case, it is not a commodity loan but the terms of the shareholder agreement.&nbsp;</span></div><div><span style="font-size: 20.8px;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: 20.8px;">Art: Still Life With Two Sacks And A Bottle by Vincent Van Gogh</span><span style="font-size: 130%;">&nbsp;</span></div>

---

### content/bava_metzia/75.txt
<a id="src-00044"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_metzia/75.txt`

Bava Metzia 75 - When Commodity Loans are Allowed (Finds)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjNZLtmAy9GQacp35nth953rwG8QMR3YXsvWQZ1e_fSapKGwjycKTpkgmu7nVKyjGjyeFn9SGj8x7tr8LwbmCdLXgWXRfUBZg0ZhyphenhyphengMBgwkW0QUzXpn-uyxGvC9va5zml0Gpy_KUVyAhavR/s1600-h/Bernardo+Strozzi+-+The+Delivery+of+the+Keys+to+St.+Peter.JPG" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5356586036845599090" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjNZLtmAy9GQacp35nth953rwG8QMR3YXsvWQZ1e_fSapKGwjycKTpkgmu7nVKyjGjyeFn9SGj8x7tr8LwbmCdLXgWXRfUBZg0ZhyphenhyphengMBgwkW0QUzXpn-uyxGvC9va5zml0Gpy_KUVyAhavR/s320/Bernardo+Strozzi+-+The+Delivery+of+the+Keys+to+St.+Peter.JPG" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 235px; margin: 0px 10px 10px 0px; width: 320px;" /></a><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">Although </span><a href="http://community.livejournal.com/talmud_daily/20490.html"><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">commodity loans are generally prohibited</span></a><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">, a person may say to his fellow, "Lend me a bag of wheat until my son comes back to unlock my wheat or until I find the key." It is deemed as if the lender acquires the other wheat right away, and consequently, if its value increases, it is as though the lender's own wheat increases, and there is no question of interest.</span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">Nevertheless, Hillel prohibits it. Hillel also wanted to prohibit a woman from lending a loaf to her friend, to be repaid with another loaf unless they assessed the value at the time of the loan, but the Sages disagreed with him.</span></div><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">Art:&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">The Delivery of the Keys to St. Peter by&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">Bernardo Strozzi</span></div>
<div>
</div>
<div>
<br /></div>

---

### content/bava_metzia/76.txt
<a id="src-00045"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_metzia/76.txt`

Bava Metzia 76 - Hiring Craftsmen (Finds)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhSNbt3-K4Znc777TxwSNEij0rN7vU78BaJwwoK1VZ17GA6U9iaoVaHjgZC6MJZw1RVQqxbcQyENF6_myyq1SbZBDz31M-9hUr6Mbc5SF1e_hRR06EMw7TfBup2IP8o75Ys9SBTSO8m06z6/s1600-h/Adriaen+van+Ostade+-+A+Flute+Player.JPG" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5356898620938407970" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhSNbt3-K4Znc777TxwSNEij0rN7vU78BaJwwoK1VZ17GA6U9iaoVaHjgZC6MJZw1RVQqxbcQyENF6_myyq1SbZBDz31M-9hUr6Mbc5SF1e_hRR06EMw7TfBup2IP8o75Ys9SBTSO8m06z6/s320/Adriaen+van+Ostade+-+A+Flute+Player.JPG" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 320px; margin: 0px 10px 10px 0px; width: 249px;" /></a><br />
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">If one hires craftsmen and they deceive one another - they can only have grudges but no monetary claims. </span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">For example, if one hired wagon drivers to deliver flutes for a bride or a funeral, or he hired them to do anything which, if not performed, would cause a loss and they reneged on their commitment and refused to work, then if he has to hire other workers at higher wages, they will have to pay the difference, or he can trick them into working for him.</span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">If they renege on their commitment in mid-task, their wages are calculated in the way least favorable to them.</span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div>
<div>
Art: A Flute Player by Adriaen van Ostade</div>

---

### content/bava_metzia/77.txt
<a id="src-00046"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_metzia/77.txt`

Bava Metzia 77 – Labor Laws (Finds)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg4kdnWkVS2VIx8kd2g4j6_mLuEhxod-KWvo_o0CXrtyauf6zqbkWgzaPGHthNCgfOeas6HkymSJRa0H9rWb36_JQ2hgDKfh9aFixr-rEObhViyBSMaJU6Gz1NpwtCUKxL-jKDKW0SKXQ7H/s1600-h/George+Wesley+Bellows+-+Dock+Builders.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5357443918093808578" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg4kdnWkVS2VIx8kd2g4j6_mLuEhxod-KWvo_o0CXrtyauf6zqbkWgzaPGHthNCgfOeas6HkymSJRa0H9rWb36_JQ2hgDKfh9aFixr-rEObhViyBSMaJU6Gz1NpwtCUKxL-jKDKW0SKXQ7H/s320/George+Wesley+Bellows+-+Dock+Builders.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 250px; margin: 0px 10px 10px 0px; width: 320px;" /></a><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">Hourly workers can stop working with their employer at any time, according to the Torah commandment "...</span><a href="http://bible.cc/leviticus/25-55.htm"><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">since the children of Israel are My slaves</span></a><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">..." - but not slaves to my slaves. They receive hourly wages for the time they have already worked. </span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">Contractors hired to perform a specific task can also quit at any time. However, if the employer has to  hire other workers at a higher rate to complete the job, the difference is deducted from the contractors' pay.</span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">If not finishing the task causes a loss, the employer can obtain a refund of significantly higher wages of replacement workers - from the first workers' pay and their tools, if he has them.&nbsp;</span></div><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">Art:&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">Dock Builders by&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">George Wesley Bellows</span></div>

---

### content/bava_metzia/78.txt
<a id="src-00047"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_metzia/78.txt`

Bava Metzia 78 – Rental Agreements (Finds)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg4rq4CexCXDLx6KCbQtuSLDyTWJiD0jy3YPX1BHd1dInkJdn4_DYek3-LGuoMPrQ76KJ96pE8IilP7YoOIIkhf1jeV26yD0wIDCzOsLV1q6p-64dHAP70atZwfPd_1X0kWbam4x5isxZnC/s1600-h/Eva+Gonzales+-+The+Donkey+Ride+-+1880.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5357628793448612450" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg4rq4CexCXDLx6KCbQtuSLDyTWJiD0jy3YPX1BHd1dInkJdn4_DYek3-LGuoMPrQ76KJ96pE8IilP7YoOIIkhf1jeV26yD0wIDCzOsLV1q6p-64dHAP70atZwfPd_1X0kWbam4x5isxZnC/s320/Eva+Gonzales+-+The+Donkey+Ride+-+1880.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 255px; margin: 0px 10px 10px 0px; width: 320px;" /></a><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">If one rents a donkey to lead it on a mountain and leads it in a valley instead, or vice versa, and the donkey dies on the way, the renter is liable.</span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">If one rents a donkey to lead it on a mountain and leads it in a valley instead, then if the animal slips, the renter is not liable since slipping is even more likely in the mountain. He was responsible if the animal died of heat since the valley was a warm place surrounded by cool mountains.</span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">If the donkey was temporarily put into the king's services, the renter waits for its return, but if it dies, the owner provides another donkey.</span></div><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">Art:&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">The Donkey Ride by&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">Eva Gonzales</span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div>
<div>
<br /></div>

---

### content/bava_metzia/79.txt
<a id="src-00048"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_metzia/79.txt`

Bava Metzia 79 - Boat Rentals (Finds)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEj84m9BzbhR_dirh8HfH5YF0bB4ZlP-cp1XA_nkgxBWUwla23BnTCtJNYCAo7A3h1cmBQuAjvWWxWryU7e38mdNRvS3w916RHh9163S8UVJDqtBtCeMX3RR7XSQppcv-Vrk2DCeq4rLtrBt/s1600-h/Claude+Oscar+Monet+-Boat+At+Low+Tide+At+Fecamp.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5357966512318079634" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEj84m9BzbhR_dirh8HfH5YF0bB4ZlP-cp1XA_nkgxBWUwla23BnTCtJNYCAo7A3h1cmBQuAjvWWxWryU7e38mdNRvS3w916RHh9163S8UVJDqtBtCeMX3RR7XSQppcv-Vrk2DCeq4rLtrBt/s320/Claude+Oscar+Monet+-Boat+At+Low+Tide+At+Fecamp.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 320px; margin: 0px 10px 10px 0px; width: 233px;" /></a><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">Regarding one who rents a boat to transport wine and it sinks midway through the voyage, Rabbi Nathan said that if the renter had already paid the rental fee, he could not have it back, but if the renter had not yet paid the fee, he does not pay it.</span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">What are the circumstances? If the contract was for a specific boat and any wine, the renter should get back the fee since the owner cannot provide the boat.  And if the contract was for any boat and specific wine, the owner should keep the fee since the renter can't provide the same wine.</span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">However, the case here is that the contract was for a specific boat and a specific wine. Since each party can blame the other for not fulfilling the contract, the payment stays where it is now.</span></div><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">Art:&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">Boat At Low Tide At Fecamp by&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">Claude Oscar Monet</span></div>

---

### content/bava_metzia/8.txt
<a id="src-00049"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_metzia/8.txt`

Bava Metzia 8 - One Lifts a Found Object, Intending to Acquire it for his Fellow (Finds)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiYnOQKgLWmZrIl2fAIc06QCn-jKkoUVcOSw8ewrAimTqboqLvIzoeUxgawizdsg5Uf5JkrUiNCG9W_RKtqFH-SaCqipMawL2dlOJ8HvHx7dD5zfa-pwWlKybqa1Fd4wWXrGlAv1-UlJR90/s1600-h/John+William+Waterhouse+-+Maidens+picking+Flowers+by+a+Stream+%5BStudy%5D.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5331627728678028162" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiYnOQKgLWmZrIl2fAIc06QCn-jKkoUVcOSw8ewrAimTqboqLvIzoeUxgawizdsg5Uf5JkrUiNCG9W_RKtqFH-SaCqipMawL2dlOJ8HvHx7dD5zfa-pwWlKybqa1Fd4wWXrGlAv1-UlJR90/s320/John+William+Waterhouse+-+Maidens+picking+Flowers+by+a+Stream+%5BStudy%5D.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 320px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 265px;" /></a>If one lifts up an object he found, intending to acquire it entirely for his fellow, then his fellow acquires it. This is true even though he deprives other potential finders of the object. It can be proved from <a href="http://community.livejournal.com/talmud_daily/2149.html">the case of two people who have found a garment</a>.<br />
<br />
There, each one is holding his end of the garment, and should his fellow drop it, the garment would partially rest on the floor, which would mean that our claimant has yet to acquire it since complete lifting is required. We must conclude that when they lift the garment, both intend to help the other acquire it.<div><br /></div><div>Art: Maidens Picking Flowers by a Stream [Study] by John William Waterhouse</div>

---

### content/bava_metzia/80.txt
<a id="src-00050"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_metzia/80.txt`

Bava Metzia 80 - Transportation Rentals (Finds)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjImTedmtrcvRjMd8PYxK9GpxpboVCOtMMbjPR7J0W6IyEoxhF0AyyyVJ2Pi1DmhTMfKGK82KiFWpstGnx5VVP0bCUynZEy2HLJw5LLaDBnxwKqeoBSDkDaDFq5hqAhUg6H3ZWihQd8emYU/s1600-h/Marc+Chagall+-+The+Green+Donkey.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5358162372157443634" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjImTedmtrcvRjMd8PYxK9GpxpboVCOtMMbjPR7J0W6IyEoxhF0AyyyVJ2Pi1DmhTMfKGK82KiFWpstGnx5VVP0bCUynZEy2HLJw5LLaDBnxwKqeoBSDkDaDFq5hqAhUg6H3ZWihQd8emYU/s320/Marc+Chagall+-+The+Green+Donkey.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 248px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 320px;" /></a><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">If one rented a donkey on which to bring wheat and he brought barley instead - the renter is liable for the injury to the donkey. Barley is lighter than wheat, so the renter first loaded the same volume of barley as wheat but then loaded some more to bring the weight up to the weight of wheat. However, the extra bulkiness of the load is hard on the donkey, which is why the renter is liable.</span><br />
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">With the same type of load as mentioned in the rental agreement, what is the amount of overload at which the renter becomes liable for injury? 1/30, and this applies to animals, boats, and human porters.</span></div><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">Art:&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">The Green Donkey by&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">Marc Chagall</span></div>
<div>
<br /></div>

---

### content/bava_metzia/81.txt
<a id="src-00051"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_metzia/81.txt`

Bava Metzia 81 - What Type of Guardian Are You? (Finds)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjevxuFlo5FF_UKTv0SD8yicLERX6Y2M7784qbbcb9mi2QfD1pLSfSI66DSJz4MlH1cQV5gcaKzWULY74N9-3G2A4um5fNOp0abpjYswbUtv3fLBHI2WdcPgcxH_O0X4vaSMsV3EqKyY3KX/s1600-h/Quiringh+Gerritsz.+van+Brekelenkam+-+Interior+with+Two+Men+by+the+Fireside+1664.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5358399075240914594" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjevxuFlo5FF_UKTv0SD8yicLERX6Y2M7784qbbcb9mi2QfD1pLSfSI66DSJz4MlH1cQV5gcaKzWULY74N9-3G2A4um5fNOp0abpjYswbUtv3fLBHI2WdcPgcxH_O0X4vaSMsV3EqKyY3KX/s320/Quiringh+Gerritsz.+van+Brekelenkam+-+Interior+with+Two+Men+by+the+Fireside+1664.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 320px; margin: 0px 10px 10px 0px; width: 242px;" /></a><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">All craftsmen are considered paid guardians. Therefore, they are liable for loss or damage due to their negligence, or even not due to their negligence, provided that the loss was not unavoidable, such as theft. </span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">Once the craftsman says to the one who hired him, "Take your property and bring the money that is due to me," he is considered an unpaid guardian, liable only for loss or damage due to negligence.</span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">One who lends money to another against security is considered a paid guardian regarding the security. The lender is permitted to rent the poor man's security to others to reduce the debt because he is as one returning lost property to its owner.</span></div>
<div>
<br /></div><div>Art: Interior with Two Men by the Fireside by Quiringh Gerritsz. van Brekelenkam</div>

---

### content/bava_metzia/82.txt
<a id="src-00052"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_metzia/82.txt`

Bava Metzia 82 - Porter Breaks a Keg (Finds)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhq5dBrS4s34jXMrq3rtct_fBD8YPut0sUdc3NBCHZQaZOTPfiEfSCfjlWrwNyBjOIaQ4_-Q_mDuMbu355qBDIvFYA2ZHt2vEdVIEWhn7nFeVzIU59BsoZ3J64mYv7Mz9_iQnRVtlZvQr-R/s1600-h/Ludwig+Passini+-+A+Young+Venetian+Water-Carrier.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5358776773472543874" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhq5dBrS4s34jXMrq3rtct_fBD8YPut0sUdc3NBCHZQaZOTPfiEfSCfjlWrwNyBjOIaQ4_-Q_mDuMbu355qBDIvFYA2ZHt2vEdVIEWhn7nFeVzIU59BsoZ3J64mYv7Mz9_iQnRVtlZvQr-R/s320/Ludwig+Passini+-+A+Young+Venetian+Water-Carrier.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 320px; margin: 0px 10px 10px 0px; width: 212px;" /></a><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">When a porter carries someone’s keg from one place to another, he has the legal responsibility of a custodian. If he accidentally slips and breaks the keg, then Rabbi Meir says that whether he is paid or not, he can swear and free himself from liability.</span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">Rabbi Yehudah says that slipping is negligence. Therefore, a paid porter is liable - as any paid custodian - but an unpaid porter is not.</span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">And Rabbi Meir? He agrees that stumbling is considered negligence, but since people are usually not careful about it, the Rabbis made a decree that a porter can be absolved through an oath because otherwise, nobody will move a keg of his fellow. He swears that he did not break it deliberately.</span></div><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">Art:&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">A Young Venetian Water-Carrier by&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">Ludwig Passini</span></div>
<div>
<br /></div>

### content/bava_metzia/83.txt

**Source file:** `content/bava_metzia/83.txt`

Bava Metzia 83 - Negligent Porters Break a Keg of Wine (Finds)
<span style="font-size: 130%;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEipzNzOwhCOFdqTOM8gbmwZyWc8RoLzFa49aQb5z0mOje0RiewSavK8sLkxhyphenhyphen0YFEQ6SvxfTkIFMqIxrZdJGoXA22kbTp_GPQ3hkfm4lwyUv2grdy8JkgoXByN3e8x2YDA-FKpek-HRQVXX/s1600-h/William+Sartain+-+Algerian+Water+Carrier.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5359289593335582290" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEipzNzOwhCOFdqTOM8gbmwZyWc8RoLzFa49aQb5z0mOje0RiewSavK8sLkxhyphenhyphen0YFEQ6SvxfTkIFMqIxrZdJGoXA22kbTp_GPQ3hkfm4lwyUv2grdy8JkgoXByN3e8x2YDA-FKpek-HRQVXX/s320/William+Sartain+-+Algerian+Water+Carrier.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 320px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 218px;" /></a>Rabbah bar bar Chanan hired porters to carry a keg of wine, and they broke it through negligence, such as stumbling on level ground. Rabbah bar bar Chanan took their cloaks as payment.<br /><br />The porters went to Rav's court and told him about it. Rav told Rabbah bar bar Chanan, "Give them back their cloaks." "Is that the law?" - he asked. "Yes," - said Rav, quoting from Proverbs, "<a href="https://biblehub.com/proverbs/2-20.htm" target="_blank">So that&nbsp;you go on the path of good people</a>..."<br /><br />They said to Rav, "We are poor people, and we labored the entire day; we are starving and have nothing to eat." Rav told Rabbah bar bar Chanan, "Pay them their fee." "Is that the law?" - he asked. "Yes," - said Rav, quoting the end of the phrase, "...and keep the ways of the righteous."</span><div><span style="font-size: 130%;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: 130%;">Art:&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: 20.8px;">Algerian Water Carrier by&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: 130%;">William Sartain</span></div>

Bava Metzia 84 - Robber Knows his Trade (Finds)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEihX_gmNGEkzDxQ0PAqL2bsX4kauVjiGFNcs3rPOeNgMIoGJRxEpBZWVxLVVqlWM6hGG2jGzvcGN973Qiy66Sa3L8txaRXUkIz7Hg41ORnUAXhlL5m19uerapEYgY8VrBNXDYhJg9_D781Q/s1600-h/Henry+Scott+Tuke+-+Boys+Bathing,+1908.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5360039268404987074" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEihX_gmNGEkzDxQ0PAqL2bsX4kauVjiGFNcs3rPOeNgMIoGJRxEpBZWVxLVVqlWM6hGG2jGzvcGN973Qiy66Sa3L8txaRXUkIz7Hg41ORnUAXhlL5m19uerapEYgY8VrBNXDYhJg9_D781Q/s320/Henry+Scott+Tuke+-+Boys+Bathing,+1908.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 320px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 242px;" /></a><span style="font-size: 130%;">Rabbi Yochanan, who was extremely beautiful, was swimming in the river. Resh Lakish, a highwayman, mistook him for a  woman and jumped after. Rabbi Yochanan told Resh Lakish that he had a sister even more beautiful than him, and if Resh Lakish decided to study Torah, he could marry her.<br /><br />Resh Lakish became a great scholar. Once, they discussed when weapons are considered finished and therefore susceptible to ritual impurity. Rabbi Yochanan said, "When they are hardened," but Resh Lakish said, "When they are polished." Rabbi Yochanan said,&nbsp;<span style="font-size: 20.8px;">"</span>Robber knows his trade<span style="font-size: 20.8px;">"</span>&nbsp;- as praise, but Resh Lakish misunderstood and said,&nbsp;<span style="font-size: 20.8px;">"</span>And what have you given me? I was called Teacher among robbers also.<span style="font-size: 20.8px;">"</span>&nbsp;Rabbi Yochanan was displeased, and Resh Lakish died. Rabbi Yochanan was inconsolable about losing his student, and his mind became disturbed. The Sages asked for mercy on him, and he departed.</span><div><span style="font-size: 130%;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: 130%;">Art:&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: 20.8px;">Boys Bathing by&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: 130%;">Henry Scott Tuke</span></div>

### content/bava_metzia/85.txt
<a id="src-00055"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_metzia/85.txt`

Bava Metzia 85 - Teaching Torah to Children (Finds)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiVVl5fkDdISeOK-HrGgRceCtE9DReP9BMFM_eMEdKoAqrvGU80FFLxu3nbOaZ6xOIzOQGLQexwETwYnUwygqrNxep4mnr8_la0rpnq-XAF1nWocx9NLAwRGhn1dc8fLMVBbV5AP-BPe5Es/s1600-h/Marc+Chagall+-+The+Three+Candles.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5360298976589432274" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiVVl5fkDdISeOK-HrGgRceCtE9DReP9BMFM_eMEdKoAqrvGU80FFLxu3nbOaZ6xOIzOQGLQexwETwYnUwygqrNxep4mnr8_la0rpnq-XAF1nWocx9NLAwRGhn1dc8fLMVBbV5AP-BPe5Es/s320/Marc+Chagall+-+The+Three+Candles.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 320px; margin: 0px 10px 10px 0px; width: 233px;" /></a><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">Rabbi Tarfon used to take oaths, "May I bury my sons..." if something was false. After his death, Rebbi traveled to his locale and asked if he had any sons left. They told Rebbi that the son of Rabbi Tarfon's daughter was alive and that every harlot whose own price was two coins would hire him for eight. Rebbi told him, "If you repent, I will give you my daughter in marriage." He repented but did not marry her so that people would not say he repented just because of her.</span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">Why did Rebbi go to such lengths to teach his friends' children? The one who teaches his fellow's son Torah merits to learn in the Heavenly Academy, and the one who teaches the son of an ignoramus can cancel decrees that God makes.</span></div><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">Art: The Three Candles by Marc Chagall</span></div><div><br /></div>

---

Bava Metzia 86 – The Story of Rabbah Bar Nachmani (Finds)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiTuNLmr8ePf3-hPa3kv61GdkPLhMgNiLVRmgtqJ2UXDK36x6WXuL7chISMcwz9e510pxKTYPlubdaV94mDVMJPrcazIHx9N2Uxz_fgOv6LnmzYUVcZkhxOeLKTP8WHaOGzfGy5EfyqHh1S/s1600-h/Jacobello+Dalle+Masegne+-+Students.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5360556668464125618" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiTuNLmr8ePf3-hPa3kv61GdkPLhMgNiLVRmgtqJ2UXDK36x6WXuL7chISMcwz9e510pxKTYPlubdaV94mDVMJPrcazIHx9N2Uxz_fgOv6LnmzYUVcZkhxOeLKTP8WHaOGzfGy5EfyqHh1S/s320/Jacobello+Dalle+Masegne+-+Students.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 257px; margin: 0px 10px 10px 0px; width: 320px;" /></a><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">Slanderers told the king that there was a man among the Jews who made twelve thousand of them idle for two months a year by teaching them Torah, and Rabbah had to flee.</span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">Finally, he escaped to a marsh and studied there. In the Heavenly Academy, there was an argument about <a href="http://bible.cc/leviticus/13-38.htm">impurity connected to skin discolorations</a>. If a white hair grew on a white spot, it was impure. If a white spot appeared under a white hair, it was pure. What if it was not known which came first? God was saying it was pure, and the Academy ruled that it was impure. They called Rabbah to decide on the issue, and his soul ascended to heaven.</span></div><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">Art:&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">Students by&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">Jacobello Dalle Masegne</span></div>

---

### content/bava_metzia/87.txt
<a id="src-00057"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_metzia/87.txt`

Bava Metzia 87 - Workers Eat While Harvesting (Finds)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjl2Ol56gMt74Z8ZMnE1NTVZRufwEGW6KkoJ6fDWwT-V6PvUFlhAD70E5mPfJby5PA8p4HX-1W3Rhhhu05mYKbt8P7qnVMJyqqFCMBSwDSubEC_zI-L-QVZ0xZk9JftOsKZudxU2cxBo7vy/s1600-h/Vincent+Van+Gogh+-+The+Potato+Eaters.png" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5360975925493908178" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjl2Ol56gMt74Z8ZMnE1NTVZRufwEGW6KkoJ6fDWwT-V6PvUFlhAD70E5mPfJby5PA8p4HX-1W3Rhhhu05mYKbt8P7qnVMJyqqFCMBSwDSubEC_zI-L-QVZ0xZk9JftOsKZudxU2cxBo7vy/s320/Vincent+Van+Gogh+-+The+Potato+Eaters.png" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 226px; margin: 0px 10px 10px 0px; width: 320px;" /></a><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">Abraham asked that people would exhibit signs of aging, and "</span><a href="http://bible.cc/genesis/24-1.htm"><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">Now Abraham was old, well on in years</span></a>.<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">" Jakov asked for feebleness to precede death, and "</span><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><a href="http://bible.cc/genesis/48-1.htm">he said to Joseph, 'Behold! – your father is ill</a>.</span><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">" </span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><a href="http://bible.cc/deuteronomy/23-24.htm">Workers may eat from the employer's food while harvesting it</a>. They may also snack on it while working on it until the work process is complete and the tithing obligation starts. This is a Torah decree, and it applies only to something that grows from the ground.</span></div><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">A worker hired to weed out a field of onions can't eat them, and the same is true for one hired to repack fig cakes that have split apart.</span></div><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">Art: The Potato Eaters by Vincent Van Gogh</span></div>
<div>
<br /></div>
<div>
<br /></div>

### content/bava_metzia/88.txt
<a id="src-00058"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_metzia/88.txt`

Bava Metzia 88 - Ox Eats While Harvesting (Finds)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhADL2p4nRpAqt26Aru0oAKLqzFVUuwQm4DRcfEmo63BqCoVDtw9cakbrMmAiUZ_seZMkKH8J2mF4WajUd46JHktPdOWu_vD7x2deIbUIMcuDyE8VPC_J_f7bJME0I-L4YPu2Pdk0gbj91V/s1600-h/Camille+Pissarro+-+Apple+harvest+at+Eragny.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5361313328957397970" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhADL2p4nRpAqt26Aru0oAKLqzFVUuwQm4DRcfEmo63BqCoVDtw9cakbrMmAiUZ_seZMkKH8J2mF4WajUd46JHktPdOWu_vD7x2deIbUIMcuDyE8VPC_J_f7bJME0I-L4YPu2Pdk0gbj91V/s320/Camille+Pissarro+-+Apple+harvest+at+Eragny.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 263px; margin: 0px 10px 10px 0px; width: 320px;" /></a><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">By Torah law, one is obligated to tithe only the produce that he grows and consumes - "...</span><a href="http://bible.cc/deuteronomy/14-22.htm"><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">you shall surely tithe</span></a><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">..." and "...</span><a href="http://bible.cc/deuteronomy/14-23.htm"><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">you shall eat</span></a><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">...", but not produce that one sells. However, the Sages have established that a tithing obligation is fixed also when the produce is sold or when the Sabbath arrives.</span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">The obligation not to stop your workers from eating when harvesting is similar to the prohibition of  "</span><a href="http://bible.cc/deuteronomy/25-4.htm"><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">You shall not muzzle an ox in its threshing</span></a><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">," which applies to already harvested produce. Clearly, all animals are included, so mentioning "ox," the Torah teaches another law: just as a worker is allowed to eat unharvested produce, so is an ox.</span></div><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">Art:&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">Apple Harvest at Eragny by&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">Camille Pissarro</span></div>

---

### content/bava_metzia/89.txt
<a id="src-00059"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_metzia/89.txt`

Bava Metzia 89 – Workers Prepare to Eat More (Finds)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjKM6Y3lbOTMWq6fConrxA_Jc78L-xuly6iQg7DQw7Cicty-1uCAu6_NHHi09hZCNvUjmISi8QcSFqTJvKl5hAG8AvJ17R-pi0Fd9KbiGjSHq-lLVdg9hbEs6xfC1fV4cnx1LF1gQlG6dZJ/s1600-h/Camille+Pissarro+-+Harvest+At+Eragny.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5361426412694094322" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjKM6Y3lbOTMWq6fConrxA_Jc78L-xuly6iQg7DQw7Cicty-1uCAu6_NHHi09hZCNvUjmISi8QcSFqTJvKl5hAG8AvJ17R-pi0Fd9KbiGjSHq-lLVdg9hbEs6xfC1fV4cnx1LF1gQlG6dZJ/s320/Camille+Pissarro+-+Harvest+At+Eragny.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 266px; margin: 0px 10px 10px 0px; width: 320px;" /></a><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-family: 'Times New Roman';"></span><div style="border-bottom-width: 0px; border-left-width: 0px; border-right-width: 0px; border-top-width: 0px; border-width: 0px; font: 100% georgia, serif; margin-bottom: 0px; margin-left: 0px; margin-right: 0px; margin-top: 0px; margin: 0px; padding-bottom: 3px; padding-left: 3px; padding-right: 3px; padding-top: 3px; padding: 3px; text-align: left; width: auto;"><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">Workers who are </span><a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2009/07/bava-metzia-87-workers-eat-while.html"><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">partaking from the harvest</span></a><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"> naturally want to eat more, and their employer wants them to eat less.</span></span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">The employer is allowed to ply the workers with wine so they will not be inclined to eat many grapes. The workers are allowed to dip their bread in brine so that they will be inclined to eat more grapes. However, the workers are not allowed to eat anything along with the grapes to increase their appetite.</span></span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">Can the workers prepare their food in a more delectable way, such as toasting the grains or grapes on fire? This differs from preparing themselves to eat more and adding something else to the food. The last question remains unresolved at this time.</span></span></div><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></span></div><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">Art:&nbsp;</span></span><span style="font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;; font-size: large;">Harvest At Eragny by&nbsp;</span><span style="font-family: &quot;Times New Roman&quot;; font-size: large;">Camille Pissarro</span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><br /></span></div>
</div>

### content/bava_metzia/9.txt
<a id="src-00060"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_metzia/9.txt`

Bava Metzia 9 - Rider Sees a Find (Finds)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjbfC_PwG2vu4VvZVJ6fMdKVfWRa26Fu8IbjmMO1SrFAIbQemyYkCxS-HnnjrFXGkaOgjuITf4ra392rjZSJF7VSclAOiUNcN8OJNj0-M5QVenSjSSyrANiH1PqwocG0L2YYoFOD2L8YzBM/s1600-h/Renee+Magritte+-+Carte+Blanche.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5332045552074427634" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjbfC_PwG2vu4VvZVJ6fMdKVfWRa26Fu8IbjmMO1SrFAIbQemyYkCxS-HnnjrFXGkaOgjuITf4ra392rjZSJF7VSclAOiUNcN8OJNj0-M5QVenSjSSyrANiH1PqwocG0L2YYoFOD2L8YzBM/s320/Renee+Magritte+-+Carte+Blanche.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 320px; margin: 0px 10px 10px 0px; width: 252px;" /></a><div>If someone was riding on an animal and he sighted a find, an ownerless article, and he said to his fellow, who was standing nearby, "Give it to me," and that other person took it and then said, "I have acquired it for myself," - he has indeed acquired it for himself. It is implied that he had it in mind when he picked it up, not that he changed his mind later.</div><div><br /></div><div>If, however, after he had given it to the rider, he said, "I acquired it first," he has said nothing; that is, his claim is dismissed, and the rider may keep it.</div><div><br /></div><div>Art: Carte Blanche by Renee Magritte</div>

---

### content/bava_metzia/90.txt
<a id="src-00061"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_metzia/90.txt`

Bava Metzia 90 – Who Can Muzzle? (Finds)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEj1Ph2YUqIjWNiuClkzgi8GVcxQIGfT89hm5fUEgNxsjTZBbAuXGKV0XWmNg9tJswUsk-yvMoeD13YMQz6DfbB3D2nd1yTfYtFP5IvSoBOKKfaVjJnfMNtAksLbgOUWUB9WsYASxLcW8Hg6/s1600-h/Antonio+Pisano+-+Head+of+a+muzzled+dog,+from+the+The+Vallardi+Album.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5362088443571325426" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEj1Ph2YUqIjWNiuClkzgi8GVcxQIGfT89hm5fUEgNxsjTZBbAuXGKV0XWmNg9tJswUsk-yvMoeD13YMQz6DfbB3D2nd1yTfYtFP5IvSoBOKKfaVjJnfMNtAksLbgOUWUB9WsYASxLcW8Hg6/s320/Antonio+Pisano+-+Head+of+a+muzzled+dog,+from+the+The+Vallardi+Album.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 320px; margin: 0px 10px 10px 0px; width: 239px;" /></a><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">One IS allowed to muzzle an animal that is suffering from diarrhea. The prohibition of muzzling concerns what's good for its body, not the anguish it feels from being unable to eat.</span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">Can a man say to a non-Jew, "Muzzle my cow and thresh with it?" In general, can a Jew ask a non-Jew to do something forbidden to a Jew? The answer is "No," based on the following ruling. If a Jew had his <a href="http://bible.cc/leviticus/22-24.htm">bull stolen and castrated</a>, thus turning the bull into an ox, the Jew is penalized by having to sell the ox. </span><a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Q.E.D."><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">Q.E.D.</span></a><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"> </span></div>
<div>
<br /></div><div>Art: Head of a Muzzled Dog, by Antonio Pisano from the The Vallardi Album</div>

---

### content/bava_metzia/91.txt
<a id="src-00062"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_metzia/91.txt`

Bava Metzia 91 - Muzzling an Animal and Mother who is a Harlot (Finds)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgLbO8SQtXqrTxOx6_0tELO1lDFiTp3QsIsSNthkLxAUPgXQA4Ek4dLursViDoRjERx99PU1m9O8CNr9_vAfmkgO1Q5GkIwPGpgtPrJPsXNGxq2h8h9ndGdoQZS4oqkpznfAh0d7bX1ERpY/s1600-h/Charles+%C3%89mile+Jacque+-+Grazing+Sheep+with+a+Sheperdhess+Beyond.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5362629055244594930" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgLbO8SQtXqrTxOx6_0tELO1lDFiTp3QsIsSNthkLxAUPgXQA4Ek4dLursViDoRjERx99PU1m9O8CNr9_vAfmkgO1Q5GkIwPGpgtPrJPsXNGxq2h8h9ndGdoQZS4oqkpznfAh0d7bX1ERpY/s320/Charles+%C3%89mile+Jacque+-+Grazing+Sheep+with+a+Sheperdhess+Beyond.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 254px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 320px;" /></a><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">One who muzzles an animal and threshes with it receives lashes and must pay four Kavs (6 liters) for a cow and three Kavs for a donkey. But why should it be so? The rule is that one does not receive lashes  and pay money for the same crime!</span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">The proof is from the case of </span><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><a href="https://talmudilluminated.com/bava_kamma/bava_kamma71.html" target="_blank">a son consorting with his mother, who is a harlot</a></span><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><a href="https://talmudilluminated.com/bava_kamma/bava_kamma71.html" target="_blank">.</a> Since the son is liable to the death penalty for incest, he is not obligated to pay, and the sheep that he gave her should be considered a present, not a payment. Since the Torah forbade that sheep as a sacrifice, he must be legally obligated to pay, only that it is unenforceable in court. So, too, in the case of muzzling.</span></div><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">Art: Grazing Sheep with a Sheperdhess Beyond by&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">Charles Emile Jacque</span></div>

---

### content/bava_metzia/92.txt
<a id="src-00063"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_metzia/92.txt`

Bava Metzia 92 – How Much Can a Worker Eat? (Finds)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiVbesmK7Dp_UscKftR7_h8ih197abI11O500a9W7o70IYtuEUGdIv99V5iNTpb8Y_S9Cfi2DGE_zApV4HWzj_wuM4eKJIDpW_7XNHO4806_AbRbA9hyjJ6p-uI7Ql755Ds7E-vyBNoc3Fj/s1600-h/Luis+Eugenio+Melendez+-+Still+Life+with+Cucumbers+and+Tomatoes+1772.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5362873193437472258" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiVbesmK7Dp_UscKftR7_h8ih197abI11O500a9W7o70IYtuEUGdIv99V5iNTpb8Y_S9Cfi2DGE_zApV4HWzj_wuM4eKJIDpW_7XNHO4806_AbRbA9hyjJ6p-uI7Ql755Ds7E-vyBNoc3Fj/s320/Luis+Eugenio+Melendez+-+Still+Life+with+Cucumbers+and+Tomatoes+1772.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 201px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 320px;" /></a><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">A worker may eat a cucumber (cucumbers were expensive vegetables) or a date (which were expensive fruit) even if worth a dinar (six times his wage). The Torah tells the worker, "</span><a href="http://bible.cc/deuteronomy/23-24.htm"><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">You may eat grapes as your desire, to your satiety</span></a>,<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">" which implies that he may eat any amount needed to satisfy his hunger. </span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">Rabbi Elazar Chisma says a worker may not eat more than his wage.</span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">But the Sages permit this - however, his friends should teach him not to be a glutton, thereby closing the door to future employment.</span></div><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">Art: Still Life with Cucumbers and Tomatoes by&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">Luis Eugenio Melendez</span></div>

---

### content/bava_metzia/93.txt
<a id="src-00064"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_metzia/93.txt`

Bava Metzia 93 - Dealing in Food Entitlement (Finds)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjvsEq6wMoHiPLU4hXrilmsWNUJ_U5P_8nx-Fzwf6Ds5SvnxX-Y0S-OJdyLhUjS9YZiXq6QhMz1x3WvCGzsZKjDfWAnDdLpqA-Gl1iAbGCyaf6osoK8FKV4KkOepg1nv_DApZFt4ZDcxt20/s1600-h/Joaquin+Sorolla+y+Bastida+-+Boy+Eating+Grapes,+1890.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5363195140376773938" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjvsEq6wMoHiPLU4hXrilmsWNUJ_U5P_8nx-Fzwf6Ds5SvnxX-Y0S-OJdyLhUjS9YZiXq6QhMz1x3WvCGzsZKjDfWAnDdLpqA-Gl1iAbGCyaf6osoK8FKV4KkOepg1nv_DApZFt4ZDcxt20/s320/Joaquin+Sorolla+y+Bastida+-+Boy+Eating+Grapes,+1890.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 230px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 320px;" /></a><span style="font-size: 130%;">The produce that the worker eats while harvesting is a charitable gift from Heaven, not a fringe benefit of his work, and therefore, he can't assign it to his wife and children.<br /><br />A person may stipulate that he will not eat from harvested produce in exchange for higher wages. He may also stipulate this for his adult children and his wife since they have an understanding, but not for his minor children or his animals.<br /><br />Of <a href="https://talmudilluminated.com/bava_metzia/bava_metzia34.html" target="_blank">the four custodians</a>,  an unpaid custodian swears concerning every mishap and is not liable; the borrower pays for everything, and the paid custodian and the renter swear if an animal broke a limb, was captured, or died of natural causes.</span><div><span style="font-size: 130%;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: 130%;">Art: Boy Eating Grapes by&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: 130%;">Joaquin Sorolla y Bastida</span></div>

---

### content/bava_metzia/94.txt
<a id="src-00065"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_metzia/94.txt`

Bava Metzia 94 – Conditions in Contracts (Finds)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgYNeBCgakIN57FB5WvDjnzMb4TJz008ElI3oEuGE7HbPWju2WmTGYzUz4zvafjdihEZ8sNtVnGOZYfou30A7yUDWY4xJVMTVwZUWUiqBuLUistrv4m-lvsuIRlWvTvqJjzoSVpNnx8ucsT/s1600-h/Peder+Severin+Kroyer+-+Woman+in+White+on+a+Beach.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5363560022873241250" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgYNeBCgakIN57FB5WvDjnzMb4TJz008ElI3oEuGE7HbPWju2WmTGYzUz4zvafjdihEZ8sNtVnGOZYfou30A7yUDWY4xJVMTVwZUWUiqBuLUistrv4m-lvsuIRlWvTvqJjzoSVpNnx8ucsT/s320/Peder+Severin+Kroyer+-+Woman+in+White+on+a+Beach.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 320px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 197px;" /></a><span style="font-size: 130%;">An unpaid custodian may stipulate to be exempt from an oath, and a borrower may stipulate to be exempt from paying.<br /><br />Whoever makes a stipulation contrary to what is written in the Torah, his stipulation is void. Any stipulation after the action is void. For example, “This item is yours on condition that you walk a mile” - the item is his, and he does not have to walk. Any stipulation that is impossible to fulfill is void. For example,  “This is your Get on condition that you cross the sea on foot” - the condition is void, the Get is valid, and the woman is divorced.<br /><br />If one borrows a cow but hires the owner along with it, <a href="http://bible.cc/exodus/22-15.htm">he is not liable if the cow dies.</a></span><div><span style="font-size: 130%;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: 130%;">Art: Woman in While on a Beach by Peder Severin Kroyer</span><div><br /></div></div>

---

### content/bava_metzia/95.txt
<a id="src-00066"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_metzia/95.txt`

Bava Metzia 95 – Deriving Borrower's Law With an "A Fortiori" Argument (Finds)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiPEGbXR2ASswqF3M9djonV24yLmDTuHugUbch8CVXmesp5EkrBCO7LSuD3DgW6uftwRTpa9SobM-NkV67XErQ9BvKZCp8Q3Wo8-JQR3uyXnOhk8dEH_yAPCavvCGyR9aahjtXsqibgrQAi/s1600-h/Thomas+Sidney+Cooper+-+Coastal+Landscape+with+Figures+and+Animal.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5363984807216896802" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiPEGbXR2ASswqF3M9djonV24yLmDTuHugUbch8CVXmesp5EkrBCO7LSuD3DgW6uftwRTpa9SobM-NkV67XErQ9BvKZCp8Q3Wo8-JQR3uyXnOhk8dEH_yAPCavvCGyR9aahjtXsqibgrQAi/s320/Thomas+Sidney+Cooper+-+Coastal+Landscape+with+Figures+and+Animal.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 263px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 320px;" /></a><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">The </span><a href="http://bible.cc/exodus/22-14.htm"><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">passage of the borrower</span></a><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"> imposes liability for a broken limb and natural death – unavoidable mishaps. It is silent, however, about theft and loss, which are avoidable mishaps.</span><br />
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">We can derive it ourselves with a</span><a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/A_fortiori_argument"><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">&nbsp;fortiori argument</span></a><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">: if a paid custodian, who is exempted from liability when the animal suffers a broken limb or dies, is nonetheless liable in cases of theft and loss, is it not logical that a borrower, who is indeed liable in cases of the animal suffering a broken limb or dying, is also liable in cases of theft and loss? Surely this is so.</span></div><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">Art:&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">Coastal Landscape with Figures and Animal by&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">Thomas Sidney Cooper</span></div>

---

### content/bava_metzia/96.txt
<a id="src-00067"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_metzia/96.txt`

Bava Metzia 96 – Borrower’s Exemption from Liability (Finds)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgwEVqTAEYjX5Mw8lpYC0lUzCmcsXTdzaKBxeq4_S_1QdlIZDIxSHvfMiwGlul2FYFrtHwGuKwfqa-z7PasTDyqVHggSle_p1DObJbM-WpBSuDixb00utgwzg_j5HheumDqqGmVceyD5WIa/s1600-h/Camille+Pissarro+-+Milking+Cows.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5364458322683594642" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgwEVqTAEYjX5Mw8lpYC0lUzCmcsXTdzaKBxeq4_S_1QdlIZDIxSHvfMiwGlul2FYFrtHwGuKwfqa-z7PasTDyqVHggSle_p1DObJbM-WpBSuDixb00utgwzg_j5HheumDqqGmVceyD5WIa/s320/Camille+Pissarro+-+Milking+Cows.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 238px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 320px;" /></a><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">When a man borrows a cow, and it breaks a limb or dies, "</span><a href="http://bible.cc/exodus/22-15.htm"><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">if its owner is with him, he shall not pay</span></a><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">."  </span><br />
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">Does the owner have to be "with him" at the time of borrowing, at the time of the accident, or both? Since it says, "</span><a href="http://bible.cc/exodus/22-14.htm"><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">if its owner is not with him, he shall surely pay</span></a><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">," the owner being with him at one point is sufficient, but at which point?</span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">Is it at the time of the borrowing when the cow comes under his control or at the time of the accident when he becomes obligated? - It is the time of borrowing because then he becomes responsible for its sustenance.</span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">And "with him" means either working for him or serving him.</span></div><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">Art: Milking Cows by Camilla Pissarro</span></div>

---

### content/bava_metzia/97.txt
<a id="src-00068"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_metzia/97.txt`

Bava Metzia 97 - Mice Kill Cat (Finds)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg5KE4KcADVpBT0G4GshmSi4p7wXibsmP5zIEU831AjJ7t-kW5_hycrhRqjkOaw-gM8B3-2_z3nM01soIJFFY3l5vHGZbpU_rsKUA3jMnS5inoxrzeCdGidfZ83s9RPCk4SvxtnLeOYO0tO/s1600-h/Gottfried+Mind+or+Mindt+-+Cat+killing+mice+in+a+landscape.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5364753297749674994" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg5KE4KcADVpBT0G4GshmSi4p7wXibsmP5zIEU831AjJ7t-kW5_hycrhRqjkOaw-gM8B3-2_z3nM01soIJFFY3l5vHGZbpU_rsKUA3jMnS5inoxrzeCdGidfZ83s9RPCk4SvxtnLeOYO0tO/s320/Gottfried+Mind+or+Mindt+-+Cat+killing+mice+in+a+landscape.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 245px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 320px;" /></a><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">A man borrowed a cat from his friend to chase away mice. The mice united against the cat and killed it. Is it considered that the cat died because of its work, in which case the borrower would not be liable, or perhaps the borrower did not act according to the loan terms in stationing the cat in a place so overpopulated with mice and thus is liable?</span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">Said Rava, "Regarding a man whom women overcame and killed, there is no judgment and no judge," that is, there is no redress. The borrower was not negligent and is thus exempt.</span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">Some say that the story was that the borrowed cat ate too many mice, became overheated, and died.</span></div><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">Art:&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">Cat killing mice in a landscape by&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: large;">Gottfried Mind or Mindt</span></div>

---

### content/bava_metzia/98.txt
<a id="src-00069"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_metzia/98.txt`

Bava Metzia 98 - Cow Half-Borrowed, Half-Rented (Finds)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgYj4ERv8uJtAo1ysJTTts96UQtIWzjSxsYGSHAHbIEHXpRPxo63yRAFn5sFHqBKjhNLXMH2ngobS8kF0kQH5qU3iG0ZZTkNRBoN2K_SjCqn-L67jaDheuOwebqzPprjJ6vi6JacDzsaSTC/s1600-h/Carl+Larsson+-+The+Cowshed.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5365227687253335042" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgYj4ERv8uJtAo1ysJTTts96UQtIWzjSxsYGSHAHbIEHXpRPxo63yRAFn5sFHqBKjhNLXMH2ngobS8kF0kQH5qU3iG0ZZTkNRBoN2K_SjCqn-L67jaDheuOwebqzPprjJ6vi6JacDzsaSTC/s320/Carl+Larsson+-+The+Cowshed.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 222px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 320px;" /></a><div><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">A man borrowed a cow for half a day and rented it for the other half a day, and the cow died. The lender claims, "It died while being borrowed," asking the borrower to be liable, but the borrower says, "I do not know." In this case, the borrower is liable.</span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">Can we disprove it from Rav Nachman's ruling? If one claims to another, "You owe me a maneh (100 zuz), and the other one says, "I do not know if I owe you"" the defendant is NOT liable. But in the first ruling, he is!</span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><br /></span></div>
<div>
<span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;">Rav Nachman will answer that the first ruling is talking about two cows, and about one of them, the borrower agrees to his liability. This makes it a case of</span><span class="Apple-style-span" style="font-size: medium;"><a href="https://talmudilluminated.com/bava_metzia/bava_metzia3.html" target="_blank">&nbsp;the borrower admitting in part</a>,&nbsp;so that he has to swear, but not knowing about the second claim, he can't swear and thus has to pay.</span></div>
<div>
<br /></div><div>Art: The Cowshed by Carl Larsson</div>

---

### content/bava_metzia/99.txt
<a id="src-00070"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bava_metzia/99.txt`

Bava Metzia 99 – Responsibility in Transit (Finds)
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjZwZqnTv53F7OoljA4qiABLMSkMvKgURqMc3Jo-23Yn34xiB7cS902JCD0gJWh4i7nIdTJAHZmNMUab_Ag5EGmJlkQ9w5Wu9gZ1-MKlGrqhSDsXjD_TUwVY6cWcxksfYOTNf16eq4O-hWd/s1600-h/Rosa+Bonheur+-+Cows+Resting.jpg" onblur="try {parent.deselectBloggerImageGracefully();} catch(e) {}"><img alt="" border="0" id="BLOGGER_PHOTO_ID_5365416263818715106" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjZwZqnTv53F7OoljA4qiABLMSkMvKgURqMc3Jo-23Yn34xiB7cS902JCD0gJWh4i7nIdTJAHZmNMUab_Ag5EGmJlkQ9w5Wu9gZ1-MKlGrqhSDsXjD_TUwVY6cWcxksfYOTNf16eq4O-hWd/s320/Rosa+Bonheur+-+Cows+Resting.jpg" style="cursor: pointer; float: left; height: 225px; margin: 0pt 10px 10px 0pt; width: 320px;" /></a><span style="font-size: 130%;">If one was borrowing a cow and the lender sent it to him with his son, slave, or agent – or with the son, the slave, or the agent of the borrower – and the cow died naturally in transit, the borrower is not liable. Even the borrower's worker does not become an agent to assume responsibility for the cow but only to transport it safely.<br /><br />If, however, the borrower said to the lender, "Send me the cow with my son (my slave, my agent)" or "with your son (your slave, your agent)" and the cow died naturally in transit, the borrower is liable – not through the law of agency, but through the law of a guarantor: in consideration of the lender sending the cow on his say-so, the borrower assumes responsibility for any mishap that befalls the animal on the way.</span><div><span style="font-size: 130%;"><br /></span></div><div><span style="font-size: 130%;">Art:&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: 20.8px;">Cows Resting by&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: 130%;">Rosa Bonheur</span></div>

---

### content/bechorot/10.txt
<a id="src-00071"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bechorot/10.txt`

Bechorot 10 – If The Firstborn Donkey Is Not Redeemed...
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhIV8Dil-UM8sr3yasSjbuwGZW7yuYqgkRRbttL2GHoSfOv35f2F-P6zxS1m0yzp15J7LcBe6xX4ti9RLBl3C9Ztd7CWc5kNTqQkintpQZYBrNQUIKjVOvg973MhrVA_DjkvQqkAYg2O6M/s1600/Ebenezer+Newman+Downard+-+A+Donkey+At+A+Gate.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhIV8Dil-UM8sr3yasSjbuwGZW7yuYqgkRRbttL2GHoSfOv35f2F-P6zxS1m0yzp15J7LcBe6xX4ti9RLBl3C9Ztd7CWc5kNTqQkintpQZYBrNQUIKjVOvg973MhrVA_DjkvQqkAYg2O6M/s1600/Ebenezer+Newman+Downard+-+A+Donkey+At+A+Gate.jpg" /></a>If one does not wish to redeem his firstborn donkey, he must decapitate it with a butcher's cleaver, from the back of the neck. Rabbah said: “Even Rabbi Shimon, who permits using the firstborn donkey before redeeming it with a sheep, agrees that after decapitation it can't be used. What is the reason? Compare it to a calf that was <i>decapitated</i> to atone for an unsolved murder case; this calf was buried in the valley and not used. So too the <i>decapitated</i> donkey cannot be used.”
<br />
<br />
How does Rabbah know Rabbi Shimon's opinion? Because in the list of foods that can become impure Rabbi Shimon does not include the meat of a decapitated donkey. We must conclude that Rabbi Shimon deems it forbidden for benefit, thus, one cannot sell it even for others to eat. However, the Talmud rejects his proof: perhaps donkey meat is not food simply because people don't usually eat it? This attack is parried: the prohibition of the Torah to eat it elevates it to the status of food.
<br />
<br />
And Rabbah? “Since he caused loss to a kohen, his donkey should now be lost to him” describes the position of Rabbi Shimon.
<br />
<br />
Art: Ebenezer Newman Downard - A Donkey At A Gate

---

### content/bechorot/11.txt
<a id="src-00072"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bechorot/11.txt`

Bechorot 11 – How Much for a Firstborn Donkey?
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhyaPJELmdeVqtSKQ1RB2XwsKcaNfmB0OKCipwF0otN823qHyWID6DeruRWJnF-hzWvfVxF_uBe-axPWYY8jgs5CucNIWA1LcTNj5_mQl2jHxsy7QT-dBHeTbskGnCxnZW82afy35HP21Q/s1600/Vincent+Van+Gogh+-+Still+Life+With+Vegetables+And+Fruit.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="232" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhyaPJELmdeVqtSKQ1RB2XwsKcaNfmB0OKCipwF0otN823qHyWID6DeruRWJnF-hzWvfVxF_uBe-axPWYY8jgs5CucNIWA1LcTNj5_mQl2jHxsy7QT-dBHeTbskGnCxnZW82afy35HP21Q/s320/Vincent+Van+Gogh+-+Still+Life+With+Vegetables+And+Fruit.jpg" width="320" /></a>The preferred method of redeeming a firstborn donkey is to give the kohen a sheep. A generous person gives a sheep worth 4 zuz, stingy – 2 zuz, and average – 3 zuz, and a zuz is $50. However, even a very lean sheep worth $10 will also make the redemption.  Alternatively, one can give anything of value, even cooked vegetables, but then the amount should be equal to the worth of the donkey.<br />
<br />
If one redeems his fellow's firstborn donkey, it is valid. Does he acquire the donkey? Do we say that it is similar to consecrated property, and the redeemer acquires it, or do we say that it still belongs to the owner, since he could have redeemed it with a very cheap sheep? The answer comes from the rule about stealing a firstborn donkey. If a thief were to steal it, he would pay the owner double, the usual penalty for stealing from an individual, and not single, the penalty for stealing consecrated property. We see then that it belongs to the owner, and we can conclude that it is not like&nbsp;consecrated&nbsp;property, and that the redeemer does not acquire it.<br />
<br />
Art:&nbsp;Vincent Van Gogh - Still Life With Vegetables And Fruit

---

### content/bechorot/12.txt
<a id="src-00073"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bechorot/12.txt`

Bechorot 12 – What is Not Good for Redeeming a Firstborn Donkey
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;">
</div>
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEi7nXJmTC2w9Bz7CVWycj1jtWF3XuA_5BeMMh5qL5Hv8Yr_FimjCteYpO4Vhpu-pnNQKoaDL0X26hfV9rQOLFGhe9U0PGAvZFS98ds5LtnU6R_RkLx2Spu9FNCOqmjrn6izzO3QxVCVJOI/s1600/William+Snr+Luker+-+Deer+In+The+New+Forest.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEi7nXJmTC2w9Bz7CVWycj1jtWF3XuA_5BeMMh5qL5Hv8Yr_FimjCteYpO4Vhpu-pnNQKoaDL0X26hfV9rQOLFGhe9U0PGAvZFS98ds5LtnU6R_RkLx2Spu9FNCOqmjrn6izzO3QxVCVJOI/s320/William+Snr+Luker+-+Deer+In+The+New+Forest.jpg" width="258" /></a>One cannot use the following to redeem a firstborn donkey: a calf, a wild animal, a slaughtered animal - even a slaughtered sheep, a sick animal  - <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2011/07/terefah-and-nevelah-two-categories-of.html">terefah</a>, a hybrid - even an offspring of a male goat and a female sheep, or a <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2011/09/chullin-80-product-of-deer-and-goat.html">koy</a> - an offspring of a deer and a goat. Rabbi Eliezer allows redemption with a hybrid, because both a goat and a sheep separately can be used.<br />
<br />
Can we redeem a firstborn donkey with a live fetus found in a womb of a slaughtered sheep? Is it a live sheep, good for a redemption, or, since it does not require proper slaughter, it is considered as meat already slaughtered, not valid for redemption? Can one use a mutant – an animal that is similar to a different species? Is it close enough to hybrid, which is forbidden?  Can one use a disqualified sacrifice? Since the sanctity of a donkey cannot possibly go over to the sacrifice, the redemption is not possible, or does this sanctity just fly away? Can one use the produce of the seventh (Shemittah) year for redemption? Is it closer to prohibited commerce or to permitted food?<br />
<br />
Art:&nbsp;William Snr Luker - Deer In The New Forest

---

### content/bechorot/13.txt
<a id="src-00074"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bechorot/13.txt`

Bechorot 13 – Firstborn of a Kosher Animal
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;">
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiitrmKsQyrKjqU3gz4zbSYBbSSypJgTFh8rflGqY3dHV0iUwlsDrCeyvjjebQIlMqWIaRhDBB5cD9Q4lNEa96JSs-TsGEHIgrLGk443p1B6K27LLnPOUKwsLtPT0pjWcWacmmtVExygQE/s1600/Willem+Romeijn+-+Cow%252C+Goats+and+Sheep+in+a+Meadow.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="229" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiitrmKsQyrKjqU3gz4zbSYBbSSypJgTFh8rflGqY3dHV0iUwlsDrCeyvjjebQIlMqWIaRhDBB5cD9Q4lNEa96JSs-TsGEHIgrLGk443p1B6K27LLnPOUKwsLtPT0pjWcWacmmtVExygQE/s320/Willem+Romeijn+-+Cow%252C+Goats+and+Sheep+in+a+Meadow.jpg" width="320" /></a></div>
If one designated a sheep for the redemption of a firstborn donkey, and the sheep died, the owner is responsible to replace it with another lamb, just as a father of a firstborn boy is responsible to replace the redemption money, should be it lost before it reaches the kohen – this is the opinion of Rabbi Eliezer. However, the Sages say that the owner is not responsible for the replacement lamb, just as he is not responsible for the second tithe, which, if lost, need not be replaced.
<br />
<br />
If one buys the fetus of an idolaters cow or sells him his own cow's fetus – although he is not allowed to do so, or buys the cow jointly with an idolater – the cow is exempt from the law of firstborn, because the Torah said “<a href="http://bible.ort.org/books/pentd2.asp?ACTION=displaypage&amp;BOOK=4&amp;CHAPTER=3#P3703">all firstborn in Israel</a>” – but not in other nations. 
<br />
<br />
By contrast, the kohanim and Levites are included in the obligation of the firstborn of kosher animals. They were only excluded from the redemption of their sons and donkeys. Thus, a kohen who owns a cow, sheep or goat that gives birth to a male as it first offspring brings it as an offering.
<br />
<br />
Art:&nbsp;Willem Romeijn - Cow, Goats and Sheep in a Meadow<br />
<br />

---

### content/bechorot/14.txt
<a id="src-00075"></a>

**Source file:** `content/bechorot/14.txt`

Bechorot 14 – Consecrating Animals with a Blemish
