Chullin 22 – Which Birds Are Fit For Sacrifices
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiPxW38uzIarsA_Okz-p0B4Q5E5LAQFw5fm1pogcO8zu_FTEoN640TIqX_aqwWiJR4ufPqXU2FjYEVGBp3KbJZWaNsn_FWR9dSP_zleF7_HP5jNjTQsJQ_-bXUXzUkF-sNjXwjeqPoX478/s1600/James+E.+Bourhill+-+Pouter+Pigeons.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="228" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiPxW38uzIarsA_Okz-p0B4Q5E5LAQFw5fm1pogcO8zu_FTEoN640TIqX_aqwWiJR4ufPqXU2FjYEVGBp3KbJZWaNsn_FWR9dSP_zleF7_HP5jNjTQsJQ_-bXUXzUkF-sNjXwjeqPoX478/s320/James+E.+Bourhill+-+Pouter+Pigeons.jpg" width="320" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">The only two species of birds mentioned in the Torah which can be offered as sacrifices are the turtledove and the pigeon. Turtledoves are migratory birds, but pigeons dwell permanently in the land. A turtledove must be mature to be fit for  a sacrifice, but a pigeon is acceptable only before it reaches maturity. We therefore have the following rules.<br />
<br />
What is acceptable in the case of turtledoves is unacceptable in the case of pigeons, and vice versa. The beginning of yellowing in both types is unacceptable. That is when a turtledove is not fully mature yet, and a pigeon begins to become mature. The reason for this is that the Torah calls pigeons “bnei yonah,” “sons of pigeons”; conversely, we understand that turtledoves must be mature.<br />
<br />
But logic should dictate otherwise: if turtledoves, which are not acceptable when young, are acceptable when mature, then pigeons, which are acceptable when young, should surely be acceptable when old! To dispel this, the Torah never called a pigeon a pigeon, but only a “son of a pigeon” to emphasize that only young ones are acceptable.<br />
<br />
Art: James E. Bourhill - Pouter Pigeons</span>

---

### content/chullin/23.txt
<a id="src-00316"></a>

**Source file:** `content/chullin/23.txt`

Chullin 23 – Intermediate Stages of Birds, Lambs, and Dough
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEj9xC09gFGx37pluTkFGxMHjo505lNdF4OZ07XDDnjdXcAT5_g1angOJ6t33x0JNJLSGemqiFZdRwoKXHP0l0LaAJ9EV_rphrep5hEaArR4LiMeUKuZF9TamEQSI2c55jPbKjjgT1ZKFd4/s1600/Antonio+Paoletti+-+Feeding+The+Pigeons+At+Piazza+St.+Marco%252C+Venice.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEj9xC09gFGx37pluTkFGxMHjo505lNdF4OZ07XDDnjdXcAT5_g1angOJ6t33x0JNJLSGemqiFZdRwoKXHP0l0LaAJ9EV_rphrep5hEaArR4LiMeUKuZF9TamEQSI2c55jPbKjjgT1ZKFd4/s320/Antonio+Paoletti+-+Feeding+The+Pigeons+At+Piazza+St.+Marco%252C+Venice.jpg" width="190" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">If the feathers of a turtledove or a pigeon started yellowing, the turtledove can't be sacrificed because it is too young, and the pigeon – because it is too old. Rabbi Zeira asked, “Is this for sure or out of doubt?” Meaning, if one promised a bird burnt offering and then brought a turtledove and a pigeon with yellowing feathers, is at least one of them valid, or, because it is a bird in a class by itself, neither is valid?<br />
<br />
Try this answer: the Torah said “sacrifices … from birds,” and this means that some birds are excluded. Which ones? Isn't it ones with yellowing feathers? - No! Excluded are <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2011/02/zevachim-85-these-must-be-removed-from.html">birds that were sodomized</a> or worshiped, and Rabbi Zeira does not get an answer.<br />
<br />
He asked a similar question about sheep. A sheep younger than twelve months is a lamb, one older than thirteen is a ram, what is its status in between? Does it require libations like either a lamb or  a ram, or is it a separate creature with no libations? Again, no answer. He also asked about dough in intermediate stages of leavening, can it be brought as part of a thanksgiving offering.<br />
<br />
Art: Antonio Paoletti - Feeding The Pigeons At Piazza St. Marco, Venice<br />
</span>

---

### content/chullin/24.txt
<a id="src-00317"></a>

**Source file:** `content/chullin/24.txt`

Chullin 24 – Five Years for Success in Study
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiiC1c0Uukrd14F0kyDugs9mjhyphenhyphenAFGlZywOjev3G3jXKFfYXxy8OEFTv-gP5MthdIzGilHGLBGeTxb0RZpFgE-Mg8dnEv6PdyPDT36B2NcAM5GvYu-PWua-8lAA_8oJqOuhl-GinN5AFt0/s1600/Emil+Jacobs+-+Young+Student.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiiC1c0Uukrd14F0kyDugs9mjhyphenhyphenAFGlZywOjev3G3jXKFfYXxy8OEFTv-gP5MthdIzGilHGLBGeTxb0RZpFgE-Mg8dnEv6PdyPDT36B2NcAM5GvYu-PWua-8lAA_8oJqOuhl-GinN5AFt0/s320/Emil+Jacobs+-+Young+Student.jpg" width="279" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">A red heifer was slaughtered by shechitah from the front of the neck, and its ashes were used to remove ritual impurity. The decapitated calf was a needed when a dead body was found in the Land of Israel: the Sages of the nearby town would kill the calf by breaking its neck from the back. Therefore we have a rule: “What is valid for the red heifer is invalid for the decapitated calf, and vice versa.”<br />
<br />
What is fit for the kohanim is unfit for the Leviim, and vice versa. The kohanim were disqualified by blemishes, but they could serve at any age. In contrast, the Leviim were not disqualified by blemishes, but they had age limitations: they would start studies at 25 and continue on to service at 30. They  retired at 50.<br />
<br />
The service of the Leviim included guarding the gates, singing in the Temple choir and playing in the Temple orchestra. From them we have a rule that any student who does not see success in the first five years of his studies will never see it. Some say that at this point he should try Kabbalah.<br />
<br />
Art: Emil Jacobs - Young Student<br />
</span>

---

### content/chullin/25.txt
<a id="src-00318"></a>

**Source file:** `content/chullin/25.txt`

Chullin 25 – What is Fit for One is Unfit for Another
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiO35ag89Fxf1QcO27ZAMkklgWpqvGg7mhTBVjZLrhfysIWwvJT8R2dkXaBeP6HOeBdEvG1CNQN-Tcs5V7e7kBRuC6ohOoywc9XreJyQfqTOZ8LdWVjMenuYzfsmsHddLuSiQDWLvcYST0/s1600/Edgar+Degas+-+Still+Life+With+Lizard.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiO35ag89Fxf1QcO27ZAMkklgWpqvGg7mhTBVjZLrhfysIWwvJT8R2dkXaBeP6HOeBdEvG1CNQN-Tcs5V7e7kBRuC6ohOoywc9XreJyQfqTOZ8LdWVjMenuYzfsmsHddLuSiQDWLvcYST0/s320/Edgar+Degas+-+Still+Life+With+Lizard.jpg" width="250" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">What is pure in the case of earthenware utensils is impure in the case of all other utensils, and vice versa. If a dead lizard is inside a clay pot, even not touching it, the pot is impure, but if it touches the outside, the pot remains pure. The opposite is true of other utensils.<br />
<br />
How do we know this highly unusual law of earthenware utensils? The Torah said, “<a href="http://bible.ort.org/books/pentd2.asp?ACTION=displaypage&amp;BOOK=3&amp;CHAPTER=11">an earthenware utensil into whose interior one of the eight dead reptiles will fall … will become impure</a>” - even if the reptile does not touch it. It also said,“<a href="http://bible.ort.org/books/pentd2.asp?ACTION=displaypage&amp;BOOK=4&amp;CHAPTER=19">any open utensil under the same roof with a dead body, if it does not have a cover, will become impure</a>”, to teach that if it does have a cover, it remains pure and protects from impurity – even if it is touched from the outside.<br />
<br />
What is pure in the case of wooden utensils is impure in the case of metal utensils, and vice versa. Wooden utensils can be used before they are fully finished, and are thus susceptible to impurity. However, if they lack a hollow of any kind, they remain pure. The reverse is true of metal utensils.<br />
<br />
Art: Edgar Degas - Still Life With Lizard</span>

---

### content/chullin/26.txt
<a id="src-00319"></a>

**Source file:** `content/chullin/26.txt`

Chullin 26 – Different Stages of Development
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEh6TTnzy6vFReYunelSYRkUMHWEUFzAmrPPkdRCHVRRDcpBGZexlL5GJSRFuK1Q1WC_aIv7Arr1PGlIrz25j6jKeURPvUmhjHxOreEYVXGdc9w-g_ihEjwP5M52MnJUgv843Z0IxeuXTPQ/s1600/Artemisia+Gentileschi+-+Judith+and+Her+Maidservant.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEh6TTnzy6vFReYunelSYRkUMHWEUFzAmrPPkdRCHVRRDcpBGZexlL5GJSRFuK1Q1WC_aIv7Arr1PGlIrz25j6jKeURPvUmhjHxOreEYVXGdc9w-g_ihEjwP5M52MnJUgv843Z0IxeuXTPQ/s320/Artemisia+Gentileschi+-+Judith+and+Her+Maidservant.jpg" width="262" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Two strands of almonds were cultivated in Israel: one, the “bitter almond,” whose fruit became bitter as it grew larger; and the other, the “sweet almond,” whose fruit became sweeter as it grew larger. What is subject to tithing in the case of bitter almonds (when they are small and sweet) is exempt in the case of sweet almonds (when they are still bitter), and vice versa. <br />
<br />
Soaked grape-seeds – before they ferment are like water and cannot be bought with second tithe money, after they ferment, they are food (wine) and can be bought with with second tithe money. The brothers whose father died – before they divide the estate they have the law of a single person (father) and have to separate animal tithe; after they divided it, even if they continue together, are like partners and do not have to separate animal tithe.<br />
<br />
A girl who is a minor – her father can sell her as a maidservant, but there is no fine for seduction; once she grows up, her father can't sell her, and there is a penalty for rape or seduction. The Sages disagree and say that there is always a penalty.<br />
<br />
Art: Artemisia Gentileschi - Judith and Her Maidservant<br />
</span>

---

### content/chullin/27.txt
<a id="src-00320"></a>

**Source file:** `content/chullin/27.txt`

Chullin 27 – Must Shechitah Be Done From The Neck?
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEj4f6NxwxFWGzAnQu8DiYAu8VfpwK5teMAZLK2F6pMDaqX98tDLRE8aHnpIQBNtey55YV_nHwsBzSZTSH7P-7rp_by7lr36Do4HoadUF-ptuLHMluj7LKXG3eZhgeL2SEBKMcBxWzrCzYs/s1600/Thomas+Wade+-+Man+Tickling+a+Woman%2527s+Nose+with+a+Feather.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEj4f6NxwxFWGzAnQu8DiYAu8VfpwK5teMAZLK2F6pMDaqX98tDLRE8aHnpIQBNtey55YV_nHwsBzSZTSH7P-7rp_by7lr36Do4HoadUF-ptuLHMluj7LKXG3eZhgeL2SEBKMcBxWzrCzYs/s320/Thomas+Wade+-+Man+Tickling+a+Woman%2527s+Nose+with+a+Feather.jpg" width="244" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Shechitah is done from the neck: one cuts more than half of the windpipe and the food pipe for an animal, and one pipe is enough for a bird.<br />
<br />
Why from the neck? Said Rav Kahana, the word “shechitah” says it: “shach” means something that bends, that is the neck, and “chat” means to prepare. But the tail also bends, so perhaps we should cut from the tail? - No, the tail is already bent, and we need something that bends occasionally. But perhaps we should cut from the ear, because it sometimes bends? - No, we need the lifeblood, and it does not go from the ear. Still, how would we know the five disqualifications of the shechitah, which are pausing, pressing, burrowing, cutting beyond and tearing? - We are forced to conclude that cutting from the neck was taught to Moses on Sinai and is not based on a word in the Torah.<br />
<br />
Rav Yeimar said, the word slaughter, “zavach” means to cut where it (the blood) flows (“zav”). But perhaps we should cut from the nose, from which mucus flows? - No, mucus always flows, and blood – only when cut. <br />
<br />
Art: Thomas Wade - Man Tickling a Woman's Nose with a Feather<br />
</span>

---

### content/chullin/28.txt
<a id="src-00321"></a>

**Source file:** `content/chullin/28.txt`

Chullin 28 – Is Shechitah Required for Birds?
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhQqMZQMSZHYe_X4YQAX9vtsE1OxTAssBYqdKaNM9Knbk0BWpvcTDRRqdadRXe51e-LJV0goWswNUqtijjNbJkkScHUU5cqlw00NHyJ7kJBQ01FmkjRd1HkqlUh6OXxpo8eA8wFNG7C5Gs/s1600/Jan+Fyt+-+A+cat+stalking+dead+songbirds+on+a+ledge.Jpeg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="231" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhQqMZQMSZHYe_X4YQAX9vtsE1OxTAssBYqdKaNM9Knbk0BWpvcTDRRqdadRXe51e-LJV0goWswNUqtijjNbJkkScHUU5cqlw00NHyJ7kJBQ01FmkjRd1HkqlUh6OXxpo8eA8wFNG7C5Gs/s320/Jan+Fyt+-+A+cat+stalking+dead+songbirds+on+a+ledge.Jpeg" width="320" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Rav Yehudah said in the name of Rabbi Yitzchak ben Pinchas, “There is no requirement for kosher slaughter of birds in the Torah.” Rather, it was instituted by the Sages. Granted, if the bird dies by itself or from a blow to a part of its body, it does become a <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2011/07/terefah-and-nevelah-two-categories-of.html">nevelah</a> and may not be eaten. However, one can kill the bird by tearing or piercing its pipes, and that would be sufficient. The hint to this in the Torah is found in the requirement to <a href="http://bible.ort.org/books/pentd2.asp?ACTION=displaypage&amp;BOOK=3&amp;CHAPTER=17">cover the blood of a killed bird</a>, – meaning, covering the blood is all that is required. <br />
<br />
Objection to the statement of Rabbi Yitzchak! We learned a rule that “If one was doing the shechitah, and inadvertently rendered it a <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2011/07/terefah-and-nevelah-two-categories-of.html">nevelah</a>, or if he pierces or tears the creature's pipes, he does not have to cover the blood. We see from here that piercing is not considered shechitah, to the extent that even blood covering is not required! What will Rabbi Yitzchak answer? He says that this rule is only about a wild animal - <a href="http://bible.ort.org/books/pentd2.asp?ACTION=displaypage&amp;BOOK=3&amp;CHAPTER=17">since covering the blood is also required for a wild animal</a> - and not about a bird.<br />
<br />
Art: Jan Fyt - A cat stalking dead songbirds on a ledge<br />
</span>

---

### content/chullin/29.txt
<a id="src-00322"></a>

**Source file:** `content/chullin/29.txt`

Chullin 29 – Can One Divide Exactly In Two Halves?
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhMxOzM3V78uDcOEKam3uIWLp6R4d1CQTvligjhUIeAKMp2bwtbqrARbCrxBHGDODY2txZoC69HtjO9F_6D5JLctcj2HSIWMlN6sQAFiz-LLQ5xXtyCq9tP5rrxZv8PsiSmQYgQJ4VPxvA/s1600/Pieter+Harmansz+Verelst+-+A+young+boy+reclining%252C+eating+from+an+earthenware+bowl.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="258" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhMxOzM3V78uDcOEKam3uIWLp6R4d1CQTvligjhUIeAKMp2bwtbqrARbCrxBHGDODY2txZoC69HtjO9F_6D5JLctcj2HSIWMlN6sQAFiz-LLQ5xXtyCq9tP5rrxZv8PsiSmQYgQJ4VPxvA/s320/Pieter+Harmansz+Verelst+-+A+young+boy+reclining%252C+eating+from+an+earthenware+bowl.jpg" width="320" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">If in doing the shechitah one cuts exactly half of the pipe's circumference, Rav says that it is valid, because God told Moses not to leave over more than half uncut, and Rav Kahana says that it is invalid, because God told Moses to but the greater part when slaughtering.<br />
<br />
An objection against Rav comes from the laws of purity. If one split a ritually impure earthenware oven into two pieces, ostensibly of the same size – they both remain impure, because it is impossible to be precise in anything, and any of the two pieces might be the larger one. However, if it were possible to be precise, the pieces would be pure! But, according to Rav, exactly half is considered like more than half, and thus the pieces should remain impure, which proves that Rav is wrong! Said Rav Pappa in Rav's defense, in an oven both pieces cannot be the larger ones, but in slaughter we care only about the part that is cut.<br />
<br />
In the end the Rav's point of view is revised as untenable, and instead we say that the argument is not about shechitah, but about half of all Jews being impure on Passover.<br />
<br />
Art: Pieter Harmansz Verelst - A young boy reclining, eating from an earthenware bowl</span>

---

### content/chullin/3.txt
<a id="src-00323"></a>

**Source file:** `content/chullin/3.txt`

Chullin 3 – Slaughter Done by a Non-observant Jew
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEi781kpqAZIOmINus2HZLPPTEugzHuIY-2_VIV48m0BPn3k2r-szb4bmqmvmOVmIwHh-D-6-P1ERIseUch8jtRhZWre8hhKYWS6JvbeQwuUaIb42zFhmBfRNCbdiMBKhOz91TTl1ilba1A/s1600/James+Charles+-+The+Knifegrinder.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEi781kpqAZIOmINus2HZLPPTEugzHuIY-2_VIV48m0BPn3k2r-szb4bmqmvmOVmIwHh-D-6-P1ERIseUch8jtRhZWre8hhKYWS6JvbeQwuUaIb42zFhmBfRNCbdiMBKhOz91TTl1ilba1A/s320/James+Charles+-+The+Knifegrinder.jpg" width="250" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">“<a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2011/06/chulin-2-shechitah-or-ritual-slaughter.html">All may slaughter and their slaughter is valid</a>” was explained by Rav Ashi as referring to a non-observant Jew. If he eats non-kosher meat to satisfy his appetite or to save money, but will eat kosher meat when it is available, then if he is handed a sharpened knife that was properly examined and found free of nicks, he will presumably not squander the opportunity to make the meat kosher. However, if he does not have an examined knife, then he cannot be trusted, for he will not bother to sharpen it. If he went ahead and slaughtered with his knife – which he should not have done – one can examine the knife afterwards, and if the knife was found to be fine, one can eat from his shechitah.<br />
<br />
Ravina said that “all” refers to those who take upon themselves to do shechitah, because most of them know the laws – provided that they already did shechitah a few times without fainting. Even if it is their first time and they do shechitah without supervision – which they should not have done – if they later say that they did not faint, their slaughter is valid.<br />
<br />
Art: James Charles - The Knifegrinder</span>

---

### content/chullin/30.txt

**Source file:** `content/chullin/30.txt`

Chullin 30 – The Process or the Result of Shechitah?
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiCAmL2ByVWeWw2ObZ0igi9Tczvnx_C-hpOt16xn5HQwOTKErE2-Miq2YVEQ5RINzA51_oYdDYoWt4kQppVzX7zp-culJ-LkyIfr10DQuLgdj7xM1VvG-_eWmd6vLp0SkdKXtk3zB7Q3ms/s1600/Caspar+David+Friedrich+-+Two+men+at+moonrise+by+the+sea" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="213" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiCAmL2ByVWeWw2ObZ0igi9Tczvnx_C-hpOt16xn5HQwOTKErE2-Miq2YVEQ5RINzA51_oYdDYoWt4kQppVzX7zp-culJ-LkyIfr10DQuLgdj7xM1VvG-_eWmd6vLp0SkdKXtk3zB7Q3ms/s320/Caspar+David+Friedrich+-+Two+men+at+moonrise+by+the+sea" width="320" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Resh Lakish said in the name of Levi the Elder, "The act of shechitah counts at the end," but Rabbi Yochanan said that the complete process of the cut, from the beginning untill end end, is called shechitah. For example, if someone started the shechitah while outside the Temple and completed it inside, then according to Rabbi Yochanan he is liable for bringing sacrifices outside the Temple, since from the beginning of the cut he was already doing the shechitah. According to Resh Lakish, he is not liable, since only the end of shechitah is significant, and that happened inside.<br />
<br />
Rav Yehudah said in the name of Rav, “If one severs the pipe in two or three places, his slaughter is valid.” But when he repeated this teaching in front of Shmuel, Shmuel said it was invalid. A defense for Rav: as we will learn later, two people can hold a knife and together make a shechitah to an animal. This proves that you can make two cuts! Answers Shmuel, “No! They are holding the same knife together and cutting. We need a clearly visible single cut.” <br />
<br />
Art: Caspar David Friedrich - Two men at moonrise by the sea<br />
</span>

---

### content/chullin/31.txt
<a id="src-00325"></a>

**Source file:** `content/chullin/31.txt`

Chullin 31 – Shechitah Must Be Done With A Sawing Motion
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhd436afFfw_ehXshydYWgae9OVbIDC-LC03hPVZl49E8QL4qQTUL_j0loEeVLHLIf8uECl1o8PSYGeVDqKWb0w8ZSiljzcu5X0cDixHJFHcxHJnkJJFOO15DlgrIzZ6B9Z5MsxRUxkrHM/s1600/Hans+Memling+-+Portrait+of+a+Man+with+an+Arrow.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhd436afFfw_ehXshydYWgae9OVbIDC-LC03hPVZl49E8QL4qQTUL_j0loEeVLHLIf8uECl1o8PSYGeVDqKWb0w8ZSiljzcu5X0cDixHJFHcxHJnkJJFOO15DlgrIzZ6B9Z5MsxRUxkrHM/s320/Hans+Memling+-+Portrait+of+a+Man+with+an+Arrow.jpg" width="258" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">If one chopped off the head of an animal, the shechitah is invalid because it must be done with a drawn-out, saw-like motion. Therefore, if he cut the head off with one motion, it is valid – provided that the knife was twice as long as the neck, so that he can accomplish the cut without going back and forth. If he used the back-and-forth motion, it is valid, and then the knife can be as small as a scalpel. If he cut off two animal heads in one motion, it is valid, provided that the knife is thrice as long as one neck. Two people can do a shechitah together, as long as they don't press.<br />
<br />
Rava examined an arrow for Rav Yonah, found it smooth, and then Rav Yonah slaughtered with it a bird in flight. But perhaps the arrow entered the side of the neck and burrowed between the pipes? - They saw that the feathers around the neck were sliced. But they need to cover the blood of the bird both below and above? - They plowed the whole field over which the bird was flying, and thus the loose earth served for covering below.<br />
<br />
Art: Hans Memling - Portrait of a Man with an Arrow</span>

---

### content/chullin/32.txt
<a id="src-00326"></a>

**Source file:** `content/chullin/32.txt`

Chullin 32 – Pause During Shechitah
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiVviUUt9vRnt-_NVaUVZMlmofYs5elTYS2ZrfHnfodT4IAJK9zfQJGEEuQI6Jl_reV4jgLCFEpKOEZALUOe4t8qxZXIFjKmKUtIFE6U79_G4Aknq7FMdKEDJJKtICtefgPDm-HGKJ-XAA/s1600/Gerard+Terborch+-+Woman+Washing+Hands.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiVviUUt9vRnt-_NVaUVZMlmofYs5elTYS2ZrfHnfodT4IAJK9zfQJGEEuQI6Jl_reV4jgLCFEpKOEZALUOe4t8qxZXIFjKmKUtIFE6U79_G4Aknq7FMdKEDJJKtICtefgPDm-HGKJ-XAA/s320/Gerard+Terborch+-+Woman+Washing+Hands.jpg" width="262" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">If while one was doing the shechitah the knife fell from his hand, and then he picked it up and completed the shechitah, it is valid – if the pause was no longer than what it takes to make a shechitah. The same applies to a case where he had to sharpen the knife, or where he grew weak while doing the shechitah, and his companion finished it for him. Rabbi Shimon says, the pause should not be longer than what it takes to examine the knife.<br />
<br />
If in doing the shechitah one properly severed the trachea, but tore the esophagus with a nicked knife, then Rabbi Yesheivav says that the animal becomes a nevelah – not slaughtered at all – and therefore carries ritual impurity. Rabbi Akiva says that the animal becomes a trefah: it is slaughtered, but considered to have an internal defect that would cause it to die within a year. Trefah cannot be eaten, but it does not carry ritual impurity.<br />
<br />
Rabbi Yesheivav stated a rule: any animal that became unfit through slaughter becomes a nevelah, but if another incidental defect caused it to become unfit, it becomes trefah, and subsequently Rabbi Akiva agreed to it.<br />
<br />
Art: Gerard Terborch - Woman Washing Hands</span>

---

### content/chullin/33.txt
<a id="src-00327"></a>

**Source file:** `content/chullin/33.txt`

Chullin 33 – Blood of Shechitah and Ritual Impurity
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhJg0WKNdc80E95R8neVqoJw8Hu2nrICoJUouURStnWdAQpKehsqehGd2R_FTG-I96wljUnN16jc6GDfRgkYzLLndFPmEu9irHK78UNwqvr4SGB4HSI-or7n_BX8q5VP4bvmqX0KKlyn78/s1600/Jean-Baptiste+Oudry+-+A+Deer+Chased+by+Dogs.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhJg0WKNdc80E95R8neVqoJw8Hu2nrICoJUouURStnWdAQpKehsqehGd2R_FTG-I96wljUnN16jc6GDfRgkYzLLndFPmEu9irHK78UNwqvr4SGB4HSI-or7n_BX8q5VP4bvmqX0KKlyn78/s320/Jean-Baptiste+Oudry+-+A+Deer+Chased+by+Dogs.jpg" width="291" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">To become susceptible to ritual impurity, food must first become wet, as the Torah said, “<a href="http://bible.ort.org/books/pentd2.asp?ACTION=displaypage&amp;BOOK=3&amp;CHAPTER=11">any usual food that has [once] been wet with water shall become unclean</a>”. In addition, the owner of the food must be content with it becoming wet. Thus, washing the fruit would qualify, while the fruit falling into the water would not.<br />
<br />
The slaughter of an animal produces blood, and the owner of the animal is content with it, thus blood prepared the animal to become ritually impure. However, we have a rule that states “if one slaughtered a domesticated animal, a wild kosher animal, or a bird,  and blood did not come out of them, they are kosher. We do not assume that the animal died just prior to shechitah. It may be eaten with unwashed hands.”<br />
<br />
Unwashed hands are considered ritually impure. But why should this rule be true? It cannot be talking about sacrifices, because kosher wild animals, such as deer, are never brought as sacrifices. The only situation where this rule can be applicable is when animals were bought with the money of the second tithe.<br />
<br />
Art: Jean-Baptiste Oudry - A Deer Chased by Dogs</span>

---

### content/chullin/34.txt
<a id="src-00328"></a>

**Source file:** `content/chullin/34.txt`

Chullin 34 – People Who Eat The Food as of it Were a Sacrifice
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjGfE-jaNkLovMkI13fivtaGgNXQyndh1szihL4ZWcqVYX0PtwHCZUMZ5yqH8pi1ldIVcGPQw9GXGjSmxNkOiIUqJ5gfNrBd9WC913Gxu2SE0ORnUdwYcsd7uK7HTNH4-0FtdAYSAozUn4/s1600/Evert+Pieters+-+Preparing+The+Meal.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjGfE-jaNkLovMkI13fivtaGgNXQyndh1szihL4ZWcqVYX0PtwHCZUMZ5yqH8pi1ldIVcGPQw9GXGjSmxNkOiIUqJ5gfNrBd9WC913Gxu2SE0ORnUdwYcsd7uK7HTNH4-0FtdAYSAozUn4/s320/Evert+Pieters+-+Preparing+The+Meal.jpg" width="274" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Previously we <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2011/07/chullin-33-blood-of-shechitah-and.html">quoted the rule</a> that “if one slaughtered a domesticated animal, a wild kosher animal, or a bird, and blood did not come out of them, ... their meat may be eaten with unwashed hands.” We also said that this rule cannot be talking about sacrifices, because wild animals were never brought as sacrifices in the Temple. Rather it was talking about the meat bought with the money of the second tithe.<br />
<br />
However, there is a problem with this understanding. While it is true that one cannot eat the food of the second tithe while being impure, the mention of the hands implies that one cannot even touch the food – and that nobody ever said. Therefore, we must re-interpret the rule as talking about sacrifices after all. What about the argument that wild animals were never brought as sacrifices? That is true, and we have to further modify our understanding as talking about people who undertook to eat regular food with all the stringencies applicable to sacrificial meat. Such a diet could include venison. Game meat can be confused with regular meat, so game meat was also treated stringently.<br />
<br />
Art: Evert Pieters - Preparing The Meal</span>

---

### content/chullin/35.txt
<a id="src-00329"></a>

**Source file:** `content/chullin/35.txt`

Chullin 35 – Levels Of Purity, One Above the Other
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgOub7hS6cnHT89UWUH9KG0mkM9chSrd7DNFPmlWIcFQp2yOXKF7guMjKdDR6717MhYrICC8KsC7FX6YR2zvuIuo_pfoEVUkL4bn99qUSkITjhTohpYp-Q2mH6YzxQdJ8_g_j0m2qK7LwU/s1600/Christoffel+Lubieniecki+-+Food+Lovers.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgOub7hS6cnHT89UWUH9KG0mkM9chSrd7DNFPmlWIcFQp2yOXKF7guMjKdDR6717MhYrICC8KsC7FX6YR2zvuIuo_pfoEVUkL4bn99qUSkITjhTohpYp-Q2mH6YzxQdJ8_g_j0m2qK7LwU/s320/Christoffel+Lubieniecki+-+Food+Lovers.jpg" width="266" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">If someone decides to keep himself on a certain level of ritual purity and to guard against contamination, he is still considered definitely impure for the next level. This is because in his mind he decided only on the given level, and a conscious effort is required for the next one. Thus, the clothing of an ignorant person is considered impure for those who conduct themselves in accordance to the laws of ritual purity, but their clothing in turn is considered impure for those to eat the kohen's portion. Those who eat the kohen's portion (priests and their family) are considered impure for those who eat sacrifices.<br />
<br />
<a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2011/07/chullin-33-blood-of-shechitah-and.html"> Earlier we said</a> that if no blood flowed during the shechitah, the meat does not become susceptible to ritual impurity. Rabbi Shimon disagrees and says that the shechitah alone prepares the meat to become impure. According to him, the reason that wetting the food makes it susceptible to impurity is because this is the final step in food preparation. But the final step in meat preparation is the shechitah itself. The shechitah then takes the place of wetting the food, and thus makes the meat susceptible to impurity.<br />
<br />
Art: Christoffel Lubieniecki - Food Lovers</span>

---

### content/chullin/36.txt
<a id="src-00330"></a>

**Source file:** `content/chullin/36.txt`

Chullin 36 – Does the Blood of Shechitah Make Food Susceptible to Impurity?
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEix5Sfhpo9do84Cxu-aPCs4QDuuhJqSKUcY7h_zLXpsPDrgeUtdESDG6Dwz0USV-23c-ea-L0k60v0ul2PH0E2DAkGmyLJVfZbO_1OhNRtENYGt1JvYJZ6napILJSEP3seSaMGLF8PZGvs/s1600/Jan+Lievens+-+Jacob+Receiving+the+Blooded+Tunic+of+Joseph.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="238" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEix5Sfhpo9do84Cxu-aPCs4QDuuhJqSKUcY7h_zLXpsPDrgeUtdESDG6Dwz0USV-23c-ea-L0k60v0ul2PH0E2DAkGmyLJVfZbO_1OhNRtENYGt1JvYJZ6napILJSEP3seSaMGLF8PZGvs/s320/Jan+Lievens+-+Jacob+Receiving+the+Blooded+Tunic+of+Joseph.jpg" width="320" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">To become susceptible to ritual impurity, food must come into contact with a liquid. The verse “<a href="http://bible.ort.org/books/pentd2.asp?ACTION=displaypage&amp;BOOK=4&amp;CHAPTER=23">and drinks the blood of its kill</a>” indicates that blood is considered a “beverage,” which can prepare food to become impure, but which kind of blood? Let's analyze the following rule. If one slaughtered an animal and the blood spattered on a nearby gourd, then Rabbi Yehudah the Prince says that the gourd can become impure, but his nephew Rabbi Chiya says that its state is in doubt.<br />
<br />
When blood is let from an animal, it drips slowly at first, until, after a few drops, it begins to spurt. The initial spurt is bright, but as the blood continues to flow, it slows and darkens in color. Only this is called the “blood of its kill,” when the animal dies. Rabbi Yehudah considers the <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2011/07/chulin-30-process-or-result-of.html">complete act of slaughter as shechitah</a>, with the “blood of its kill” being part of it, whereas Rabbi Chiya only considers the <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2011/07/chulin-30-process-or-result-of.html">final moment as shechitah</a>, thus at each stage it is only a doubt if a valid shechitah will result.<br />
<br />
Art: Jan Lievens - Jacob Receiving the Blooded Tunic of Joseph<br />
</span>

---

### content/chullin/37.txt
<a id="src-00331"></a>

**Source file:** `content/chullin/37.txt`

Chullin 37 – An Animal that is Close to Its Death
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgMTBnqVvVCrBXVUhzx5u_WshmwQ2AOvmAdpaMogLDJ47vL0YPJmIua1_F4Q3-G-5zaUqEzqddsxZuWYXa-56iE0tlqXOYj8yYgYZfJbkFLVO9idCTtpGiiPw-pTo8hCx57-aLZhYAvJKo/s1600/Frans+Snyders+-+A+deer%252C+a+fawn+and+other+dead+game+suspended+on+hooks.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgMTBnqVvVCrBXVUhzx5u_WshmwQ2AOvmAdpaMogLDJ47vL0YPJmIua1_F4Q3-G-5zaUqEzqddsxZuWYXa-56iE0tlqXOYj8yYgYZfJbkFLVO9idCTtpGiiPw-pTo8hCx57-aLZhYAvJKo/s320/Frans+Snyders+-+A+deer%252C+a+fawn+and+other+dead+game+suspended+on+hooks.jpg" width="242" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Water and other liquids are not the only agents that prepare foods to accept ritual impurity. The “love” or the “esteem for the holy things” is another. This unusual concept works in the following way: even the frankincense and the wood, which are not edible at all, can accept impurity if they are part of a sacrifice, and certainly food. This is derived from an extra word “meat” in the phrase “<a href="http://bible.ort.org/books/pentd2.asp?ACTION=displaypage&amp;BOOK=3&amp;CHAPTER=7">and the meat, anybody who is pure can eat the meat</a>.”<br />
<br />
If an animal is close to death, then we are afraid that perhaps it died before the shechitah. Therefore, for such an animal we need additional signs of vitality. Rabban Shimon ben Gamliel says that it needs to jerk its foreleg and its hind leg. Rabbi Eliezer says that it is sufficient for it to spout blood. The Sages say that it needs to jerk either a foreleg or a hind leg, or wag its tail. A small animal that merely extended its foreleg but did not retract it is not kosher, since this is just the spasm of the expiration of life.<br />
<br />
Art: Frans Snyders - A deer, a fawn and other dead game suspended on hooks</span>

---

### content/chullin/38.txt
<a id="src-00332"></a>

**Source file:** `content/chullin/38.txt`

Chullin 38 – Signs of Vitality
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEi45pBWAvP8S7-LU6j6fphKwFnpOrAKx4s35AMF0wHINP1DlNaSczDeptKUp5sJYBcmMovwvGQp3exYfvogCQrR3xOhsJYQCnsuLYDKFk-cFHQ6jixuxQA-TPlZlWHJqG5dGnVZky1l908/s1600/Frank+Johnson+-+The+Wounded+Buffalo.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="224" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEi45pBWAvP8S7-LU6j6fphKwFnpOrAKx4s35AMF0wHINP1DlNaSczDeptKUp5sJYBcmMovwvGQp3exYfvogCQrR3xOhsJYQCnsuLYDKFk-cFHQ6jixuxQA-TPlZlWHJqG5dGnVZky1l908/s320/Frank+Johnson+-+The+Wounded+Buffalo.jpg" width="320" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">How do we know that an animal that is close to death is allowed to be eaten altogether? Since the Torah said “<a href="http://bible.ort.org/books/pentd2.asp?ACTION=displaypage&amp;BOOK=3&amp;CHAPTER=11">This is the animal (“chaya” meaning a live creature) that you may eat</a>”, then perhaps an animal that is close its death you may not eat?<br />
<br />
No! That's can't be, because the Torah also said, “<a href="http://bible.ort.org/books/pentd2.asp?ACTION=displaypage&amp;BOOK=5&amp;CHAPTER=14">Do not eat nevelah, an animal that died by itself</a>” which means that all the time that it is alive, you may slaughter and eat it. But perhaps <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2011/07/terefah-and-nevelah-two-categories-of.html">nevelah</a> and close to death are the same thing!? Rather, since Ezekiel said in his prayer “I never ate <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2011/07/terefah-and-nevelah-two-categories-of.html">terefah</a> or nevelah,” we understand that he never ate the meat of an animal that was close to death, though normally this is allowed – for otherwise, what would be his special praise?<br />
<br />
What is considered an animal close to death? One that cannot rise even when prompted to. Even if it gnaws on hard foods, this is done only out of desperation and in an attempt to escape death. If it lows with low mooing sounds, releases waste or wiggles its ear – it is alive.<br />
<br />
Art: Frank Johnson - The Wounded Buffalo</span>

---

### content/chullin/39.txt
<a id="src-00333"></a>

**Source file:** `content/chullin/39.txt`

Chullin 39 – Shechitah for the Sake of an Idolater
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjtwtsGoBIRXknIkFmtCkdor87-nYlH7a69QOJSbT4_E1LW9Ji0PyswNZdRuU51uT_4Y3Bj5hjAKj9gBSjMjKrVh_tp6pXUAS_tLi-1H8F_ljNnhDQ3NIES91JEtftTWcJxv_ATPsT744g/s1600/Jacob+Willemsz+de+Wet+the+Elder+-+Figures+Offering+A+Sacrifice+In+A+Temple.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="217" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjtwtsGoBIRXknIkFmtCkdor87-nYlH7a69QOJSbT4_E1LW9Ji0PyswNZdRuU51uT_4Y3Bj5hjAKj9gBSjMjKrVh_tp6pXUAS_tLi-1H8F_ljNnhDQ3NIES91JEtftTWcJxv_ATPsT744g/s320/Jacob+Willemsz+de+Wet+the+Elder+-+Figures+Offering+A+Sacrifice+In+A+Temple.jpg" width="320" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">If an idolater asks a Jew to perform shechitah to the idolater's animal, the shechitah is valid. Rabbi Eliezer declares the meat forbidden. According to Rabbi Eliezer, the unspoken thought of an idolater is to dedicate the animal for his idol. Therefore, even if he sells the animal to the Jew but keeps a small part for the himself, the complete animal is prohibited. Actually, the first teacher agrees that the intent of the idolater takes effect, only the first teacher requires that it be spoken, and according to Rabbi Eliezer, even the thought is sufficient, and we can even assume that thought.<br />
<br />
Rabbi Yose disagrees and claims that the owner's thought has no effect at all. He argues thus. If in the Temple, where the kohen's intent is pervasive and makes or breaks a sacrifice, the owner's intent does not matter, then certainly in the case of regular food, the owner's intent is ineffective.<br />
<br />
Rabbi Eliezer answers that firstly, when the Torah uses the term "one who brings the sacrifice," it means both the kohen and the owner. Secondly, just as in the Temple, the owner's idolatrous intent matters, so too it matters for regular shechitah outside the Temple.<br />
<br />
Art: Jacob Willemsz de Wet the Elder - Figures Offering A Sacrifice In A Temple</span>

---

### content/chullin/4.txt
<a id="src-00334"></a>

**Source file:** `content/chullin/4.txt`

Chullin 4 – The Path to a Person's Heart is Paved with Food and Drink
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjQMaBaqecfm5fuE18MLNI-M5ejqY9fa4Hxg2XHlNMD4wfG28M4JIKvPF36PDGOiKKrVb_bKGYGFjvXKHXhFl_TjYh3M3X4CHZar5HtHZ8156uRqfdxeN-82oZPSFD0vDQVjaJILmMczNM/s1600/Paul+Gauguin+-+Portrait+Of+The+Artist+With+The+Idol+.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjQMaBaqecfm5fuE18MLNI-M5ejqY9fa4Hxg2XHlNMD4wfG28M4JIKvPF36PDGOiKKrVb_bKGYGFjvXKHXhFl_TjYh3M3X4CHZar5HtHZ8156uRqfdxeN-82oZPSFD0vDQVjaJILmMczNM/s320/Paul+Gauguin+-+Portrait+Of+The+Artist+With+The+Idol+.jpg" width="240" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Previously <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2011/06/chullin-3-slaughter-done-by-non.html">we learned</a> that a Jew who habitually eats non-kosher meat can still be trusted with kosher slaughter, since, given the choice, he will expend the minimal effort required, and the kosher slaughter is still significant in his eyes.<br />
<br />
Rav Anan said that even a Jew who worships idols – which is considered as an abandonment of the whole Torah – can still do shechitah. We know this because Yehoshaphat, the righteous king of Judah, <a href="http://bible.cc/2_chronicles/18-2.htm">partook of the feast of idol worshiping Ahab, who thus enticed him to join forces in battle</a>.<br />
<br />
But perhaps Ahab slaughtered the animals, but Yehoshaphat did not eat them? - There is no enticement with mere words. Incidentally, although the Torah says “if your brother will entice you (to idol worship)” - that too is done with food and drink. But was not God upset with Satan for enticing Him against Job, without food? - God is different, since He does not eat anyway.<br />
<br />
Back to Yehoshaphat, perhaps he only drank but did not eat? – It is not fitting for a king to drink but not eat at a feast.<br />
<br />
Art: Paul Gauguin - Portrait Of The Artist With The Idol </span>

---

### content/chullin/40.txt
<a id="src-00335"></a>

**Source file:** `content/chullin/40.txt`

Chullin 40 – Slaughter Done for the Sake of a Mountain
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjZ62_vFA4jbWpkmQ-kp9NciiS-KxB_zXyhukS0UpdOHmYYQ3NWUp80yBPrkT-OQ1eAelrUVC455jJJSnxczEhYL5GlJTsdnesgGpURyBzI2Oiu_LFyGQ3I48qz0X1EQg2_f5Bi5f0HRWg/s1600/Gustave+Dore+-+Gorge+In+The+Mountains.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="210" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjZ62_vFA4jbWpkmQ-kp9NciiS-KxB_zXyhukS0UpdOHmYYQ3NWUp80yBPrkT-OQ1eAelrUVC455jJJSnxczEhYL5GlJTsdnesgGpURyBzI2Oiu_LFyGQ3I48qz0X1EQg2_f5Bi5f0HRWg/s320/Gustave+Dore+-+Gorge+In+The+Mountains.jpg" width="320" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">If one slaughters an animal for the sake of mountains, for the sake of seas, for the sake of rivers, or for the sake of deserts, his slaughter is invalid.<br />
<br />
Had he slaughtered for the sake of the spirit of the mountain, it would clearly be an idolatrous sacrifice, and would be forbidden for all benefit. That would be true regardless of the importance of the idol, be it the greatest angel Michael or the smallest worm with spiritual qualities ascribed to it. So by right, slaughtering for the sake of a mountain should be allowed – but the Sages made it forbidden because it is too close to an idolatrous sacrifice. However, they did not go so far as to prohibit it for all benefit.<br />
<br />
Rav Huna gave the following rule: if someone else's animal was lying in front of an idol, and one started to slaughter it – once he cut one pipe, or even less, makes a small cut – he made it prohibited for use. Even thought normally one cannot prohibit something that is not his, in a case like this, where he did an action, even a small action suffices.<br />
<br />
Art: Gustave Dore - Gorge In The Mountains</span>

---

### content/chullin/41.txt
<a id="src-00336"></a>

**Source file:** `content/chullin/41.txt`

Chullin 41 – A Person Cannot Forbid Something That Is Not His
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjouY2w6vI9vhAyseIUV2TIuBuBMiRnW84DNWWJnrtZDstybuO3vSKVRXe0Z-QNpAgbspIi0qEKBRKN3sElXhAbyT73afbAoQgUd5t4tTaTRrPrGTvl1zqfoMGtluFfRHaMFfH5vD3vuLA/s1600/Carl+Spitzweg+-+Still+Life+With+A+Jellyjar%252C+A+Carafe+And+A+Bottle+Of+Wine.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjouY2w6vI9vhAyseIUV2TIuBuBMiRnW84DNWWJnrtZDstybuO3vSKVRXe0Z-QNpAgbspIi0qEKBRKN3sElXhAbyT73afbAoQgUd5t4tTaTRrPrGTvl1zqfoMGtluFfRHaMFfH5vD3vuLA/s320/Carl+Spitzweg+-+Still+Life+With+A+Jellyjar%252C+A+Carafe+And+A+Bottle+Of+Wine.jpg" width="286" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">If an idolater performed a libation with a Jew's wine, but did it not in front of an idol, then Rabbi Yehudah ben Beteira and Rabbi Yehudah ben Bava say that the wine remains kosher, for two reasons: libations are normally done in front of an idol, and moreover, a person cannot forbid something that is not his. This point of view argues against <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2011/08/chullin-40-slaughter-done-for-sake-of.html">what Rav Huna said about slaughter in front of idol</a>.<br />
<br />
This opinion also argues against the concept of kosher wine. According to it, if a Jew owns the wine, it never becomes non-kosher, even if touched or processed by non-Jews. However, it does not become law, and it was not mentioned in the <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/search/label/Avodah%20Zarah">whole tractate of Avodah Zarah</a>.<br />
<br />
One may not slaughter into a sea or into a river, because it may seem that he is slaughtering to the spirit of the sea or the river. One may slaughter into a pool of water, because blood mixed with water would never be used in idol worship.<br />
<br />
If one slaughters a regular animal in the name of some free-will offering, then people may confuse it with an actual offering, and the shechitah is declared non-kosher.<br />
<br />
Art: Carl Spitzweg - Still Life With A Jellyjar, A Carafe And A Bottle Of Wine</span>

---

### content/chullin/42.txt
<a id="src-00337"></a>

**Source file:** `content/chullin/42.txt`

Chullin 42 – These Are The Cases of Terefah
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhk4CUQr_SLO_krQzRo52GqaykgkL5RTGy8dG-9ifjDNLGySiNOtPxcEQfQvZ3BaAmipkTTi2FNt8tmZ6xQ0oDV4NZqazPa2-jS6_iCn53-LhdYNjPcRAAF7B3_yZuoWuHH1E7mW9B-3rk/s1600/George+Frederick+Watts+-+The+Wounded+Heron.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhk4CUQr_SLO_krQzRo52GqaykgkL5RTGy8dG-9ifjDNLGySiNOtPxcEQfQvZ3BaAmipkTTi2FNt8tmZ6xQ0oDV4NZqazPa2-jS6_iCn53-LhdYNjPcRAAF7B3_yZuoWuHH1E7mW9B-3rk/s320/George+Frederick+Watts+-+The+Wounded+Heron.jpg" width="244" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">The Torah said, “<a href="http://bible.ort.org/books/pentd2.asp?ACTION=displaypage&amp;BOOK=2&amp;CHAPTER=22#P2142">Do not eat flesh torn off in the field by a predator</a>.” This cannot mean that the animal already died by itself – for then it would be a case of nevelah, carcass. Rather, it is talking about an animal that is fatally wounded. Even if it was properly slaughtered, it is forbidden to be eaten as “terefah.” The defect may be caused by an animal or a man, in any place, it can even be congenital, and “in the field” simply describes a common scenario.<br />
<br />
There are eight general categories of <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2011/07/terefah-and-nevelah-two-categories-of.html">terefah</a>, taught to Moses on Sinai, and they can be arranged according to the Hebrew acronym of “dan chanak nefesh(דן חנק נףש).” They are: clawed, punctured, deficient, removed, torn, fallen, severed, and fractured. For practical purposes the classification of terefah was divided into eighteen cases, starting with an animal whose esophagus was punctured, one whose trachea was severed, whose brain was punctured, and so on.<br />
<br />
The laws that follow are complex, and the difficulty is compounded by the fact that not everybody knows the necessary details of the <a href="http://www.animalcorner.co.uk/farm/cows/cow_anatomy.html">animal anatomy</a>. Artscroll illustrations&nbsp;can help.<br />
<br />
Art: George Frederick Watts - The Wounded Heron</span>

---

### content/chullin/43.txt
<a id="src-00338"></a>

**Source file:** `content/chullin/43.txt`

Chullin 43 – Seven Teachings of Terefah
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhWH3v4b101fmb6tet6gpKrj5kJHy_Y1UkmLbsOXpGWSAotd5u8IzKq7Fw4c2QKlY4NzaZz6wetUrKCDdm3WrhxU8H7unSgNHYoJetztdp9grNTA_peKTaj7BoYjZe1IrrHR89xF1O-zRI/s1600/James+Hayllar+-+The+Thorn.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhWH3v4b101fmb6tet6gpKrj5kJHy_Y1UkmLbsOXpGWSAotd5u8IzKq7Fw4c2QKlY4NzaZz6wetUrKCDdm3WrhxU8H7unSgNHYoJetztdp9grNTA_peKTaj7BoYjZe1IrrHR89xF1O-zRI/s320/James+Hayllar+-+The+Thorn.jpg" width="238" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">There were seven more signs of <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2011/07/terefah-and-nevelah-two-categories-of.html">terefah</a>. They included the teaching of Rav Matna about the ball of the thighbone that popped out of its place in the socket, the teaching of Rachish bar Pappa about an animal that became diseased in one kidney, and so on. However, how could they change the <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2011/08/chullin-42-these-are-cases-of-terefah.html">classical number of the eighteen cases</a>? They did not, rather, those who teach those seven rules combine all cases of punctured organs into one, and then add the seven.<br />
<br />
The esophagus has two layers, a red one and a white one. If one was punctured, but the other was not, the animal is not a terefah. The gizzard also has two layers, so the above rule applies. If both layers either in the esophagus or in the gizzard were perforated, but the holes are not aligned with each other – some say that in the case of the esophagus it is kosher, but in the case of gizzard it is terefah, and some say the opposite.<br />
<br />
Ulla said, if a thorn is lodged in the esophagus, we do not suspect that it healed (which would still be terefah), rather, it was never punctured. <br />
<br />
Art: James Hayllar - The Thorn</span>

---

### content/chullin/44.txt
<a id="src-00339"></a>

**Source file:** `content/chullin/44.txt`

Chullin 44 – The Pharynx
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgjLcj89gx-zYM7rDmr1M8OFbM-ntY6bVVTk_RfdqP_IR6yiMxdj86_UqavNGp613Qa3YVZWWWcoo7sY0FPrHDqvI3QjGx0HzzjVQJkT6t_F7YrThauZqfWDkJtQJnaC5uMctAe4Clmazg/s1600/Winslow+Homer+-+The+Country+Store.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="203" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgjLcj89gx-zYM7rDmr1M8OFbM-ntY6bVVTk_RfdqP_IR6yiMxdj86_UqavNGp613Qa3YVZWWWcoo7sY0FPrHDqvI3QjGx0HzzjVQJkT6t_F7YrThauZqfWDkJtQJnaC5uMctAe4Clmazg/s320/Winslow+Homer+-+The+Country+Store.jpg" width="320" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">The stiff, uppermost section of the food-pipe, roughly equivalent to the pharynx, is where the food-pipe is attached to the jaw. Rav says that any slight puncture in it renders the animal a <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2011/07/terefah-and-nevelah-two-categories-of.html">terefah</a>. Why? According to Rav, there is no limit where one can cut the food-pipe, and it is only the windpipe that has limits. It follows then that the pharynx is a place of shechitah, and no puncture there is tolerated. On the contrary, Shmuel says that there is a definite limit where the food-pipe can be cut, and it is below the pharynx. Accordingly, the pharynx itself can be punctured, as long as the defect is less than its half.<br />
<br />
If the majority of the trachea of an animal was split, it is terefah. They brought such a case to examine before Rav, and Rav ruled the animal terefah, because he measured on the outside of the windpipe. However, Rabbah bar bar Chanah measured on the inside, declared the animal kosher, and bought thirteen measures of its meat. But didn't he buy it on the cheap and therefore benefited from his own ruling? – No, he didn't, because he bought it at the going market price.<br />
<br />
Art: Winslow Homer - The Country Store<br />
</span>

---

### content/chullin/45.txt
<a id="src-00340"></a>

**Source file:** `content/chullin/45.txt`

Chullin 45 – Who Is An Honest Sage?
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgplVxBP21-obZQM1ZdZpa3RWgGyGteLB36Xm16h4oebmCIqCCFwg-UJoJz8XaHGPnOhOpdwcqVnGMc-cXIxKZeW0ook1uSVEUl1tpFP5If17siTs4IKbrfF8EjVtENhPmZ7TNFWH8PW3A/s1600/Justus+Juncker+-+A+Scholar+Sitting+At+His+Desk.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgplVxBP21-obZQM1ZdZpa3RWgGyGteLB36Xm16h4oebmCIqCCFwg-UJoJz8XaHGPnOhOpdwcqVnGMc-cXIxKZeW0ook1uSVEUl1tpFP5If17siTs4IKbrfF8EjVtENhPmZ7TNFWH8PW3A/s320/Justus+Juncker+-+A+Scholar+Sitting+At+His+Desk.jpg" width="268" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Rav Chisda said: “Who is considered an honest Torah scholar? – One, who in a case of an equal doubt if his animal was slaughtered correctly or it became a <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2011/07/terefah-and-nevelah-two-categories-of.html">terefah</a>, decided that it was a terefah and bore the loss.” About him the Psalms say, “When you eat the labor of your hands, happy are you and it will be well with you.” Rav Zevid explained, “Happy are you in this world” - because he does not rely on the support of others. “It will be well with you” - in the World to Come – because he will stay away from theft, which would diminish his share in the World to Come.<br />
<br />
If an animal's windpipe was perforated like a sieve, then if the flesh was merely moved to the side, the animal is kosher unless half of the windpipe was perforated; however, if the flesh in the perforations was missing, then once the holes combine to an area of an issar coin, the animal is terefah.<br />
<br />
Further cases of terefah: if the membrane of the brain was punctured, and this means the lower membrane; or if the heart was punctured into its chamber.<br />
<br />
Art: Justus Juncker - A Scholar Sitting At His Desk</span>

---

### content/chullin/46.txt
<a id="src-00341"></a>

**Source file:** `content/chullin/46.txt`

Chullin 46 – The Spine, The Liver, and The Lung
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhEMou6bKHHJYWwC11ApsDbLOJ8loA5zi8sTO79k1DFoHE00iATpfXDl-3eamKEJHNginnMnXLTYxbUAz08nG_jaVEUhzMtaMNyPy73roOVjCWvIVBorAh5kFARukiJ_VOl_s3x55tF-RM/s1600/Juan+Bautista+de+Espinosa+-+Still+Life+Of+Fruits+And+A+Plate+Of+Olives.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="237" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhEMou6bKHHJYWwC11ApsDbLOJ8loA5zi8sTO79k1DFoHE00iATpfXDl-3eamKEJHNginnMnXLTYxbUAz08nG_jaVEUhzMtaMNyPy73roOVjCWvIVBorAh5kFARukiJ_VOl_s3x55tF-RM/s320/Juan+Bautista+de+Espinosa+-+Still+Life+Of+Fruits+And+A+Plate+Of+Olives.jpg" width="320" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">If the spine was broken and its cord severed – the animal is a terefah. Rabbi Yehudah the Prince says that the majority of the spinal cord must be severed, but Rabbi Yakov says that even if the spinal cord was merely punctured – the animal is a terefah. Rabbi Yehudah ruled stringently in practice, like Rabbi Yakov, but the law is like Rabbi Yehudah's own lenient view.<br />
<br />
If the liver was removed and nothing remained of it – the animal is a terefah. Elsewhere we learned that if less than an olive-volume remains, it is a terefah. Which is right? The opinion that requires an olive-volume belongs to Shimon the son of Rabbi Yehudah. He considered liver an organ important for the animal, therefore a healthy food, and ate it. Rabbi Chiya is the one who held that any remaining piece of the liver is sufficient. He considered the liver not such an important organ, not a healthy food, and threw it away.<br />
<br />
If the lung was punctured in both membranes, the animal is a terefah. The lung can be examined by blowing it or by submerging it in warm water.<br />
<br />
Art: Juan Bautista de Espinosa - Still Life Of Fruits And A Plate Of Olives<br />
</span>

---

### content/chullin/47.txt
<a id="src-00342"></a>

**Source file:** `content/chullin/47.txt`

Chullin 47 – Adhesion of the Lung
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiY0b-4fto_Et9hA4w2Zr5xwXFxMeL-V9rzeuIl3mf1I_6hlNO_PSjcxP-BkuuKyZClXPth1ROM1aGtwejzR_eoMVZ2cIiKqWg1UJdtIJNGto8YAp-kB7Tvpi0PB5occL9FijQ8nn8-BS0/s1600/Claude+Oscar+Monet+-+The+Blue+House+At+Zaandam.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="240" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiY0b-4fto_Et9hA4w2Zr5xwXFxMeL-V9rzeuIl3mf1I_6hlNO_PSjcxP-BkuuKyZClXPth1ROM1aGtwejzR_eoMVZ2cIiKqWg1UJdtIJNGto8YAp-kB7Tvpi0PB5occL9FijQ8nn8-BS0/s320/Claude+Oscar+Monet+-+The+Blue+House+At+Zaandam.jpg" width="320" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">A lung has five lobes, three on the right and two on the left. If two lobes are found to adhere to each other, there is no point in the examination – the animal is terefah even if the lungs are airtight. Rashi says that the adhesion is the result of a hole in the lungs, from which viscous fluids leaked, causing it to close. It is nevertheless terefah, because such healing is impermanent. Tosafot say that there was no hole as yet, but that the adhesion will cause it to happen. Since a puncture will inevitably occur, the animal is terefah immediately. This is true only for two lobes that are not in proximity of each other, for otherwise this is the way they naturally grow.<br />
<br />
Rava says that an extra lobe in the lungs makes an animal a terefah. Rav Acha was sitting in front of Mereimar's house when a butcher brought a case of an extra lobe for examination. Mereimar declared it kosher. Rav Acha said to the butcher, “Go ask Mereimar again.” Mereimar said to the butcher, “Tell the one sitting in front of my house that the law is not like Rava.”<br />
<br />
Art: Claude Oscar Monet - The Blue House At Zaandam</span>

---

### content/chullin/48.txt
<a id="src-00343"></a>

**Source file:** `content/chullin/48.txt`

Chullin 48 – Defects in the Lungs
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgxSTJsQaA7LLa3y8vBQsgPVSTRnA4I1hH1L75DSQiMXKL2XrIgUjEVczEcLHaaDr9pSg_Kts9k4izaO6gnarbJbnkkdRZcthFQXYSKNCNgXdq5P7AM2TsREa3ns0S0X04ZmXyjifbWs0s/s1600/Louis+Coulon+-+The+Prick+Of+The+Needle.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgxSTJsQaA7LLa3y8vBQsgPVSTRnA4I1hH1L75DSQiMXKL2XrIgUjEVczEcLHaaDr9pSg_Kts9k4izaO6gnarbJbnkkdRZcthFQXYSKNCNgXdq5P7AM2TsREa3ns0S0X04ZmXyjifbWs0s/s320/Louis+Coulon+-+The+Prick+Of+The+Needle.jpg" width="262" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Ulla said in the name of Rabbi Yochanan, “If the insides of the lung have dissolved to the point that they pour back and forth in the encasing membranes, like water in a jug, the animal is still kosher.” Rabbi Abba challenged this from the following rule. We learned in the eighteen basic cases of terefah that if a lung was punctured or is deficient, the animal is terefah. Does “deficient” not include the case of Ulla? – Ulla answers, “No! Punctured means a hole that leaves all the material in place, and deficient means some material is missing around the hole. Still, this rule is talking about external deficiencies, and not about internal ones.”<br />
<br />
What if a needle was found in the lung? Some say that it probably entered there through the digestive tract, must have perforated the lung at some point, and is therefore a terefah, since such punctures never properly heal. However, others say that, although less likely, it entered through the trachea, never perforated the lung, and the animal is therefore kosher. They also assume that the minor deterioration in the vicinity of the needle is not significant.<br />
<br />
Art: Louis Coulon - The Prick Of The Needle</span>

---

### content/chullin/49.txt
<a id="src-00344"></a>

**Source file:** `content/chullin/49.txt`

Chullin 49 – A Needle Found in the Liver
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEi32yGm6ZiwmF4TeC68_a4JPUSz-K0iyG4gvayB_Ws4QT3xEWTBpIL14DHOFfClfCqw6tqAwyee-H3XWY865EsSv-oTSGO3ttLx_EAu7E6So45gDYpzEveTQkq8JRBA5Yc_b_CF7UBNP2Y/s1600/Jules+%2528Adolphe+Aime+Louis%2529+Breton+-+Peasant+Woman+Threading+A+Needle.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEi32yGm6ZiwmF4TeC68_a4JPUSz-K0iyG4gvayB_Ws4QT3xEWTBpIL14DHOFfClfCqw6tqAwyee-H3XWY865EsSv-oTSGO3ttLx_EAu7E6So45gDYpzEveTQkq8JRBA5Yc_b_CF7UBNP2Y/s320/Jules+%2528Adolphe+Aime+Louis%2529+Breton+-+Peasant+Woman+Threading+A+Needle.jpg" width="208" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">There was once a case of a needle found in the liver of an animal, and Mar the son of Rav Yosef was inclined to rule the animal terefah. Rav Ashi said to him, “Why is this worse than a needle in an ordinary piece of meat? Rather, I look at the position of the needle. If its head it sticking out of the liver, then clearly it has come into the liver by way of puncturing from the outside, and thus has made an animal a terefah, because it punctured the digestive track. But if the head is inside, then it must have taken the vascular route and is beginning to exit out of the liver, thus the animal is kosher.”<br />
<br />
Abomasum is the fourth and final division in the stomach of a cow. If it was punctured, the animal is terefah. Incidentally, the kohanim, who receive this abomasum with its rennet as one of the gifts due them, have adopted the practice of allowing this fat for consumption, following Rabbi Ishmael, who is also a kohen. He also explains the order of blessings to their benefit, as: they bless the people, and God blesses them.<br />
<br />
Art: Jules (Adolphe Aime Louis) Breton - Peasant Woman Threading A Needle</span>

---

### content/chullin/5.txt
<a id="src-00345"></a>

**Source file:** `content/chullin/5.txt`

Chullin 5 – An Idol-Worshiping Jew Cannot Do Shechitah
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhaTC6CzmQr-9VZWOTKG_pd1jvPY-42o6XpaPKkAX5j1vyssqpWEccc9ALUkeQUWqSnGvpzoo9TQTwKiGP17UnXov6G8M_B6UeDb4WMsi3UNpM3WqJKcKN3QIFR0gJ9QHssGbHxS3desQ4/s1600/Sir+Edwin+Henry+Landseer+-+Isaac+van+Amburgh+and+his+Animals.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="203" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhaTC6CzmQr-9VZWOTKG_pd1jvPY-42o6XpaPKkAX5j1vyssqpWEccc9ALUkeQUWqSnGvpzoo9TQTwKiGP17UnXov6G8M_B6UeDb4WMsi3UNpM3WqJKcKN3QIFR0gJ9QHssGbHxS3desQ4/s320/Sir+Edwin+Henry+Landseer+-+Isaac+van+Amburgh+and+his+Animals.jpg" width="320" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Previously was learned <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2011/06/chullin-4-path-to-persons-heart-is.html">the opinion of Rav Anan</a> that an idol-worshiping Jew can do kosher slaughter of animals. Here is a challenge to it. <br />
<br />
The Torah said, “<a href="http://bible.cc/leviticus/1-2.htm">When a man among you brings an offering to God: from the animals</a>...” The words “among you” tell us that some people are excluded from bringing voluntary offerings to God, namely, completely non-observant Jews. Further, “among you” means that only to Jews can the term “non-observant” apply, but all non-Jews can bring offerings. The words “from the animals” are extra and teach another law: people who are similar to animals in that they do not recognize their Creator are included and are still allowed to bring sacrifices, in the hope that they will improve their behavior. <br />
<br />
Then who is considered non-observant? Those who deny the complete Torah, that is, those who pour libations to idols and those who violate Shabbat in public. With this, Rav Anan's proof is refuted, and only people who observe Shabbat but violate some commandments, such as eating non-kosher meat, are allowed to do shechitah.<br />
<br />
Art: Sir Edwin Henry Landseer - Isaac van Amburgh and his Animals<br />
</span>

---

### content/chullin/50.txt
<a id="src-00346"></a>

**Source file:** `content/chullin/50.txt`

Chullin 50 – Intestines, Rectum
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEh0ZNtecNgDMCNu_gMTpjNVucDnOL_uFTEPyOal4fDrqd_VP7ibv_0GlAenQKabdd4uPTHwb9lTMy1ZJdhXuAF3vQ-a0rWzlaxxTFuv9fdIFNxzbZzM8NEHU4JmHCQg2Z-P6ou4i-6vbQM/s1600/Lorenzo+Delleani+-+Wise+Counsel.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEh0ZNtecNgDMCNu_gMTpjNVucDnOL_uFTEPyOal4fDrqd_VP7ibv_0GlAenQKabdd4uPTHwb9lTMy1ZJdhXuAF3vQ-a0rWzlaxxTFuv9fdIFNxzbZzM8NEHU4JmHCQg2Z-P6ou4i-6vbQM/s320/Lorenzo+Delleani+-+Wise+Counsel.jpg" width="254" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">If the intestines are punctured, the animal is terefah. However, it is also possible that the puncture happened after the animal was slaughtered. In that case it would be kosher. To find out when did the puncture really happen, one can compare a puncture in the intestines to the new one, made just for the purpose. If they look similar, the first puncture was made by people handling the meat after the slaughter, and the animal is kosher. If they differ, the animal is terefah.<br />
<br />
They brought such a case before Rava, who made an additional puncture, and seeing that it looked different, wanted to declare the animal a terefah. His son Rav Mesharshiya said to him, “Think of all the hands that the first puncture went through before it came to you.” Rav Mesharshiya then rubbed the new puncture, and it appeared the same as the old ones. Thi showed that the animal was kosher. Rava said, “My son is as wise as Rabbi Yochanan.”<br />
<br />
If the rectum was punctured, this does not make the animal terefah, because the hips support it. Even if only a finger-width of the rectum remained intact, it is kosher.<br />
<br />
Art: Lorenzo Delleani - Wise Counsel</span>

---

### content/chullin/51.txt
<a id="src-00347"></a>

**Source file:** `content/chullin/51.txt`

Chullin 51 – Blind Pouch, Reticulum
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiVAcTD0PH-aI6TaWvZy6jafDYTvLsiYfXIBx1dvoeR2K9Xq_l53Q0QQ9R71jqPuJrvtCAFs3VPIgtzr_07c5BrH6Vt-FcrO8hEFgOlWpnyydEFri65ykoqn-PJumHNw16ufE9KaBg-jLg/s1600/Joseph+Crawhall+-+Pigeons+on+the+Roof.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiVAcTD0PH-aI6TaWvZy6jafDYTvLsiYfXIBx1dvoeR2K9Xq_l53Q0QQ9R71jqPuJrvtCAFs3VPIgtzr_07c5BrH6Vt-FcrO8hEFgOlWpnyydEFri65ykoqn-PJumHNw16ufE9KaBg-jLg/s1600/Joseph+Crawhall+-+Pigeons+on+the+Roof.jpg" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">If an inner paunch of the animal was punctured or the greater part of its outer paunch was torn, the animal is a terefah. What is an inner paunch? The smallest definition says it is the blind pouch, or the cecum, “hated by wolves” in Hebrew, since even wolves don't eat it. The largest definition says that it is the entire bottom of the paunch, which faces the ground when the animal is standing.<br />
<br />
Reticulim is the second compartment of the stomach. If it is punctured from the outside, the animal is a terefah. If a needle was found it in, and it goes through both walls, the animal is a terefah, provided that the puncture occurred while the animal was still alive. A drop of blood can testify to that. However, if a scab formed over the opening of the puncture would, then it is clear that the puncture occurred more than three days before. Thus the animal was terefah when one bought it, and he can ask for his money back.<br />
<br />
If an animal fell from a roof, it is considered terefah without any further signs, unless it survives for the next twenty-four hours.<br />
<br />
Art: Joseph Crawhall - Pigeons on the Roof</span>

---

### content/chullin/52.txt
<a id="src-00348"></a>

**Source file:** `content/chullin/52.txt`

Chullin 52 – Clawed by a Wolf
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhwk9NbcxPR1PquXmiakXDiuiPqIo0AqrNsEAVNkLX1zRT7uG5UaRu5MwaxSolj5zwwa0PaiegW_utQ3zabrXd3DY81Fn_61Qu5TQRB0zQG3pe-1ubAeX7lm6UYl0br3FCx-q5_8Ub9vzc/s1600/William+Henry+Hamilton+Trood+-+Cats.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhwk9NbcxPR1PquXmiakXDiuiPqIo0AqrNsEAVNkLX1zRT7uG5UaRu5MwaxSolj5zwwa0PaiegW_utQ3zabrXd3DY81Fn_61Qu5TQRB0zQG3pe-1ubAeX7lm6UYl0br3FCx-q5_8Ub9vzc/s320/William+Henry+Hamilton+Trood+-+Cats.jpg" width="240" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">If most of the ribs of an animal are broken, that animal is <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2011/07/terefah-and-nevelah-two-categories-of.html">terefah</a>. Rav Kahana and Rav Assi had two questions for Rav, which they wisely combined into one: “If a rib on one side of a vertebra and on another side was uprooted, what is the law?” They also wanted to know about one rib, but figured that if Rav gets angry when answering their question, then even one rib makes it a terefah. Rav answered, “That animal is split in half! It is nevelah!” This was a form of getting angry, and they had their two answers.<br />
<br />
If the skull of an animal was crushed in its greater part, the animal is terefah. If it was clawed by a wolf or a larger animal, it is a terefah due to the deposits of decayed meat under the predator's claws, which leads to bacterial infection. Some say that even a cat's clawing can be dangerous – but only if the cat is angry because of the prey's escape. Once a cat was chasing a chicken, and the door was slammed in its face, and the cat left five red spots on the door.<br />
<br />
Art: William Henry Hamilton Trood - Cats</span>

---

### content/chullin/53.txt
<a id="src-00349"></a>

**Source file:** `content/chullin/53.txt`

Chullin 53 – The One That is Clawed
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhRf49GU-PA-E2aA6qNYCDc_CC1qdsD9DpYUWzTpt65zyGDwdmTDDgFUfJtx1GiLITno54sCQPTW02Lv0FSI2bNCIJ5QwaRzwh9X7lHNR6EK_76Dkz-x4-T3434cv-Ny4mpCvBFtHUtVco/s1600/Geza+Vastagh+-+The+British+Lion.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="234" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhRf49GU-PA-E2aA6qNYCDc_CC1qdsD9DpYUWzTpt65zyGDwdmTDDgFUfJtx1GiLITno54sCQPTW02Lv0FSI2bNCIJ5QwaRzwh9X7lHNR6EK_76Dkz-x4-T3434cv-Ny4mpCvBFtHUtVco/s320/Geza+Vastagh+-+The+British+Lion.jpg" width="320" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">A small (sparrow) hawk can render small fowl terefah by clawing them, and a large hawk (falcon) can do it to large fowl. Clawing makes an animal terefah only if done with the foreleg, not hind leg and not a tooth, and not if the paw was severed before the predator drew it back.<br />
<br />
If a lion entered among the oxen, and subsequently a detached lion's claw was found embedded in the back of one of the oxen, we have two ways to reason. On the one hand, majority of lions do claw, and minority does not. That majority that claws usually does not leave a nail detached. Hence we might conclude that the ox rubbed himself against a wall and had the claw embed itself into its back. Or we can say that although most oxen rub themselves against the wall, but a claw does not usually become embedded in them, so perhaps this one was clawed. Rav, who rules leniently in cases of doubtful clawing, will declare the animal kosher, but Shmuel will say that it is terefah.<br />
<br />
An animal that was possibly clawed needs to be examined for the typical signs, the reddening of the meat.<br />
<br />
Art: Geza Vastagh - The British Lion</span>

---

### content/chullin/54.txt
<a id="src-00350"></a>

**Source file:** `content/chullin/54.txt`

Chullin 54 – The Non-Fatal Injuries
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg8p5VksIs4EtbpfwfLTs8jv9xx7EJ4h40n6DJ1Z8glqNaTcp3RYDT8OymAnlgIplqAau9cqQKJs2aAk1gwtyjx1_QQrq2hvWWY1Qft9cT31vaUqhVl8FNC3GQWiU0YwrrBshtYEy17CGE/s1600/Henry+Herbert+La+Thangue+-+The+Thorn.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="282" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg8p5VksIs4EtbpfwfLTs8jv9xx7EJ4h40n6DJ1Z8glqNaTcp3RYDT8OymAnlgIplqAau9cqQKJs2aAk1gwtyjx1_QQrq2hvWWY1Qft9cT31vaUqhVl8FNC3GQWiU0YwrrBshtYEy17CGE/s320/Henry+Herbert+La+Thangue+-+The+Thorn.jpg" width="320" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">If an animal is pierced by a thorn, this is not as strict as clawed by a predators, since the thorn does not usually lead to infection. The animal is not <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2011/07/terefah-and-nevelah-two-categories-of.html">terefah</a> unless the thorn went all the way to the body cavity.<br />
<br />
People in the family of Yosef the Hunter used to strike an animal on the sciatic nerve and cause it die in this manner. Nevertheless, this defect does not cause it to be a terefah, because with proper medicine it would heal.<br />
<br />
Now the discussion turns to non-fatal injuries, those that do not cause the animal to become terefah, such as the case when the trachea was split lengthwise, and not cut across, or when a piece of it less than the size of an Italian issar coin was missing. Rabbi Yochanan said that the <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2011/08/chullin-42-these-are-cases-of-terefah.html">list of fatal injuries</a> is specific, and things that are not on that list are kosher. Resh Lakish disagreed and said that the list of non-fatal injuries is specific and the rest are  terefah. Which case do they argue about? – The one described by Rav Matna, where the ball of the thighbone popped out of its place in the socket.<br />
<br />
Art: Henry Herbert La Thangue - The Thorn</span>

---

### content/chullin/55.txt
<a id="src-00351"></a>

**Source file:** `content/chullin/55.txt`

Chullin 55 – No Spleen, No Kidneys, The Animal Is  Still Kosher
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEggo9o0ltv6gnYQ6M2m1GKPQhUzoFmqGeLvbb_GkmHpLmsvl3aOH-vChJDyHAIlpevJ3o7NQVVnbUowa30BSkVbE1KBjt3dedD7iaPrkpiaXOC0jo-zQvP0K51M8IyIfULIK_viller2O4/s1600/Martin+Johnson+Heade+-+Thunder+Storm+On+Narragansett+Bay.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="172" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEggo9o0ltv6gnYQ6M2m1GKPQhUzoFmqGeLvbb_GkmHpLmsvl3aOH-vChJDyHAIlpevJ3o7NQVVnbUowa30BSkVbE1KBjt3dedD7iaPrkpiaXOC0jo-zQvP0K51M8IyIfULIK_viller2O4/s320/Martin+Johnson+Heade+-+Thunder+Storm+On+Narragansett+Bay.jpg" width="320" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">If the spleen was removed the animal remains kosher. Rav Avira explained that this was only said when the spleen was removed entirely, but if it was punctured, the animal is terefah – since the puncture causes great pain and illness in the body.<br />
<br />
If the kidneys were removed the animal remains kosher. However, Rachish bar Pappa said that if the animal was diseased in even one kidney, it is a terefah.<br />
<br />
The animal remains kosher if the lower jaw was removed. However, this is only true if it can be kept alive by human intervention of stuffing and pushing food into its throat. An animal whose uterus was removed remains kosher. One whose lung shriveled because of some fright of natural events, such as thunder and lightning, remains kosher, but not if it was scared of human. A flayed animal – Rabbi Meir declared it kosher, and the Sages sais that it is terefah, and later Rabbi Meir agreed to the opinion of the Sages.<br />
<br />
Art: Martin Johnson Heade - Thunder Storm On Narragansett Bay<br />
</span>

---

### content/chullin/56.txt
<a id="src-00352"></a>

**Source file:** `content/chullin/56.txt`

Chullin 56 – These are the Cases of Terefah in Fowl
