<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEimcGd7M-3FfPFSzue1T6TSdTyhTzHGCnWyhQPK8KacP3e9qetIJn4TA1lB27xcYEWbdK_Ub21LQN85YS4I7gqG4pf_bUNd7x0-O9QwS2j9ug2llPiRepMCenDaVP-QSgKOAsfLpeyZ0YQ/s1600/Wallerant+Vaillant+-+Young+Sportsman+with+Rabbit+and+Fowl.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEimcGd7M-3FfPFSzue1T6TSdTyhTzHGCnWyhQPK8KacP3e9qetIJn4TA1lB27xcYEWbdK_Ub21LQN85YS4I7gqG4pf_bUNd7x0-O9QwS2j9ug2llPiRepMCenDaVP-QSgKOAsfLpeyZ0YQ/s320/Wallerant+Vaillant+-+Young+Sportsman+with+Rabbit+and+Fowl.jpg" width="271" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">These are the cases of terefah in fowl: a bird whose esophagus was punctured, or one whose trachea was severed. If a weasel struck (bit) it on its head in a place that makes it a terefah, that is, opposite the brain, and there is a concern that the brain membrane may have been punctured. If the gizzard was punctured, or if the intestines were punctured.<br />
<br />
If a fowl fell into fire and its internal organs were scorched, then if they turned green, it is terefah, but if they remained red, it is kosher. If one trod on a fowl or knocked it against the wall, or if an animal crushed it, then if it fluttered and remained alive for twenty-four hours, and one then slaughtered it, it is kosher.<br />
<br />
Art: Wallerant Vaillant - Young Sportsman with Rabbit and Fowl</span>

---

### content/chullin/57.txt
<a id="src-00353"></a>

**Source file:** `content/chullin/57.txt`

Chullin 57 – Non-Fatal Injuries in Birds
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEj433qYqQJc_vvUr_bn-M3KmJJmVjCjpGxDyq2Yy2K_fiNOVGgXSL1yetGj_QayaTOLf_EsE2Ce_tv54pq2FmsKY0BmaY0gZerrD-tkr3d42sErLYHZV7illB8jwD_UKTD58krHDGlm1ys/s1600/Alfred+Sisley+-+Still-Life%253A+Heron+with+Spread+Wings.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="249" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEj433qYqQJc_vvUr_bn-M3KmJJmVjCjpGxDyq2Yy2K_fiNOVGgXSL1yetGj_QayaTOLf_EsE2Ce_tv54pq2FmsKY0BmaY0gZerrD-tkr3d42sErLYHZV7illB8jwD_UKTD58krHDGlm1ys/s320/Alfred+Sisley+-+Still-Life%253A+Heron+with+Spread+Wings.jpg" width="320" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Birds have less vitality than animals, as evidenced by the fact that only one of the two pipes – either the trachea or the esophagus – need to be cut for the bird to be considered slaughtered. Because of this we might have thought that injuries similar to <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2011/08/chullin-54-non-fatal-injuries.html">those of animals</a> would be fatal in birds. Therefore, we need the rules for birds that are kosher despite being injured, and here they are.<br />
<br />
If the trachea was split lengthwise, and not cut across; if a weasel struck (bit) it on its head in a place that does not make it terefah; if its crop was punctured, and Rabbi Yehudah the Prince says that even if it was removed; if its intestines came out but were not punctured; if its wings were broken, if its legs were broken, or if its feathers were plucked – in all of these cases the bird remains kosher. Rabbi Yehudah says that if its down (small, downy feathers without long shafts that cover the bird's skin) were removed, it is terefah.<br />
<br />
Art: Alfred Sisley - Still-Life: Heron with Spread Wings</span>

---

### content/chullin/58.txt
<a id="src-00354"></a>

**Source file:** `content/chullin/58.txt`

Chullin 58 – Can Terefah Live?
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEh9jU2-ZOgI6RXv1odybfx-4fauYCZVEK_VSPQWPcBZtYXhH5tZjS0eh4uy14VDCUYLtpWbaUE8qiBmmqlnaQEL6gXmYOV5tdRW_va2PxMcJHu_opcysKc8A2saNApArfhZGrQ1-T-bQNA/s1600/Frans+Hals+-+Boy+With+A+Skull.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEh9jU2-ZOgI6RXv1odybfx-4fauYCZVEK_VSPQWPcBZtYXhH5tZjS0eh4uy14VDCUYLtpWbaUE8qiBmmqlnaQEL6gXmYOV5tdRW_va2PxMcJHu_opcysKc8A2saNApArfhZGrQ1-T-bQNA/s320/Frans+Hals+-+Boy+With+A+Skull.jpg" width="274" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">There was a man in Einbul whose skull was missing a piece as large as a drill hole, but they fashioned for him a piece of dried gourd shell and he lived. Rabbi Shimon ben Elazar said, “That's no proof! It occurred in the summertime, but once the cold season came upon him, he died” – because in Rabbi Shimon's view a terefah cannot survive for more than a year. The final law is that once an animal survived for twelve months, it is not a terefah. Also, if it is a female and gave birth, it is not a terefah.<br />
<br />
No worm can survive for more than twelve months. Therefore, dates stored in a container for that long are permitted to be eaten, since earth-produced worms disappeared, and new worms are not forbidden until they emerge from the fruit. <br />
<br />
Incidentally, gnats don't live for more than a day. Then what about a popular saying, “For seven years the female gnat kept aloof from the male gnat, because she said to him, 'You saw a fat inhabitant of Mechozah who went swimming in the water and you sucked blood without telling me!'” – They are talking in gnat-years.<br />
<br />
Art: Frans Hals - Boy With A Skull</span>

---

### content/chullin/59.txt
<a id="src-00355"></a>

**Source file:** `content/chullin/59.txt`

Chullin 59 – Which Animals Are Kosher?
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiFw61WKBBFe7Jh8GVuo9TzXhEcQmG4wDe5uCmHy9DPBwOFRCdaoGOxTLk5d1-AXf2l50dMhAbcCI5aTFSptMcX-DPRALzLjzctTGNV9d0X__FeL587q3A5sT8-X5zACu47lH9DBi6x5JU/s1600/Winslow+Homer+-+Fallen+Deer.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="223" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiFw61WKBBFe7Jh8GVuo9TzXhEcQmG4wDe5uCmHy9DPBwOFRCdaoGOxTLk5d1-AXf2l50dMhAbcCI5aTFSptMcX-DPRALzLjzctTGNV9d0X__FeL587q3A5sT8-X5zACu47lH9DBi6x5JU/s320/Winslow+Homer+-+Fallen+Deer.jpg" width="320" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">If an animal inhaled smoke, was overcome by cold, or ate animal poison – all of which are dangerous to animals but not to humans – it is kosher. If it ate human poison or if it was bit by a snake, it is still kosher, but it is prohibited to eat it because of a potential danger to human life.<br />
<br />
Once a deer had its hind legs severed. Rav inspected it and, because the cut was below the sinews of the knee, pronounced it kosher. He wanted to taste it lightly roasted, but Shmuel said to him, “Perhaps a snake bit it before the leg was severed. Put it in the oven to check.” The meat was indeed poisoned and fell apart. Shmuel applied to Rav the words of Solomon, “No harm shall befall a righteous,” and Rav applied to Shmuel the words of Daniel, “No secret is withheld from you.”<br />
<br />
The signs of a kosher domestic and of a kosher wild animal are listed in the Torah: it should have hooves that are completely split into two, and it should be a ruminant that brings up its cud. <br />
<br />
Art: Winslow Homer - Fallen Deer</span>

---

### content/chullin/6.txt
<a id="src-00356"></a>

**Source file:** `content/chullin/6.txt`

Chullin 6 – Truly Righteous Do Not Accidentally Eat Forbidden Foods
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjVH6nHTm4kdjbt5i0DwkMwVg4VbW4pTtXYonSELbHR2vb42jm_RcxRuTSYC-WM_CZIVxgw2kL64eTLwl48FAzsGkVBtZEMA2KNGU4w2wa2fbr26FdXvQmrb2UFhV98UgNV8oC6d79tYVc/s1600/Antoine+Vollon+-+Still+Life+with+a+Pen%252C+Jug%252C+Bottle+and+Eggs+on+a+Table.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="259" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjVH6nHTm4kdjbt5i0DwkMwVg4VbW4pTtXYonSELbHR2vb42jm_RcxRuTSYC-WM_CZIVxgw2kL64eTLwl48FAzsGkVBtZEMA2KNGU4w2wa2fbr26FdXvQmrb2UFhV98UgNV8oC6d79tYVc/s320/Antoine+Vollon+-+Still+Life+with+a+Pen%252C+Jug%252C+Bottle+and+Eggs+on+a+Table.jpg" width="320" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Once Rabbi Shimon ben Elazar was sent by Rabbi Meir to bring wine from some Cutheans (Samaritans). On his way, a certain elder (some say, prophet Elijah) told him, “<a href="http://bible.cc/proverbs/23-2.htm">Put a knife to your jaw, if you are man of spirit</a>.” Upon hearing this, Rabbi Meir declared the wine of Cutheans prohibited, because some Cutheans were discovered to be idol worshipers, and to Rabbi Meir even a minor probability of transgression was significant.<br />
<br />
Later, Rabbi Yochanan drank their wine. Did he not hear about Rabbi Meir's decree, or did he not agree to it? Based on the rule that the righteous do not accidentally eat forbidden foods, we can deduce that he knew about it, but did not agree to it.<br />
<br />
Rabbi Zeira and Rav Assi  were served roasted eggs mixed with wine, and Rabbi Zeira did not eat them, because he suspected that tithes were not separated from the wine. However, seeing that Rav Assi ate the food, he reasoned that the righteous do not accidentally eat forbidden food, searched the stores of his knowledge and found that one should not worry about doubtful tithes when they are served in a mixture.<br />
<br />
Art: Antoine Vollon - Still Life with a Pen, Jug, Bottle and Eggs on a Table<br />
</span>

---

### content/chullin/60.txt
<a id="src-00357"></a>

**Source file:** `content/chullin/60.txt`

Chullin 60 – God and His Creations
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjm9jxruJNIhNrsrPDZnUuDob0N9EKTfvv4bFu5QtMTaDYkZvOaCFtUP6n_ThCHYbRgBFszKyykqa2Ztag0HlukQGV8NKw5Yj_M3bB85hCXGebDLe-7QUHx9vfPrDTmbI4dDzA0Ij2NEcs/s1600/Edward+Stott+-+The+High+Grasses.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="242" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjm9jxruJNIhNrsrPDZnUuDob0N9EKTfvv4bFu5QtMTaDYkZvOaCFtUP6n_ThCHYbRgBFszKyykqa2Ztag0HlukQGV8NKw5Yj_M3bB85hCXGebDLe-7QUHx9vfPrDTmbI4dDzA0Ij2NEcs/s320/Edward+Stott+-+The+High+Grasses.jpg" width="320" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">When the grasses heard God <a href="http://bible.ort.org/books/pentd2.asp?ACTION=displaypage&amp;BOOK=1&amp;CHAPTER=1#P11">tell the trees to grow separately, each according to its species</a>, they reasoned logically and said, “If the trees, who are naturally separated, are nevertheless commanded about not mixing, then we who have a tendency to become mixed, should certainly observe separation!” This prompted the Minister of the World (the angel into whose hands the entire world has been given) to say the following phrase from the psalms, “May the glory of God endure forever, may God rejoice in his works!”<br />
<br />
Ravina asked a related question, “If someone planted two types of grasses together, is that a forbidden mixture?” Perhaps not, since they were not commanded to grow separately, or maybe yes, since they guessed it on their own?<br />
<br />
Rav Assi asked a question: “<a href="http://bible.ort.org/books/pentd2.asp?ACTION=displaypage&amp;BOOK=1&amp;CHAPTER=1#P12">The earth brought forth vegetation on Tuesday</a>, but <a href="http://bible.ort.org/books/pentd2.asp?ACTION=displaypage&amp;BOOK=1&amp;CHAPTER=2#P36">the plants were not there on Friday</a>. That's a contradiction!” He answered, “All vegetation remained underground until Adam prayed for it.” Rav Nachman bar Pappa had a garden. He planted seeds there, but they did not grow. He prayed, the rain came, and they grew. He said, “That is the teaching of Rav Assi!”<br />
<br />
Art: Edward Stott - The High Grasses<br />
</span>

---

### content/chullin/61.txt
<a id="src-00358"></a>

**Source file:** `content/chullin/61.txt`

Chullin 61 – The Signs of Kosher Birds
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjJGuJrhP0JzUHGhQ2zRI8qq17iY7qzPwPhMfLM8rw4Q3JfeHRm2SB9Nt9ijWXQ4x8pmSR8Gptsh0AtshkBgMX83AlhnRizFJBzSqtWu9doSVFZhaorKv3MR8t5aAq-c4hy35TmM26BZT0/s1600/Joseph+Crawhall+-+The+Aviary.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjJGuJrhP0JzUHGhQ2zRI8qq17iY7qzPwPhMfLM8rw4Q3JfeHRm2SB9Nt9ijWXQ4x8pmSR8Gptsh0AtshkBgMX83AlhnRizFJBzSqtWu9doSVFZhaorKv3MR8t5aAq-c4hy35TmM26BZT0/s320/Joseph+Crawhall+-+The+Aviary.jpg" width="219" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">The signs of kosher birds were not stated in the Torah. Instead, the Torah lists twenty-four types of birds that are not kosher, with the implication that all others are kosher. The Sages, however, said, “Any bird that claws is nonkosher, but any bird that has an added toe, has a crop, and whose gizzard can be peeled, is kosher.” Rabbi Elazar the son of Rabbi Tzadok saiys, “Any bird that part the toes of its feet when placed on a twig, so as to grab it better, is nonkosher.”<br />
<br />
Thus, there should be thousands of bird types that are kosher. However, later, and perhaps already in the times of writing down the Talmud, that is, around sixth century, the people became less knowledgeable in the names of the birds, with the result that they no longer knew with certainly which birds are nonkosher. The signs above, given by the Sages, also cannot be ascertained with ease. The result of this is that only those few birds that are known by tradition to be kosher can be eaten, while the rest cannot.<br />
<br />
Art: Joseph Crawhall - The Aviary</span>

---

### content/chullin/62.txt
<a id="src-00359"></a>

**Source file:** `content/chullin/62.txt`

Chullin 62 – Identifying Kosher Birds
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg2rhew_Kum3hcUbekYiMAfFbIK_j5CW-Eg8wZ8APp9vm0nhw51v1z_ZZaEvYJC4mM8p6A-QpK12tUBXSW9Byl_YKqbo-lv4FEQ1Gj0uAdHP8j3hdk4gIYyljuspntEWNZHEiPVzVn6a9U/s1600/Herbert+William+Weekes+-+The+Sermon+-+A+Raven+Addressing+a+Gaggle+of+Geese.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="250" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg2rhew_Kum3hcUbekYiMAfFbIK_j5CW-Eg8wZ8APp9vm0nhw51v1z_ZZaEvYJC4mM8p6A-QpK12tUBXSW9Byl_YKqbo-lv4FEQ1Gj0uAdHP8j3hdk4gIYyljuspntEWNZHEiPVzVn6a9U/s320/Herbert+William+Weekes+-+The+Sermon+-+A+Raven+Addressing+a+Gaggle+of+Geese.jpg" width="320" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">The Torah lists twenty-four types of non-kosher fowl, and all other birds are kosher. The exact identification of the species' names, and the translations of the Hebrews terms are subject to many disagreements, with the <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2011/08/chullin-61-signs-of-kosher-birds.html">practical result that only a few birds are known to be kosher</a>.<br />
<br />
However, we can formulate some logical rules, even if we don't know the exact physical birds they refer to. Twenty of the non-kosher birds possess all three kosher signs, that is, extra toe, crop, and gizzard that can be peeled – but they claw their prey. The raven has two of the kosher signs. The ossifrage and the osprey have one kosher sign, a different one each. An eagle has no kosher signs. To determine if a bird is kosher it is first compared to the eagle. If it is unlike an eagle and has at least one kosher sign, and it does not belong to the other twenty-three non-kosher types, then it is kosher.<br />
<br />
Ameimar formulated a rule: even if one is not expert in identifying an ossifrage and an osprey – which are rare – if he sees a bird with one kosher sign, it is kosher, provided that it does not claw. <br />
<br />
Art: Herbert William Weekes - The Sermon - A Raven Addressing a Gaggle of Geese</span>

---

### content/chullin/63.txt
<a id="src-00360"></a>

**Source file:** `content/chullin/63.txt`

Chullin 63 – The Names of the Birds
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhHVJ6AaUm6akTc33s3nSbu0GnQt9prVk5OMoeUqse_pIaFnYK6H5K1TjlX1l8qB9JYSkRpM3TI6i0aNYpqHvSC5synk18GfWu3wy49k-z7UOhcN1jmRZW8F8MZ89_l9WQVfXjIjNuOPYc/s1600/Wladyslaw+Aleksander+Malecki+-+Storks%2527+Seym.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="247" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhHVJ6AaUm6akTc33s3nSbu0GnQt9prVk5OMoeUqse_pIaFnYK6H5K1TjlX1l8qB9JYSkRpM3TI6i0aNYpqHvSC5synk18GfWu3wy49k-z7UOhcN1jmRZW8F8MZ89_l9WQVfXjIjNuOPYc/s320/Wladyslaw+Aleksander+Malecki+-+Storks%2527+Seym.jpg" width="320" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Rav Yehudah said, “The cormorant ('shalach') is the bird who draws fish from the sea.” Its name is related to “sholeach” – draw or send. Rabbi Yochanan, when observing this bird, would exclaim, “Your judgments are in the great deep” – because the fish that is destined to perish at that time is captured by the cormorant in the depth. When observing an ant, he would say, “Your righteousness is like the mighty mountains.” This phrase from the psalms means that God provides for the tiniest ant. Alternatively, it emphasizes that an ant can carry a burden much larger than itself.<br />
<br />
The stork in Hebrew is “racham,” which connotes mercy – because it is a harbinger of rain. Rav Bibi bar Abaye said, “That is only when it sits on something makes the 'sherakrak' sound. If it sits on the ground and shrieks, it is a sign that Messiah is about to come.” But there was one stork that settled in a plowed field and shrieked, and a stone came down and cracked its skull?! – That one was a liar. <br />
<br />
Art: Wladyslaw Aleksander Malecki - Storks' Seym<br />
</span>

---

### content/chullin/64.txt
<a id="src-00361"></a>

**Source file:** `content/chullin/64.txt`

Chullin 64 – The Eggs
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiAwL3F1GafoQy_5CHRLGSINv8lpiBBM01exIAHMIZTkrHS3pQG5sHnClrMfBn942OBN224W6V2K5NWVOr_-43rbykcVO9iIHtacc9CQa_Gn5PVo2rXpF4geA4E7OhhtOLGg_uHEe-uHmA/s1600/Willem+Roelofs+-+Still+life+with+eggs.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="206" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiAwL3F1GafoQy_5CHRLGSINv8lpiBBM01exIAHMIZTkrHS3pQG5sHnClrMfBn942OBN224W6V2K5NWVOr_-43rbykcVO9iIHtacc9CQa_Gn5PVo2rXpF4geA4E7OhhtOLGg_uHEe-uHmA/s320/Willem+Roelofs+-+Still+life+with+eggs.jpg" width="320" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">If an idolater sells eggs, one can buy them and not be concerned that they come from birds that are <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2011/07/terefah-and-nevelah-two-categories-of.html">nevelah or terefah</a>. But let's be concerned that they come from a non-kosher bird altogether! – We are dealing with the case where he says which kosher bird they come from, and in additional they have the kosher signs. What are these signs? They are spherical and rounded, though not a perfect sphere, with one of its ends rounded and one tapered. Then why can't we rely on these signs alone? – Because there are crow's eggs that look kosher.<br />
<br />
If an egg has a spot of blood in it, then if it is only in the place of the embryo, one can discard the blood and eat the egg, but if it is in another place, then one can assume the whole egg started developing, and it is forbidden. Some say that the place of an embryo is in the connection to the yolk, others that it is in the yolk, and still others that it is in the  egg white. The custom has thus become to discard an egg with any blood spot.<br />
<br />
Art: Willem Roelofs - Still life with eggs</span>

---

### content/chullin/65.txt
<a id="src-00362"></a>

**Source file:** `content/chullin/65.txt`

Chullin 65 – Grasshoppers
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;">
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgzgn7Msm6XvbjrD5gDwiqjDG2Bo6yqh5fAZHe7Woluc2om1iWzTmqFQPNAK2jXkb9sZaTa1QVOADlBoJ8bvB8e8UqGvu5sxDdPZO0N_Jq49ZdYX8SYafh7h5xFTVpZf1a3j3VMrwI52vI/s1600/Balthasar+Van+Der+Ast+-+Carnations%252C+a+parrot+tulip%252C+a+grasshopper+and+a+lizard+on+a+ledge.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="198" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgzgn7Msm6XvbjrD5gDwiqjDG2Bo6yqh5fAZHe7Woluc2om1iWzTmqFQPNAK2jXkb9sZaTa1QVOADlBoJ8bvB8e8UqGvu5sxDdPZO0N_Jq49ZdYX8SYafh7h5xFTVpZf1a3j3VMrwI52vI/s320/Balthasar+Van+Der+Ast+-+Carnations%252C+a+parrot+tulip%252C+a+grasshopper+and+a+lizard+on+a+ledge.jpg" width="320" /></a></div>
<span style="font-size: medium;">If a bird flocks with other kosher birds, it is kosher , and if with non-kosher type, then it is non-kosher – this is the opinion of Rabbi Eliezer. However, the Sages say that this is only true if it also resembles them. If “according to its type” is not written in the Torah with the regard to this non-kosher type, then all agree that the bird that flocks with this non-kosher type may still be kosher.<br />
<br />
To be kosher, a grasshopper must have the following signs: four walking legs, four wings, two jumping legs, and its wings must cover the its greater part. Rabbi Yose says, “Its name must be 'chagav', or grasshopper.”<br />
<br />
The school of Rabbi Ishmael derives, from the additional words in the Torah, that grasshoppers with a bold head, with an elongated head, and with a tail are also kosher.<br />
<br />
Art: Balthasar Van Der Ast - Carnations, a parrot tulip, a grasshopper and a lizard on a ledge</span>

---

### content/chullin/66.txt
<a id="src-00363"></a>

**Source file:** `content/chullin/66.txt`

Chullin 66 – Kosher Fish
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjVxZf2qgCGF6mcV9VlmLUaKUvFwnpzbvPygzbLP4nlvwhzsWS9k-Zb-AM6iKCLVRkQwIjHKEG1crcd0yNju7zabxzOz5szdyOc5L_YjWGOZvqm_ws9a5jg9hQ_5amOC98fShPJnz2F9tk/s1600/Alexander+Adriaenssen+-+The+Fishmonger.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="250" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjVxZf2qgCGF6mcV9VlmLUaKUvFwnpzbvPygzbLP4nlvwhzsWS9k-Zb-AM6iKCLVRkQwIjHKEG1crcd0yNju7zabxzOz5szdyOc5L_YjWGOZvqm_ws9a5jg9hQ_5amOC98fShPJnz2F9tk/s320/Alexander+Adriaenssen+-+The+Fishmonger.jpg" width="320" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Any fish that has a fin and a scale is kosher. If it does not have fins and scales when young, but will develop them later, like sardines, it is also kosher. If it has them when in the water but sheds them when caught, like tuna, it is kosher.<br />
<br />
Any fish that has a scale certainly has a fin. If so, why did the Torah list both? – To make it abundantly clear for those who don't know the Torah that well. Furthermore, the Torah said “<a href="http://bible.ort.org/books/pentd2.asp?ACTION=displaypage&amp;BOOK=3&amp;CHAPTER=11#P3004">Those that have fins and scales in the seas and rivers you may eat, and those that don't have the fins and scales in the seas and rivers you may not eat</a>.” Why is this repetition? – To make one who eats fish without fins and scales transgress both a positive and a negative commandment.<br />
<br />
Since the Torah only mentioned the requirement of fins and scales for seas and rivers, those worm-like creatures that originate in a vessels are permitted – as long as they have not left the vessel. A practical application is that one may drink water and not worry about worms in it, since they are kosher anyway.<br />
<br />
Art: Alexander Adriaenssen - The Fishmonger</span>

---

### content/chullin/67.txt
<a id="src-00364"></a>

**Source file:** `content/chullin/67.txt`

Chullin 67 – Worms in Beer
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjwMbOg_DPywNNROkWZs7xju__cnlHkqzy2AJfK7DyVv7PyW-M2_ozfuxOUZBbxp2BYNOX1L6GBQlNPVr1rZaUDD5L6g4XJlxk91YfPZGSdc76dUnlt08pv_7rT8WCim6ky8Zp2t4A5yRg/s1600/William+Huggins+-+The+Diet+of+Worms.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjwMbOg_DPywNNROkWZs7xju__cnlHkqzy2AJfK7DyVv7PyW-M2_ozfuxOUZBbxp2BYNOX1L6GBQlNPVr1rZaUDD5L6g4XJlxk91YfPZGSdc76dUnlt08pv_7rT8WCim6ky8Zp2t4A5yRg/s320/William+Huggins+-+The+Diet+of+Worms.jpg" width="237" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Worms that germinate in vessels or cisterns <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2011/08/chullin-66-kosher-fish.html">are permitted to be eaten</a>, since the requirement of fins and scales applies only to creatures originating in seas and rivers. This permit equally applies to other beverages. <br />
<br />
Ran Huna said the rule: one should not pour beer through a sifter of wood chips at night, because a worm may part from the beer and crawl upon a chip momentarily. When it does, it becomes a creature that creeps upon the ground, and one would transgress a prohibition if he eats it while drinking the beer. But if so, let us suspect that the worm departed from the beer and adhered to the wall of the vessel and then fell back!? – That would not be a problem. The interior wall of the vessel is considered the worm's natural habitat, and the worm is not considered parted from the vessel.<br />
<br />
Similarly, worms that germinate in detached fruit are permitted, until they emerge and crawl on the ground. Rav Yosef inquired, if a worm germinated in a detached fruit and died upon contact with the ground, or only part of the worm emerged, or if one swallowed it in mid-air? – Unresolved.<br />
<br />
Art: William Huggins - The Diet of Worms</span>

---

### content/chullin/68.txt
<a id="src-00365"></a>

**Source file:** `content/chullin/68.txt`

Chullin 68 – The Meat in the Field
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiGt41R9FOTbPziCHFwmjvADDZllEJA504wIghCOP2Q42OkL9VFMyxfT8PJ5I21S9McvuAuZF3LWUczdQzB2owbDsE40U98Z_mMsjkCyH3aMQorhhtCLGUPeETNlxwZXHJ7cKco36vkdao/s1600/Jean-Francois+Millet+-+Peasants+Bringing+Home+a+Calf+Born+in+the+Fields.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="259" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiGt41R9FOTbPziCHFwmjvADDZllEJA504wIghCOP2Q42OkL9VFMyxfT8PJ5I21S9McvuAuZF3LWUczdQzB2owbDsE40U98Z_mMsjkCyH3aMQorhhtCLGUPeETNlxwZXHJ7cKco36vkdao/s320/Jean-Francois+Millet+-+Peasants+Bringing+Home+a+Calf+Born+in+the+Fields.jpg" width="320" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">If one slaughters a pregnant animal, the fetus is considered to have been slaughtered together with its mother, and it does not require a shechitah of its own. Of course, it has to be killed before being eaten, but that killing can be done in any possible way. In fact, if two such animals grow up and have an offspring, this offspring does not require shechitah either.<br />
<br />
If an animal was in difficult labor and the fetus put forth its foreleg and then drew it back, the fetus can be eaten without shechitah, as above, except for the foreleg. However, if it put forth its head and then drew it back, it is considered to have been born, and it will require its own shechitah.<br />
<br />
The foreleg that was put forth is prohibited because <a href="http://bible.ort.org/books/pentd2.asp?ACTION=displaypage&amp;BOOK=2&amp;CHAPTER=22#P2142">of the phrase</a> “and meat in the field, <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2011/07/terefah-and-nevelah-two-categories-of.html">terefah</a>, you will not eat.” The words “in the field” are extra, since a predator can attack anywhere, and it teaches an additional lesson: once meat has gone outside of its bounds (its mother's womb), it becomes forbidden. The Talmud started this topic because of its connection to the laws of terefah discussed earlier.<br />
<br />
Art: Jean-Francois Millet - Peasants Bringing Home a Calf Born in the Fields</span>

---

### content/chullin/69.txt
<a id="src-00366"></a>

**Source file:** `content/chullin/69.txt`

Chullin 69 – Can a Limb be Born?
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEi1wGHVa1ZIXlSobLrVWu9i36QJTUb2_ZlFDZbCdlT1vwks7yFeZyKhWG55Ol2PUKDtv-zLA2S8ZcEZsiYxocNhCcPGg1Y_EiUe6Ck1GQlH7cwsbXFswnDpbrTq3al5OJgOv3fGcRpSoBY/s1600/Rosa+Bonheur+-+Doe+And+Fawn+In+A+Thicket.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEi1wGHVa1ZIXlSobLrVWu9i36QJTUb2_ZlFDZbCdlT1vwks7yFeZyKhWG55Ol2PUKDtv-zLA2S8ZcEZsiYxocNhCcPGg1Y_EiUe6Ck1GQlH7cwsbXFswnDpbrTq3al5OJgOv3fGcRpSoBY/s320/Rosa+Bonheur+-+Doe+And+Fawn+In+A+Thicket.jpg" width="273" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Rav said that once a fetus puts forth its foreleg, then even if it draws it back, the limb becomes prohibited. However, Rabbi Yochanan disagrees. What is the root of their disagreement? Rav says that once the limb is out of its mother's womb, it is considered to have been born. If the complete fetus is subsequently born, then its shechitah will permit the limb to be eaten. But if its mother is slaughtered, then the fetus is permitted, but the limb is forever forbidden.<br />
<br />
Sometimes, when an animal was in difficult labor, they would cut off a piece of the fetus, to ease the pain of the animal. Since there is a necessity for this measure, it is not prohibited as cruelty to animals. If he leaves the limb inside the womb and later slaughters the mother, this limb (and the whole fetus) is permitted to be eaten. The Torah said, “<a href="http://bible.ort.org/books/pentd2.asp?ACTION=displaypage&amp;BOOK=3&amp;CHAPTER=11#P2998">Any that has a split hoof and chews its cud – among the animals</a>...” &nbsp;“Among the animals” (ba behemah) can be understood as “within an animal” – and this serves as the source for the law about a fetus.<br />
<br />
Art: Rosa Bonheur - Doe And Fawn In A Thicket</span>

---

### content/chullin/7.txt
<a id="src-00367"></a>

**Source file:** `content/chullin/7.txt`

Chullin 7 – Even the Animals of the Righteous Do Not Eat Forbidden Foods
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgLHXSeb2dZWHC1lKEwnfoOKf82e-bR4_4-gZa6DZDS5JM0EWNPPxpYEQ-1FcfWsCv3sd99tKR9e-KXS8oO3rka6aX_mgQiYwJEVP95Zgt0pMlrc8x5mOidkCqcfA4oxxP23nJMBG6DzwY/s1600/Willem+Maris+-+A+Herdboy+With+Donkeys+On+Scheveningen+Beach.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="213" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgLHXSeb2dZWHC1lKEwnfoOKf82e-bR4_4-gZa6DZDS5JM0EWNPPxpYEQ-1FcfWsCv3sd99tKR9e-KXS8oO3rka6aX_mgQiYwJEVP95Zgt0pMlrc8x5mOidkCqcfA4oxxP23nJMBG6DzwY/s320/Willem+Maris+-+A+Herdboy+With+Donkeys+On+Scheveningen+Beach.jpg" width="320" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;"><a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2011/07/chullin-6-truly-righteous-do-not.html">Previously we saw a few cases</a> of practical applications of the rule that truly righteous do not accidentally eat forbidden foods. This rule itself is based on the same rule about their animals.<br />
<br />
Rabbi Pinchas ben Yair was on his way to redeem captives – which is one of the most important commandments – when he encountered the river Ginai. He said to the river, “Ginai, split your waters, so that I may cross through you.” The river answered, “You are trying to do the will of your Maker, but you may or may not succeed, while I will certainly accomplish the will of my Maker and continue to flow.” Rabbi Pinchas said, “If you do not split, I decree that water shall never flow again through you,” at which the river split. <br />
<br />
There was a man with Rabbi Pinchas, bringing flour for matzah. “Split also for him!” - commanded Rabbi Pinchas, and the river obeyed. There also was an Arab merchant with them, and Rabbi Pinchas made the river split for him yet again.<br />
<br />
When Rabbi Pinchas arrived at an inn, they poured barley for his donkey, but it refused to eat. They sifted and then cleaned the barley, but it still did not eat. “Perhaps you bought it from a source that cannot be trusted to separate the tithes,” - suggested Rabbi Pinchas - “The poor creature is going to perform the will of its Maker, so it should not be given forbidden foods.” Then the donkey ate.<br />
<br />
But, when one buys grain for an animal, he needs not tithe it? - True, if he buys it initially for the animal. In this case, however, they bought it for the needs of Rabbi Pinchas, who was known to never accept presents, and thus the exemption from tithing did not apply.<br />
<br />
Art: Willem Maris - A Herdboy With Donkeys On Scheveningen Beach</span>

---

### content/chullin/70.txt
<a id="src-00368"></a>

**Source file:** `content/chullin/70.txt`

Chullin 70 – Difficult Labor for a Firstborn
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg4uGkcuqOyKhSB6uC4gGH2cHmh66LYuvvMKcKXoRpifU5DjROcKwy7_2nbVJQfQT3DFU36DNFKaVtV6Z_S9i46d2Nvk3XZO-nvLpBPy-YxO3vmpxfye5YB1cC5ND6bbvhQYgNKVTootSA/s1600/Eug%25C3%25A8ne+Verboeckhoven+-+A+Sheep+And+Two+Lambs+Resting+In+A+Summer+Landscape.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="256" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg4uGkcuqOyKhSB6uC4gGH2cHmh66LYuvvMKcKXoRpifU5DjROcKwy7_2nbVJQfQT3DFU36DNFKaVtV6Z_S9i46d2Nvk3XZO-nvLpBPy-YxO3vmpxfye5YB1cC5ND6bbvhQYgNKVTootSA/s320/Eug%25C3%25A8ne+Verboeckhoven+-+A+Sheep+And+Two+Lambs+Resting+In+A+Summer+Landscape.jpg" width="320" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Any male firstborn lamb, kid or calf is automatically sanctified as a firstborn at birth. If the labor is normal, the firstborn is given to the priests, who later on brings it as a sacrifice. The animal is not worked, and even if it becomes blemished, its meat is not sold in the market. If an animal delivering its first young child is in difficult labor and one has to cut off pieces to save the mother, one may cut each limb as it emerges and throw it to the dogs. If the majority of the fetus emerged and it then died, it must be buried, and its mother is now exempt from the law of firstborn.<br />
<br />
If an animal's fetus died inside the womb and the shepherd extended his hand into the womb and touched it, the shepherd does not become impure with corpse-impurity. This is derived through logic: if its mother permits the fetus to be eaten, by her slaughter, then certainly it can purify from corpse-impurity. The law for non-kosher animals that are not slaughtered for food should be the same. Rabbi Yose HaGlili disagrees in the case of a non-kosher animal.<br />
<br />
Art: Eugène Verboeckhoven - A Sheep And Two Lambs Resting In A Summer Landscape</span>

---

### content/chullin/71.txt
<a id="src-00369"></a>

**Source file:** `content/chullin/71.txt`

Chullin 71 – Swallowed Impurity
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiP3_iENJoDecLHqbnza9hpjLzoew6N_kUxufhg2pV40X9cfQCuDZl_KGTDO3cdQ-jpelF0e9g8bQ2Hp_L3gJ5jAY14G-23GdpjMkV9R85TEJRRUOW2bcZ99-_KzVj4Nv8RRf3syFHv43I/s1600/G.+Horning+Jensen+-+Turning+the+clay+in+the+pottery.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="270" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiP3_iENJoDecLHqbnza9hpjLzoew6N_kUxufhg2pV40X9cfQCuDZl_KGTDO3cdQ-jpelF0e9g8bQ2Hp_L3gJ5jAY14G-23GdpjMkV9R85TEJRRUOW2bcZ99-_KzVj4Nv8RRf3syFHv43I/s320/G.+Horning+Jensen+-+Turning+the+clay+in+the+pottery.jpg" width="320" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">If a woman's fetus died inside her womb, and the midwife extended her hand into the womb and touched it, the midwife is impure for seven days with corpse-impurity, but the woman is pure until the fetus emerges from her womb.<br />
<br />
The operative principle here is that of “swallowed-up,” or absorbed impurity, which does not transmit impurity to anything else. It is derived from the following phrase in the Torah, “<a href="http://bible.ort.org/books/pentd2.asp?ACTION=displaypage&amp;BOOK=3&amp;CHAPTER=11#P3035">And one who eats of the dead animal carcass shall immerse himself</a>...” and become pure after sunset. This instruction includes even the case when he swallowed the meat just prior to sunset, and then immersed himself, so that the impure meat has not yet been digested – and he is nevertheless pure, which proves our principle.<br />
<br />
Rabbah said that the same is true for a swallowed-up pure object: it does not become impure. What's the proof? Compare the human to a clay vessel, which protects from the impurity from outside. The power of  a human is even stronger, since it protects from the swallowed-up impurity.<br />
<br />
What about swallowing an impurity via the rectum? Its protection must be even stronger, since the rectum leads to digestion.<br />
<br />
Art: G. Horning Jensen - Turning the clay in the pottery</span>

---

### content/chullin/72.txt
<a id="src-00370"></a>

**Source file:** `content/chullin/72.txt`

Chullin 72 – Kosher Slaughter Makes the Meat Ritually Pure
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"></div><div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiL093Y9OATLH6V2jfxIEHIr3LOCtAp_pKi3G_eYfZpiVGB4EeLu8tY99nXEi1pV9FF8yCARD4JDiRj-gnOGdsxySJUt_WIAuZbYV40M4UfK-Zq6e5a7pvOuq9BXOVpI6ua9Rk2ZtDcwm0/s1600/Frans+Snyders+-+The+market+game.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiL093Y9OATLH6V2jfxIEHIr3LOCtAp_pKi3G_eYfZpiVGB4EeLu8tY99nXEi1pV9FF8yCARD4JDiRj-gnOGdsxySJUt_WIAuZbYV40M4UfK-Zq6e5a7pvOuq9BXOVpI6ua9Rk2ZtDcwm0/s320/Frans+Snyders+-+The+market+game.jpg" width="280" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">If an animal was in difficult labor and the fetus put forth its foreleg, and one severed it, to ease the mother's pain and then, since it did not help, slaughtered the mother, the remaining flesh of the fetus is ritually pure, since it has been slaughtered together with its mother. The severed limb itself is impure: if the fetus was alive, the limb was severed from a live animal and has the impurity of a dead animal (<a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2011/07/terefah-and-nevelah-two-categories-of.html">nevelah</a>); and if the fetus was dead, the limb is actual nevelah.<br />
<br />
If one first slaughtered its mother and then severed the foreleg, then the flesh of the fetus is impure because it touched the limb – so says Rabbi Meir. However, the Sages say that flesh is impure with a special light impurity decreed by the Sages, which would only make a difference in the case of sacrifices.<br />
<br />
All agree that kosher slaughter makes the meat ritually pure. Why? Logically, one could even argue that should be impure, like non-kosher animals. However, since a kosher animal was fit for food when it was young, its slaughter purifies the meat even if it later became a <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2011/07/terefah-and-nevelah-two-categories-of.html">terefah</a> (sick), whereas non-kosher ones were never fit.<br />
<br />
Art: Frans Snyders : The market game</span>

---

### content/chullin/73.txt
<a id="src-00371"></a>

**Source file:** `content/chullin/73.txt`

Chullin 73 – A Dangling Limb
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg7rTPuN0bbNfuMD9KCmTx8vaEgv_wCB-7Q3qSXeptp0E2oAtao4gc-JmBsfkFlpGTuarub8tZs29ISGu8TUch3hky_1KWbMH5OK9Hz2PTRsJC3mlpRIrbdt3ePN3y-kg8WXEOHhrsiyvQ/s1600/William+Huggins+-+Rams+and+Ewes+in+a+Landscape.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="256" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg7rTPuN0bbNfuMD9KCmTx8vaEgv_wCB-7Q3qSXeptp0E2oAtao4gc-JmBsfkFlpGTuarub8tZs29ISGu8TUch3hky_1KWbMH5OK9Hz2PTRsJC3mlpRIrbdt3ePN3y-kg8WXEOHhrsiyvQ/s320/William+Huggins+-+Rams+and+Ewes+in+a+Landscape.jpg" width="320" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">A dangling limb is a limb that is somewhat detached from the body of an animal and is connected to it by a strip of flesh. If the limb can heal, then it is treated as part of the animal and is rendered permissible by the animal's kosher slaughter. However, if it cannot heal, then we have the following disagreement.<br />
<br />
Resh Lakish says that the dangling limb is similar to a limb of a fetus protruding from its mother's womb, and it is subject to the <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2011/09/chullin-72-kosher-slaughter-makes-meat.html">disagreement between Rabbi Meir and the Sages</a>. Rabbi Yochanan says that in the case of a dangling limb there is no disagreement, but rather it is considered attached to the body of the animal, and shechitah makes it permitted for consumption and free from impurity – except that the Sages later forbade to eat it.  By contrast, if the animal with a dangling limb dies by itself, the limb is considered to have been detached before death, and its impurity is less than of a nevelah. How so? A piece of meat separated from a torn limb is pure, while a piece of meat separated from an animal that died by itself is impure.<br />
<br />
Art: William Huggins - Rams and Ewes in a Landscape</span>

---

### content/chullin/74.txt
<a id="src-00372"></a>

Chullin 74 – Calf of a Slaughtered Cow
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEimOGvQXNu1e1hjhS1uqPwi0dkcDxdKz3wQYszpXfmCB3w-WCG9H1_CpXq2OIFEK9tuDBjAMVD6cVUdVxxt-WrB_aF3BAL1730ZGNnaGH2ATgcJnT7s2UE1-BZHVOQsAKOsJeZ9j3gWHkQ/s1600/Pieter+Aertsen+-+The+Cook.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEimOGvQXNu1e1hjhS1uqPwi0dkcDxdKz3wQYszpXfmCB3w-WCG9H1_CpXq2OIFEK9tuDBjAMVD6cVUdVxxt-WrB_aF3BAL1730ZGNnaGH2ATgcJnT7s2UE1-BZHVOQsAKOsJeZ9j3gWHkQ/s320/Pieter+Aertsen+-+The+Cook.jpg" width="157" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">If one slaughters a cow pregnant with an eight-month calf, alive or dead, or a dead nine-month calf, it may be killed and eaten without shechitah, even after it grows up. This rule is the subject of the last few pages, but the Talmud first discusses the exceptions to it, and now quotes the rule itself. It is also restated to introduce the dissenting opinion of Rabbi Meir.<br />
<br />
If the nine-month fetus was alive, then it is an independent animal and requires shechitah; additionally, it cannot be killed today, on the same day as its mother – these are the words of Rabbi Meir, but the Sages disagree. For animals other than cows the law is the same, only the gestation term is adjusted accordingly. <br />
<br />
A firstborn donkey cannot be used by its owner, until he redeems it with a lamb or a young goat, which he gives to a priest. Can the calf of a slaughtered cow be used for this redemption? Is it considered an independent animal, and then it could be used for redemption, or since it does not need a shechitah, is it considered like meat in a pot, and then it can't be used for redemption?<br />
<br />
<br />
Art: Pieter Aertsen - The Cook</span>

---

Chullin 75 – Calf of a Slaughtered Cow: Disagreements and Final Law
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiyNVax_xtQ_MbxMfaA-nXkZ8by61uEpD2jUrpbesKRihyphenhyphenvWhTNLOtor4fvdJmkT0W8O6FpBU9xf-CIl9v9RqNUFhYOIRypd1xmWh_H4j-9GRaEzwmLDrZsceIEiRY96Ok1LIiehM-UbW8/s1600/Adrien+Moreau+-+Plowing+The+Fields.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="214" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiyNVax_xtQ_MbxMfaA-nXkZ8by61uEpD2jUrpbesKRihyphenhyphenvWhTNLOtor4fvdJmkT0W8O6FpBU9xf-CIl9v9RqNUFhYOIRypd1xmWh_H4j-9GRaEzwmLDrZsceIEiRY96Ok1LIiehM-UbW8/s320/Adrien+Moreau+-+Plowing+The+Fields.jpg" width="320" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Rabbi Yochanan and Resh Lakish further disagree about the calf of the slaughtered pregnant cow. If its mother became ritually impure, is the calf considered part of her, with the same impurity as her, or is it an independent being simply touching her, which results in less impurity? Further, that fat which normally goes on the Altar and is thus prohibited for consumption in the case of other animals, is it considered permitted  meat in the case of the calf, since all of it is permitted?<br />
<br />
Rabbi Shimon Shezuri made a statement: the calf of a slaughtered cow, even when it is five years old and is plowing in the field, is still permitted through the shechitah of its mother and may be killed in any way and eaten. But we've been saying this all along!? – Actually, the Sages have prohibited this as soon its feet touch the ground, and have put the requirement of  a regular shechitah back, because otherwise people watching it may decide that shechitah is never required. Rabbi Shimon Shezuri says that the Sages made no such decree.<br />
<br />
Art: Adrien Moreau - Plowing The Fields</span>

---

**Source file:** `content/chullin/76.txt`

Chullin 76 – Injuries to the Hind Leg
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg5zLFy1Tm1addw4j0piRICR1a3v2A3RMIYvwUjS-gptJQEoAlqILBgw0Ch9cHBEszIPoZy2-W_W3ax1SE1CGplIcHODG2sU_OGO6P_lupNxKC1tl2RytUYPDFQfrPYBjE9HuwGvcqLUfU/s1600/George+Cochran+Lamdin+-+The+Little+White+Heifer.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg5zLFy1Tm1addw4j0piRICR1a3v2A3RMIYvwUjS-gptJQEoAlqILBgw0Ch9cHBEszIPoZy2-W_W3ax1SE1CGplIcHODG2sU_OGO6P_lupNxKC1tl2RytUYPDFQfrPYBjE9HuwGvcqLUfU/s320/George+Cochran+Lamdin+-+The+Little+White+Heifer.jpg" width="252" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">If an animal's hind leg was severed below the joint, it is still fit for consumption, but if it was severed above the joint, then it is unfit, because it has been rendered <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2011/07/terefah-and-nevelah-two-categories-of.html">terefah</a>. The animal's hind leg has two joins, so which one are we talking about? There are different opinions on that, and also different reported versions of these opinions.<br />
<br />
A “junction of sinews” are the three sinews that attach the middle leg muscles to the bone of the lower leg. If they are removed, the animal becomes a terefah.<br />
<br />
If a bone was fractured and the broken ends pierced the skin, the animal remains kosher, but the limb itself is in question. If the greater part of the flesh remains, the shechitah of the animal makes the limb fit for consumption, but if not, then this is a dangling limb, and it is forbidden for consumption.<br />
<br />
Art: George Cochran Lamdin - The Little White Heifer</span>

---
