<a id="src-00375"></a>

**Source file:** `content/chullin/77.txt`

Chullin 77 – Amniotic Sac
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEi61wKamo74yiXOFBdFImgpGCDnU-rXv4A8eNggIYhhgjc__QbByaPiPT7qUCZXvTDb3RqmeUEKQ7iSu1Rfg-h35wnNlDkXXAmVppYjA6Qh-wfwcunn3FynbZ_zCMXaj0DrQG8T4u3MCjk/s1600/Charles+%25C3%2589mile+Jacque+-++A+Flock+Of+Sheep+In+A+Barn.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="255" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEi61wKamo74yiXOFBdFImgpGCDnU-rXv4A8eNggIYhhgjc__QbByaPiPT7qUCZXvTDb3RqmeUEKQ7iSu1Rfg-h35wnNlDkXXAmVppYjA6Qh-wfwcunn3FynbZ_zCMXaj0DrQG8T4u3MCjk/s320/Charles+%25C3%2589mile+Jacque+-++A+Flock+Of+Sheep+In+A+Barn.jpg" width="320" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">If one slaughters an animal and finds inside an amniotic sac, one he is not squeamish can eat it, because the Torah permitted it with the phrase “<a href="http://bible.ort.org/books/pentd2.asp?ACTION=displaypage&amp;BOOK=5&amp;CHAPTER=14#P5291">Every animal (even an amniotic sac)... you may eat</a>.” However, it is not really food, and therefore it does not carry the ritual impurity of foods. When one planned to eat it, this thought elevates it to the status of food, and now it can carry ritual impurity. <br />
<br />
If an amniotic sac partially emerged from the womb before the the animal was slaughtered, the complete sac is prohibited for consumption even after the animal was slaughtered. There is a suspicion that the partially emerged part contained the head of the fetus, which would make it legally born, and then the shechitah of the mother would not make the sac permissible.<br />
<br />
If an animal carrying its first miscarried an amniotic sac, it may or may not have been a male firstborn, and even if it was a male, it may have been deformed, therefore it can thrown to the dogs. However, if the mother was a sacrifice, the sac needs to be buried -- because both male and female young would be sanctified.<br />
<br />
Art: Charles Émile Jacque -  A Flock Of Sheep In A Barn<br />
</span>

---

### content/chullin/78.txt
<a id="src-00376"></a>

**Source file:** `content/chullin/78.txt`

Chullin 78 – It and Its Offspring
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiVJN8QW-0orbxIADEckgDLOQyT72hkGAqE9Pp4CU8LEisqMVx0MYhMY80ksJYiKNZ4eFvgEKMGlgLiztwO-UdEZQmy_w5M0oWR4rzGAbLVx1I3BA0c5mrVyKDWeDCuAlkbeAftEqVBsIk/s1600/Eug%25C3%25A8ne+Verboeckhoven+-+Shepherd+Girl+With+Cattle+And+Sheep+At+Rest.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="217" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiVJN8QW-0orbxIADEckgDLOQyT72hkGAqE9Pp4CU8LEisqMVx0MYhMY80ksJYiKNZ4eFvgEKMGlgLiztwO-UdEZQmy_w5M0oWR4rzGAbLVx1I3BA0c5mrVyKDWeDCuAlkbeAftEqVBsIk/s320/Eug%25C3%25A8ne+Verboeckhoven+-+Shepherd+Girl+With+Cattle+And+Sheep+At+Rest.jpg" width="320" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">The Torah said, “<a href="http://bible.ort.org/books/pentd2.asp?ACTION=displaypage&amp;BOOK=3&amp;CHAPTER=22#P3395">Whether it is a bull, a sheep or a goat, do not slaughter [a female animal] and its child on the same day</a>.” This prohibition is true both in the Land of Israel and outside, in the time of the Temple and now, for ordinary animals and for sacrifices.<br />
<br />
For example, if one slaughtered an animal and its offspring, both regular animals, outside the Temple, and both are now fit for consumption, then for the second slaughter he is liable like for any other negative commandment of the Torah. However, if both the parent and the offspring were sacrifices and he slaughtered both outside the Temple Courtyard, then for the first slaughter he is liable because he did it outside the Temple, and may be cut off from the people, but the second animal is now unfit for slaughter on the same day, and thus the slaughterer is not liable for slaughtering it outside. He is liable for "it and its offspring" slaughter though.<br />
<br />
Two different people can slaughter the two animals, and the second one – that one who does the action now forbidden – only he is liable.<br />
<br />
Art: Eugène Verboeckhoven - Shepherd Girl With Cattle And Sheep At Rest</span>

---

### content/chullin/79.txt
<a id="src-00377"></a>

**Source file:** `content/chullin/79.txt`

Chullin 79 – Does “It and its offspring” Apply to Males?
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiwo-MvvVq_J34s20stSigT3rait8c4K4VWzC_XqoJMgF6Yof0Qw1j85QfijLepffBL31Y21Q0zBKf1s6Amkp6eccIycNJn15iO7ZWn4fIhE5wmFrkFKY9zPz3A79iujFapte2OeSrqvM8/s1600/Martin+Johnson+Heade+-+Two+Hummingbirds+At+A+Nest.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="247" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiwo-MvvVq_J34s20stSigT3rait8c4K4VWzC_XqoJMgF6Yof0Qw1j85QfijLepffBL31Y21Q0zBKf1s6Amkp6eccIycNJn15iO7ZWn4fIhE5wmFrkFKY9zPz3A79iujFapte2OeSrqvM8/s320/Martin+Johnson+Heade+-+Two+Hummingbirds+At+A+Nest.jpg" width="320" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">The prohibition to slaughter an animal and its offspring on the same day applies to female animals and their offspring, but not to male parents – these are the words of the Sages, but Chananyah says that it applies equally to both. <br />
<br />
The Sages compare the situation to that of a mother bird hovering over her young in the nest, where the mother bird is mentioned specifically and must be sent away. Chananyah says that you can't compare the two: sending away the mother bird does not apply to a nest that you own, whereas “it and its offspring” applies even to stray animals that are not yours. <br />
<br />
Actually, the Sages agree to Chananyah in this, however, they say that “it” means only one parent, and now by analogy with the bird it must be the mother! And Chananyah, what does he have to say now? He answers that “it" means the father, and “its offspring” implies the mother.<br />
<br />
Practically, if the father is known with certainty, then it should not be slaughtered on the same day as its offspring, even though one does not violate a definite Torah prohibition.<br />
<br />
Art: Martin Johnson Heade - Two Hummingbirds At A Nest</span>

---

### content/chullin/8.txt
<a id="src-00378"></a>

**Source file:** `content/chullin/8.txt`

Chullin 8 – Hot Knife
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhcMezIoVI_ytsLaK76RhDEjtmI7vUx-Saw2A7T1B1LF8SOHNwRAhDmclHbzTko9TtlT3RWqUH32JnuRYNM-StGiX37-JzmDRT80hVSH32b7WbeL9xUX57jsy0NUIxleiZLuhXChwfnY6E/s1600/Francis+Wheatley+-+Knives%252C+Scissors+and+Razors+to+Grind.jpeg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhcMezIoVI_ytsLaK76RhDEjtmI7vUx-Saw2A7T1B1LF8SOHNwRAhDmclHbzTko9TtlT3RWqUH32JnuRYNM-StGiX37-JzmDRT80hVSH32b7WbeL9xUX57jsy0NUIxleiZLuhXChwfnY6E/s320/Francis+Wheatley+-+Knives%252C+Scissors+and+Razors+to+Grind.jpeg" width="245" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Rabbi Zeira said in the name of Shmuel, “If someone made a knife white-hot and slaughtered with it, his slaughter is valid, since the knife first cuts and then later burns, and thus the shechitah happens because of the sharpness of the knife, not because of its heat.” <br />
<br />
One is allowed to slaughter with the knife of idolatry, because he damages the animal by killing it, and does not derive benefit, but he is not allowed to cut the meat with this knife, because this improves it.<br />
<br />
However, the forbidden fat collected on the knife of idolatry surely makes the meat non-kosher!? Rav agrees and says that one must peel away some meat at the place of incision, and Rabbah bar bar Channah says that one needs only wash the meat. What is the argument? Rav considers the place of the incision hot enough to absorb the forbidden fat. Alternatively, both consider it hot, but Rabbah says that the pipes are busy expelling the blood and do not absorb fat. Or perhaps both consider the place of incision cold, yet Rav says that it absorbs the forbidden fat because of the pressure exerted by the knife.<br />
<br />
Art: Francis Wheatley - Knives, Scissors and Razors to Grind</span>

---

### content/chullin/80.txt
<a id="src-00379"></a>

**Source file:** `content/chullin/80.txt`

Chullin 80 – The Product of a Deer and a Goat
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEh5nLdD9bsEYIzkhMtPlHTF_dz1TZjQD6Qj4MU0t5ZG9g5pxqcC06kMHF7RzxI_qfUD9vSCv0n5QeRuy4kRjewm1pMftN3Wx2U_7q22jpmLG4sVaQSFr9kaF52s8GCJmi8DSg7firKAYzM/s1600/Roelandt+Jacobsz+Savery+%253A+A+stag%252C+deers%252C+herons%252C+goats%252C+parrots+and+other+animals+in+a+forest.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="221" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEh5nLdD9bsEYIzkhMtPlHTF_dz1TZjQD6Qj4MU0t5ZG9g5pxqcC06kMHF7RzxI_qfUD9vSCv0n5QeRuy4kRjewm1pMftN3Wx2U_7q22jpmLG4sVaQSFr9kaF52s8GCJmi8DSg7firKAYzM/s320/Roelandt+Jacobsz+Savery+%253A+A+stag%252C+deers%252C+herons%252C+goats%252C+parrots+and+other+animals+in+a+forest.jpg" width="320" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">The product of crossbreeding between a deer and a goat is called a “koy”. Rabbi Eliezer and the Sages disagree about its laws, for example, in the case of a male deer that mated with a female goat, who then gave birth. The Sages hold that when the Torah mentions a goat, part-goat is also included, and Rabbi Eliezer maintains that it's not. Accordingly, the Sages say that the prohibition to slaughter an animal and its offspring on the same day applies to a koy, while Rabbi Eliezer says that it does not. <br />
<br />
When one slaughters a wild animal, one has to cover its blood with earth. A koy, being partly a wild animal, may require covering its blood – if we attach any importance to the father – or it may not. Accordingly, the Sages do not allow to slaughter a koy on a holiday, because we may dig the earth only for clear cases of blood covering, and not for doubtful ones.<br />
<br />
Some say that crossbreeding between a deer and a goat is impossible, and that the “koy” is perhaps a wild ram, or a separate species, not clearly wild or domestic.<br />
<br />
Art: Roelandt Jacobsz Savery : A stag, deers, herons, goats, parrots and other animals in a forest</span>

---

### content/chullin/81.txt
<a id="src-00380"></a>

**Source file:** `content/chullin/81.txt`

Chullin 81 – Unfit Slaughter Is No Slaughter At All!
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgRmt2s5QRpNJD59lSg8QrkXE6CjCBB6ny0BJssKIkZC9COV7CdN_PnBd5-HoPjo9BCw0ooBjwrTw9y0w9LzgwDUA04xisXVMbSMuuxRP3MUdy3ANR1GrOAxYdMd0VQIcUXroojp57uzeI/s1600/English+Provincial+School+-+The+Head+Of+A+Prize+Bull.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgRmt2s5QRpNJD59lSg8QrkXE6CjCBB6ny0BJssKIkZC9COV7CdN_PnBd5-HoPjo9BCw0ooBjwrTw9y0w9LzgwDUA04xisXVMbSMuuxRP3MUdy3ANR1GrOAxYdMd0VQIcUXroojp57uzeI/s320/English+Provincial+School+-+The+Head+Of+A+Prize+Bull.jpg" width="253" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">If the shechitah did not allow for the meat of the animal to be eaten, then Rabbi Shimon does not consider this act as shechitah. Therefore, if one made a shechitah but found that the animal was a <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2011/07/terefah-and-nevelah-two-categories-of.html">terefah</a> anyway, or if he slaughtered an idolatrous sacrifice, or a bull sentenced to be stoned for goring, a red heifer, or a calf designated to be decapitated to atone for a unresolved murder case, and then slaughtered its offspring, then according to Rabbi Shimon he is not liable for slaughtering an animal and its offspring on the same day.<br />
<br />
In fact, according to Rabbi Shimon, the prohibition of “it and its offspring” does not apply to sacrifices at all. Rav Hamnuna said, this is because after slaughter the meat is not ready to be eaten until its blood is thrown on the Altar, and thus it is not a shechitah. Rava said that this is because perhaps they will not throw the blood on the Altar. Then the warning they can give him becomes doubtful at best, and one is not liable for transgressing a law without a clear unequivocal warning immediately prior to the act.<br />
<br />
Art: English Provincial School - The Head Of A Prize Bull</span>

---

### content/chullin/82.txt
<a id="src-00381"></a>

**Source file:** `content/chullin/82.txt`

Chullin 82 – Permutations of Animal and its Offspring
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiL8aJDBvtvgeU3FuJueyh6UdN2Kic1ejfHBrx-DaZnPS5_RvbqBxNXB_M1jTxvVqJa7MMYayjDI964TqgElhBf8wncx1U04nNusm6QpuJoC3g6Hy1yljj_ir4u1GuhkGHVAyvZGGEtSOo/s1600/George+W.+Horlor+-+Calves+Feeding.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="248" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiL8aJDBvtvgeU3FuJueyh6UdN2Kic1ejfHBrx-DaZnPS5_RvbqBxNXB_M1jTxvVqJa7MMYayjDI964TqgElhBf8wncx1U04nNusm6QpuJoC3g6Hy1yljj_ir4u1GuhkGHVAyvZGGEtSOo/s320/George+W.+Horlor+-+Calves+Feeding.jpg" width="320" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">If two people bought a cow and its offspring from one person on one day, whoever bought first may slaughter first, and the other one <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2011/09/chullin-78-it-and-its-offspring.html">is enjoined from slaughtering on that day</a>. However, if the second buyer preceded the first and slaughtered his animal, he has gained the right to eat its meat, and is not penalized for this.<br />
<br />
If one slaughtered a cow and then slaughtered its two calves, he transgressed twice and is liable to two sets of lashes, but if he slaughtered the calves and then the mother, he transgressed only once. <br />
<br />
If one slaughtered a cow, its daughter and its daughter's daughter on one day, he transgressed twice, but if he first slaughtered a cow and its daughter's daughter's (for which he is not liable), and then slaughtered the daughter that day, he transgressed only once. However, Sumchos says that he transgressed twice here too: when he slaughtered the middle generation, he was doing two transgressions with one act, and it is Sumchos' opinion, for example, that for eating two portions of non-kosher food was is liable twice.<br />
<br />
Art: George W. Horlor - Calves Feeding</span>

---

### content/chullin/83.txt
<a id="src-00382"></a>

**Source file:** `content/chullin/83.txt`

Chullin 83 – How Long is “One Day” for Cow and its Offspring?
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjvP4-CpT6W9ehIe8e4BqtVzaNKpxMcww-kKxP_8pO1yFWNKb5xr4QTi1Ie7urKw9tJjD4ZknwOaZJz7EfqvAQ_ZzqCWPzZNajaiVulwdouMaQGGGlHjTsUr08emDKvtXsbORVRUHpjqnA/s1600/William+Hart+-+Sunset+With+Cows.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="226" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjvP4-CpT6W9ehIe8e4BqtVzaNKpxMcww-kKxP_8pO1yFWNKb5xr4QTi1Ie7urKw9tJjD4ZknwOaZJz7EfqvAQ_ZzqCWPzZNajaiVulwdouMaQGGGlHjTsUr08emDKvtXsbORVRUHpjqnA/s320/William+Hart+-+Sunset+With+Cows.jpg" width="320" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">On four days of the year it could be assumed that whoever is buying an animal intends to slaughter it immediately. Therefore, on the eve of these days a seller who sells an animal, if he already sold its parent or offspring today, is required to inform the buyer and say “I already sold its mother today.” The buyer then will not come to violate the prohibition to slaughter the animal and its offspring on one day. These four occasions are: last day of Succot (Simchat Torah), Passover, Shavuot, Rosh HaShanah, and in Galilee also Yom Kippur,  because there they prepared for Yom Kippur with lavish feasts.<br />
<br />
What is considered “one day” regarding the prohibition of “it and its offspring?” As Ben Zoma interpreted, “one day” is mentioned describing the creation of the world, and there it means “there was evening and there was morning, one day,” and “one day” is mentioned for the “cow and its offspring.” In both cases the day starts in the evening at sunset and continues on the next day till sunset.<br />
<br />
Art: William Hart - Sunset With Cows</span>

---

### content/chullin/84.txt
<a id="src-00383"></a>

**Source file:** `content/chullin/84.txt`

Chullin 84 – The Mitzvah to Cover the Blood
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhy5ZGa1JhawfgeF2GtYePtCorLHyqYKO9Q1xRTz-qPuGLzBNk347dx0KQam7Cu-wFbf16hKtLHWZrCXjG2kgw_sSLfxljeURBL-T6K5OM6-kxSofdPME2WQO31B7X72fusWx8q-KXdYno/s1600/Jan+Vermeer+Van+Delft+-+Young+Girl+in+an+Antique+Costume.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhy5ZGa1JhawfgeF2GtYePtCorLHyqYKO9Q1xRTz-qPuGLzBNk347dx0KQam7Cu-wFbf16hKtLHWZrCXjG2kgw_sSLfxljeURBL-T6K5OM6-kxSofdPME2WQO31B7X72fusWx8q-KXdYno/s320/Jan+Vermeer+Van+Delft+-+Young+Girl+in+an+Antique+Costume.jpg" width="267" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">The Torah said, “<a href="http://bible.ort.org/books/pentd2.asp?ACTION=displaypage&amp;BOOK=3&amp;CHAPTER=17#P3246">One... who traps a wild beast or a fowl and spills its blood by slaughtering it in a kosher way must cover its blood with earth</a>.” Thus the mitzvah of covering the blood applies in the Land of Israel and outside, in the time of the Temple and now; however it applies only to regular animals and not to sacrifices, and only to wild beasts and fowl, but not to domestic animals. <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2011/09/chullin-80-product-of-deer-and-goat.html">The “koy” animal is special</a>: one should not slaughter it on a festival, and if he did, he should not cover its blood, so as not to dig in the earth.<br />
<br />
Why did the Torah mentioned “trapping,” since fowl don't need to be trapped? To teach that one should eat meat only occasionally, as if he had to trap it each and every time. Additionally, <a href="http://bible.ort.org/books/pentd2.asp?ACTION=displaypage&amp;BOOK=5&amp;CHAPTER=12#P5255">one should only eat meat if he has a great desire for it</a>, has flocks, or is otherwise rich. Others should eat it only on Shabbat. However, later generations became weaker and should eat whatever is necessary to maintain their health.<br />
<br />
One should underspend on himself, be within means for his children, and overspend on his wife.<br />
<br />
Art: Jan Vermeer Van Delft - Young Girl in an Antique Costume</span>

---

### content/chullin/85.txt
<a id="src-00384"></a>

**Source file:** `content/chullin/85.txt`

Chullin 85 – Covering the Blood in Cases of Unfit Slaughter
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg4lnatfSmW-jIJz74R9r24Ay6p7-kCzw8HTqEi7mUBhHtKHE9BVYyv45PmpB94JdderQPaEzsqjzTtGP2jkLAGkDyKYW64s4UAWLSEfrNqiJ1niYX4Qm6-RR2uI6vJOZs3RIMyhoZcDZE/s1600/Winslow+Homer+-+The+Dinner+Horn.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg4lnatfSmW-jIJz74R9r24Ay6p7-kCzw8HTqEi7mUBhHtKHE9BVYyv45PmpB94JdderQPaEzsqjzTtGP2jkLAGkDyKYW64s4UAWLSEfrNqiJ1niYX4Qm6-RR2uI6vJOZs3RIMyhoZcDZE/s320/Winslow+Homer+-+The+Dinner+Horn.jpg" width="226" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Rav Eina gave an authoritative discourse and said that one who slaughters for a dangerously sick person on Shabbat should also cover the bird's blood. Rabbah was stupefied and said, “Even circumcision is allowed on Shabbat only for clear-cut cases, and not for doubtful ones, surely covering the blood should not be allowed!” But he was refuted from the laws of shofar blowing.<br />
<br />
If one slaughters a wild animal or a bird, but it is found to be <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2011/07/terefah-and-nevelah-two-categories-of.html">terefah</a>, then Rabbi Meir requires him to cover the blood, but the Sages exempt him. Why do the Sages exempt him? Because it is unfit slaughter, and it is not called slaughter at all. <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2011/09/chullin-81-unfit-slaughter-is-no.html">But this is Rabbi Shimon</a>! Then why is he called “Sages” here, but back then in discussing the laws of “it and its offspring” he is called Rabbi Shimon, and there Rabbi Meir is called the Sages? That is because Rabbi Yehudah the Prince, the compiler of the Mishnah, agreed with Rabbi Shimon here, but agreed with his opponent, Rabbi Meir, over there. By ascribing an opinion to “the Sages” Rabbi Yehudah was indicating what he thought the law should be.<br />
<br />
Art: Winslow Homer - The Dinner Horn</span>

---

### content/chullin/86.txt
<a id="src-00385"></a>

**Source file:** `content/chullin/86.txt`

Chullin 86 – Shechitah by a Deaf-mute, Deranged, or Minor
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjVNWyGyx7r3NQ1TRQ7o2DGEjc_w695KKG2ksTqIwwMQjrZ2PNSEc4NF1IRvT1WDu_K8Vt_Z5wNVysLtYN-hDYtqp0JWY8UQ_8op5ZhAeL_pGcPEX1Z3_fpqJM04Q-MeL3M0Dl07gFfwc8/s1600/John+William+Waterhouse+-+Windswept.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjVNWyGyx7r3NQ1TRQ7o2DGEjc_w695KKG2ksTqIwwMQjrZ2PNSEc4NF1IRvT1WDu_K8Vt_Z5wNVysLtYN-hDYtqp0JWY8UQ_8op5ZhAeL_pGcPEX1Z3_fpqJM04Q-MeL3M0Dl07gFfwc8/s320/John+William+Waterhouse+-+Windswept.jpg" width="219" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Rabbi Chiya's flax was attacked by moths, and Rabbi Yehudah the Prince told him to kill a bird in a way which would make it a <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2011/07/terefah-and-nevelah-two-categories-of.html">terefah</a>; the moths will smell the blood and abandon the flax. Why not kill it outright? – That would also work, but even making it a terefah would allow him not to cover its blood. <br />
<br />
But could it really happen? When Rabbi Chiya and his sons came to Israel, there ceased to be earthquakes and violent winds, the wine did not sour and the flax was not afflicted, since their merit protected everybody!? – Yes, it protected everybody but not them.<br />
<br />
If a deaf-mute, a deranged person, or a minor slaughtered a wild beast or a bird, with others observing them, <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2011/06/chulin-2-shechitah-or-ritual-slaughter.html">this is kosher</a>, but the observer is the one obligated to cover the blood. If nobody saw them, their shechitah is surely bungled, and one need not cover the blood. The same applies for “<a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2011/09/chullin-78-it-and-its-offspring.html">it and its offspring</a>,” - these are the words of Rabbi Meir, but the Sages disagree. Actually, the Sages disagree about covering the blood also, but they waited for Rabbi Meir to finish his words.<br />
<br />
Art: John William Waterhouse - Windswept<br />
</span>

---

### content/chullin/87.txt
<a id="src-00386"></a>

**Source file:** `content/chullin/87.txt`

Chullin 87 – Covering the Blood of Multiple Animals
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgy4sqt4Z3t1QTM5oWitRY7pFnP2OroZUcmqTBHRll0Oj4clPqnDTvbssh6zZ7A99aPttxVAWQb-ooUZ7otxKy4VDHIIvL96nxpj196GZMDcRBUzPw9ki_KyJ87h0G22czzrgWZ4pyZfk4/s1600/Camille+Pissarro+-+Strong+Winds%252C+Pontoise.jpg" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="265" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgy4sqt4Z3t1QTM5oWitRY7pFnP2OroZUcmqTBHRll0Oj4clPqnDTvbssh6zZ7A99aPttxVAWQb-ooUZ7otxKy4VDHIIvL96nxpj196GZMDcRBUzPw9ki_KyJ87h0G22czzrgWZ4pyZfk4/s320/Camille+Pissarro+-+Strong+Winds%252C+Pontoise.jpg" width="320" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">For multiple acts of slaughter, one needs to cover the blood only once - whether he slaughters a hundred wild animals, a hundred birds, or animals and birds. Rabbi Yehudah requires separate covering for an animal and a bird since the Torah said, "animal or bird."<br />
<br />
If one slaughtered an animal and did not cover its blood, and another person saw this, he is obligated to do blood covering. If one covered the blood, and it became uncovered, he does not have to cover it again. If the wind covered the blood with earth, one does not have to cover it, but if it became uncovered, one has to do blood covering.<br />
<br />
Once a man slaughtered an animal, but another person covered the blood first. Rabban Gamliel obligated the mitzvah thief to pay the slaughterer ten golden dinars (about $12,000). Was the penalty for the mitzvah or for the blessing connected to the mitzvah? Consider the following story. <br />
<br />
A Sadducee told Rabbi Yehudah the Prince, "The one who created the wind did not fashion the mountains,"  quoting Amos. Rabbi Yehudah said, "But the verse continues – it is God of Legions!" The Sadducee asked for three days to find an answer, during which time Rabbi Yehudah fasted and prayed to win the debate. When he was breaking the fast, a Roman arrived saying that the Sadducee did not find an answer and threw himself from a rooftop. Rabbi Yehudah invited the messenger to his meal, and at the end, asked him, "Do you want to hear the blessings after the meal or to take forty golden dinars (about $50,000)?" The Roman chose the blessings, and the Heavenly voice pronounced, "The four blessings after a meal are worth forty golden dinars." His family rose to prominence as a result, and we see that the penalty was for the blessing.<br />
<br />
Art: Camille Pissarro - Strong Winds, Pontoise<br />
</span>

---

### content/chullin/88.txt
<a id="src-00387"></a>

**Source file:** `content/chullin/88.txt`

Chullin 88 – Materials for Covering the Animal Blood
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjeugU4zj0ME7fExOAZ9cI6Vtkk1hJO6aeeRIhzdp65F0hBm56TSf93EoRkGW7ntDX4AbAWQAjGZ1sZaXaQQZsIoKr2mBiRF700fyFQ7_5Vlw9sp8Vy_FgfV_bJuORsv8wSneJpV7f-Hrs/s1600/Francisco+De+Zurbaran+-+Still-Life+with+Pottery+Jars.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="170" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjeugU4zj0ME7fExOAZ9cI6Vtkk1hJO6aeeRIhzdp65F0hBm56TSf93EoRkGW7ntDX4AbAWQAjGZ1sZaXaQQZsIoKr2mBiRF700fyFQ7_5Vlw9sp8Vy_FgfV_bJuORsv8wSneJpV7f-Hrs/s320/Francisco+De+Zurbaran+-+Still-Life+with+Pottery+Jars.jpg" width="320" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">If blood from animal slaughter became mixed with water and the amount of water is such that the mixture still looks like blood, one has to cover it. If blood mixed with red wine, then we look at wine as if it were water. If the corresponding amount of water in the mixture would not make it loose its appearance of blood, one still has to cover it. The same is true if it mixed with some other blood that does not require covering, such as blood of a domestic animal, but Rabbi Yehudah argues and says that blood cannot nullify other blood, and one always has to cover the mixture.<br />
<br />
Blood that splattered – the Sages say that it too has to be covered, but Rabbi Yehudah says that covering any part of it is enough. All derive their opinion from the words in the Torah “its blood” but interpret them differently.<br />
<br />
One may cover blood with fine sand or dung, lime or ground pottery, but not with course sand or dung, nor with uncrushed bricks. Rabban Shimon ben Gamliel stated a rule: “Blood can be covered with anything in which plans can grow.”<br />
<br />
Art: Francisco De Zurbaran - Still-Life with Pottery Jars<br />
</span>

---

### content/chullin/89.txt
<a id="src-00388"></a>

**Source file:** `content/chullin/89.txt`

Chullin 89 – Sciatic Nerve
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgyK-x7d6uY6m5aH7EO_lARjf90vdMK8U3PQUelCKbc6T6cwm_AD4F0bo6nn_f4AkLGAcgbrXh_XZkzjiTPczadESOsluPR_AIezs6-chwuBoeeXY1f5oJIP3K_iQPeYPLMa7qzsFH5Trw/s1600/Francois-Andre+Vincent+-+Job+Being+Scolded+by+his+Wife.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="265" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgyK-x7d6uY6m5aH7EO_lARjf90vdMK8U3PQUelCKbc6T6cwm_AD4F0bo6nn_f4AkLGAcgbrXh_XZkzjiTPczadESOsluPR_AIezs6-chwuBoeeXY1f5oJIP3K_iQPeYPLMa7qzsFH5Trw/s320/Francois-Andre+Vincent+-+Job+Being+Scolded+by+his+Wife.jpg" width="320" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">When the book of Job says that “God suspended the Earth on nothing,” it alludes to that one who remains silent in the time of provocation, literally, “without anything,” and in his merit God maintains the world.<br />
<br />
The sciatic sinew, “gid hanasheh,” is prohibited by the Torah on the account of the angel fighting with Jacob and striking him on the hip, dislocating his  thighbone. The Torah says, “<a href="http://bible.ort.org/books/pentd2.asp?ACTION=displaypage&amp;BOOK=1&amp;CHAPTER=32#P961">Therefore, the Children of Israel are not to eat the displaced sinew that is in the spoon of the thigh, to this day</a>.” The “spoon” is the rounded, spoon-like flesh around the top of the thighbone.<br />
<br />
The exact prohibition mentioned the sciatic sinew, and the commonly known sciatic nerve constitutes  part of it. The prohibition applies both in the Land of Israel and outside, when the Temple is standing and now, to both regular animals and sacrifices. It applies to domestics and wild animals but not to fowl, because they do not have spoon-shaped flesh on their thigh.<br />
<br />
Art: Francois-Andre Vincent - Job Being Scolded by his Wife</span>

---

### content/chullin/9.txt
<a id="src-00389"></a>

**Source file:** `content/chullin/9.txt`

Chullin 9 – Need to Validate Slaughter After It Is Done
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjLgiGivAVbky1dTfBvb8NE7HobiEsVzTbguZaCOQsXLYuDatqCVJkdjLMA3qf8DIurnwHQMifv0weul_uEtKQvLCGE8pN7A_ubv9uBSfpTifLSteIg3cnfQx5tZzuwsldYMR7ZhYPj5pM/s1600/Benjamin+Gerritsz.+Cuyp+-+The+Circumcision.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="235" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjLgiGivAVbky1dTfBvb8NE7HobiEsVzTbguZaCOQsXLYuDatqCVJkdjLMA3qf8DIurnwHQMifv0weul_uEtKQvLCGE8pN7A_ubv9uBSfpTifLSteIg3cnfQx5tZzuwsldYMR7ZhYPj5pM/s320/Benjamin+Gerritsz.+Cuyp+-+The+Circumcision.jpg" width="320" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">A Torah scholar must learn how to do three things which require effort and practice: signing his name as a judge or witness, slaughtering, and circumcision.<br />
<br />
If while slaughtering one paused, this invalidates the slaughter. How long is the pause? Enough to inspect the pipes, that is, the trachea and esophagus, to make sure that the majority of both pipes were cut and that the knife did not leave the area designated for slaughtering.<br />
<br />
After slaughtering, he must indeed inspect the pipes as explained above, and if he did not inspect them, the meat is forbidden to eat. Rabbi Eliezer ben Antignos said that it is forbidden as <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2011/07/terefah-and-nevelah-two-categories-of.html">terefah</a> (sick or incorrectly slaughtered animal), but others say that it is forbidden as <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2011/07/terefah-and-nevelah-two-categories-of.html">nevelah</a> (meat that was not slaughtered at all).<br />
<br />
What is the argument? Both agree to the principle of Rav Huna, “An animal during its lifetime is in a prohibited state, until it becomes known that it was slaughtered properly. Once it has been slaughtered, it is in a permitted state, unless we know that it became a terefah,” but they argue about how far to take its prohibited state.<br />
<br />
Art: Benjamin Gerritsz. Cuyp - The Circumcision</span>

---

### content/chullin/90.txt
<a id="src-00390"></a>

**Source file:** `content/chullin/90.txt`

Chullin 90 – Exaggerations and Hyperbole
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEirXaUg7zZZVwkQWH4Sqo3SPp6SO9Q8Dafz4uwA4yrFQYZlCGntQ41RVF3aQuCCrpM8GIzzNosWVewWcZWX0W0bXBuOHHRv9khwWpOrpm7N6SBdp3iEu-QBxEBQfic-u0WTQVz7rI76AHs/s1600/Thomas+George+Cooper+-+A+ewe+with+lambs+in+a+coastal+landscape.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="242" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEirXaUg7zZZVwkQWH4Sqo3SPp6SO9Q8Dafz4uwA4yrFQYZlCGntQ41RVF3aQuCCrpM8GIzzNosWVewWcZWX0W0bXBuOHHRv9khwWpOrpm7N6SBdp3iEu-QBxEBQfic-u0WTQVz7rI76AHs/s320/Thomas+George+Cooper+-+A+ewe+with+lambs+in+a+coastal+landscape.jpg" width="320" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Rabbi Chiya bar Yosef said, “The prohibition of sciatic sinew applies only to sacrifices that are eaten, but not, for example, to a burnt offering.” Rabbi Yochanan disagreed.<br />
<br />
Rav Pappa said that they don't really argue. Rabbi Chiya is talking about the the sinew not removed from the thigh, and then there is no prohibition to burn it, whereas Rabbi Yochanan is discussing a case where the sinew was already removed, and then it is prohibited to burn it.<br />
<br />
Rav Nachman bar Yitzhak said that they do disagree. According to Rabbi Yochanan, the complete thigh is brought to the Altar – because it would be unseemly to bring it cut – but then the sinew is removed and thrown onto the mound at the center of the Altar, which also contained ashes.<br />
<br />
At times, the mound had 300 kor (4,000 cubic feet) of ashes on it. Rava said, “That is an exaggeration.” Other examples of exaggerations, according to Rava, are that they gave a lamb to drink from a golden cup, or that 300 kohanim were needed to purify the Temple curtain in a mikva. The Torah itself uses hyperbole when it said, “<a href="http://bible.ort.org/books/pentd2.asp?ACTION=displaypage&amp;BOOK=5&amp;CHAPTER=1#P4918">large cities fortified to the heavens</a>.”<br />
<br />
Art: Thomas George Cooper - A ewe with lambs in a coastal landscape<br />
</span>

---

### content/chullin/91.txt
<a id="src-00391"></a>

**Source file:** `content/chullin/91.txt`

Chullin 91 – The Fight Between Jacob and Angel
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEihwLk68kQdbcrxS204uv9u01DHhFsJqQwnkKgqfDXicdVDREyh_DhYyTlKvtut-CT9ef-dl5n7DL5htysPiRvNxAHJlwuuPqsGTPaTGjVmkKX4arRMhYqlfQKJcQrUQm9so6nH3r1O7WU/s1600/Luca+Giordano+-+Jacob+Wrestling+With+The+Angel.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEihwLk68kQdbcrxS204uv9u01DHhFsJqQwnkKgqfDXicdVDREyh_DhYyTlKvtut-CT9ef-dl5n7DL5htysPiRvNxAHJlwuuPqsGTPaTGjVmkKX4arRMhYqlfQKJcQrUQm9so6nH3r1O7WU/s320/Luca+Giordano+-+Jacob+Wrestling+With+The+Angel.jpg" width="223" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">The prohibition of eating the sciatic sinew applies to the sinew of the right thigh and of the left thigh, but Rabbi Yehudah says that it applies to only one thigh, and logic dictates that it should be the right one. Is this the logic of the Torah or of the Sages? In other words, is Rabbi Yehudah certain that the Torah prohibited only the right sinew, or is he uncertain which one is prohibited, and so both are prohibited out of doubt?<br />
<br />
Consider the following rule: if one ate a portion of the right sinew and of the left one, then according to the Sages he incurs double punishment, eighty lashes, but Rabbi Yehudah gives him only one punishment. Now if Rabbi Yehudah is in doubt about which sinew it is, then the person eating it can only be given a doubtful warning, which is no warning at all! Must be then that Rabbi Yehudah is certain that only the right sinew is prohibited. Why the right one? <br />
<br />
One explanation is that the angel fighting with Jacob embraced him with his right hand and extended it to Jacob's right haunch and dislocated it. Another one – Jacob thought it was a non-Jew and positioned him to his right, to better protect himself. Yet another explanation, the angel looked like a Sage, and Jacob position himself to the left of the Sage, to show respect.<br />
<br />
Art: Luca Giordano - Jacob Wrestling With The Angel</span>

---

### content/chullin/92.txt
<a id="src-00392"></a>

**Source file:** `content/chullin/92.txt`

Chullin 92 – Why Did The Angel Need to Go?
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjhi8WuHLFhgbazLBDzPMXzYAGTi7ISVTzva2zvvlwD6d-nZWQCesxCYiqy9bO1PxjnA4X7O1SLh39Hz33sIACHfKji-sww58tiwy5KKBrqpGftkOlv0XYJ80aNv6sPlBT64HIkOJ03jro/s1600/Giorgio+da+Castelfranco+Veneto+%2528+Giorgione%2529+-+The+Singing+Lesson.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="273" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjhi8WuHLFhgbazLBDzPMXzYAGTi7ISVTzva2zvvlwD6d-nZWQCesxCYiqy9bO1PxjnA4X7O1SLh39Hz33sIACHfKji-sww58tiwy5KKBrqpGftkOlv0XYJ80aNv6sPlBT64HIkOJ03jro/s320/Giorgio+da+Castelfranco+Veneto+%2528+Giorgione%2529+-+The+Singing+Lesson.jpg" width="320" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">“<a href="http://bible.ort.org/books/pentd2.asp?ACTION=displaypage&amp;BOOK=1&amp;CHAPTER=32#P955">Let me leave!” said [the stranger]. “Dawn is breaking.</a>” “Are you thief or a kidnapper, who fears dawn?” – asked Jacob. “I am an angel, and since my creation my turn to sing a song to God has not arrived, till now, so I don't want to miss it,” – answered the angel. That is why Jacob then asked for a blessing.<br />
<br />
We see from here that some angels sing a song to God only once in a lifetime. Even those that do it daily can only sing their song after the prayers are said on earth. Moreover, angels mention the name of God only after three words, “Holy, holy, holy (is) God of Multitudes,” whereas people say “Listen, Israel, God... Is One,” mentioning the name of God after two words.<br />
<br />
Earlier we mentioned that the prohibition of sciatic sinew does not apply to fowl because they lack the spoon-shaped flesh over the thighbone. But we see that they do!? – Yes, there is a spoon, but it is not round. Rabbi Yirmiyah inquired, “What if some bird does have a round spoon-shaped flesh?” – Inquiry unresolved.<br />
<br />
Art: Giorgio da Castelfranco Veneto ( Giorgione) - The Singing Lesson</span>

---

### content/chullin/93.txt
<a id="src-00393"></a>

**Source file:** `content/chullin/93.txt`

Chullin 93 – Fat and Blood
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEig6VXBby55jh-bZ5Y70oBmvNXmQix6oe3QQeAExRt_F1xrFNjrdElrd4DHOKzRl8ZiSTuvvnLyn0B5PDEOAgXnUIBSWcjNI0GOrBdeqKswKrFGb__KvIf56W2L8nPT87gBAMCW8ZZii74/s1600/Esaias+Boursse+-+Interior+with+Woman+Cooking+.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="284" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEig6VXBby55jh-bZ5Y70oBmvNXmQix6oe3QQeAExRt_F1xrFNjrdElrd4DHOKzRl8ZiSTuvvnLyn0B5PDEOAgXnUIBSWcjNI0GOrBdeqKswKrFGb__KvIf56W2L8nPT87gBAMCW8ZZii74/s320/Esaias+Boursse+-+Interior+with+Woman+Cooking+.jpg" width="320" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Some of the animal fat is prohibited by the Torah, and some is similar to it and is prohibited by the Sages. For example, the Torah prohibited “<a href="http://bible.ort.org/books/pentd2.asp?ACTION=displaypage&amp;BOOK=3&amp;CHAPTER=3#P2780">the fat that is on the flanks</a>.” &nbsp;As a rule, that includes only fat that is visible when the animal is flayed, but the fat covered by the muscle is permitted. However, as Rav Yehudah taught in the name of Shmuel, the fat that is under the loins is prohibited. How could this be, if it is covered by the loins? – As Abaye explained, when an animal is alive, its limbs separate from one another, and at times that fat is uncovered.<br />
<br />
Rav Abba said, “The blood vessels in the foreleg are prohibited.” Rav Safra said to him, “Moses! Did the Merciful One say 'You shall not eat meat?'” Rava answered him, “Moses! Did the Merciful One say 'You may eat blood?'” Rather, if you are roasting the meat, the heat extracts the blood. However, if you are cooking the meat in a pot, you need to cut the vessels open first and salt them. Otherwise the prohibited blood gets reabsorbed into the meat.<br />
<br />
Art: Esaias Boursse - Interior with Woman Cooking </span>

---

### content/chullin/94.txt
<a id="src-00394"></a>

**Source file:** `content/chullin/94.txt`

Chullin 94 – One Should Be Honest in Thoughts and Actions
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgr1oXzKfr4YW0POCulGKyEd6KHxClzAk0S_iRq1gy2mNfEXP_fUkuDveRkwvTKuZ-4-jOzrQwN7npXjKwq0zUyav01Y_-1CIPjrdROd7uWP6hYmIEwtlUKNazw-4ApnK9n69BkFonVbDk/s1600/Francisco+De+Goya+y+Lucientes+-+A+Butcher%2527s+Counter.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="229" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgr1oXzKfr4YW0POCulGKyEd6KHxClzAk0S_iRq1gy2mNfEXP_fUkuDveRkwvTKuZ-4-jOzrQwN7npXjKwq0zUyav01Y_-1CIPjrdROd7uWP6hYmIEwtlUKNazw-4ApnK9n69BkFonVbDk/s320/Francisco+De+Goya+y+Lucientes+-+A+Butcher%2527s+Counter.jpg" width="320" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">A Jew may send a complete animal thigh to an idolater as a present, and not worry about removing the sciatic sinew. A non-Jew is allowed to eat it, and there is no danger that he will resell it to a Jew, since it is clear that it was not cut and the sinew was not removed.<br />
<br />
However, a cut-up thigh should not be sent, because a Jew might buy it. But how could a Jew buy presumably non-kosher meat from an idolater? – We are dealing with a place where the majority butchers were Jewish, and when a non-kosher slaughter (terefah) occurred, they announced it. Jews then would refrain from buying from a re-seller on that day.<br />
<br />
Another reason that a cut-up thigh may not be sent is that a Jew would then be deceiving an idolater, who would think that he got a super kosher piece of meat, and deceiving any person (literally, “stealing his mind”) is prohibited. One should not accustom himself to sleekness and enticement, and even one deceiving or misleading word is not allowed. <br />
<br />
Art: Francisco De Goya y Lucientes - A Butcher's Counter<br />
</span>

---

### content/chullin/95.txt
<a id="src-00395"></a>

**Source file:** `content/chullin/95.txt`

Chullin 95 – Meat Out From Sight
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"><a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjDtL-3fuTGP4P06u2bkKEwEwHMVDQMLJ7o-TrPsyg1jR5xm-ZwimhSpXM_0jSQ0fZI7MkP6TSeTKX6pgfB1wqFa0W08y6dchrsX0Yjc3AJm5NmubSS4MsDZyA75EZD-dgTco6WVIvBGaQ/s1600/Edward+Frederick+Brewtnall+-+The+three+ravens.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjDtL-3fuTGP4P06u2bkKEwEwHMVDQMLJ7o-TrPsyg1jR5xm-ZwimhSpXM_0jSQ0fZI7MkP6TSeTKX6pgfB1wqFa0W08y6dchrsX0Yjc3AJm5NmubSS4MsDZyA75EZD-dgTco6WVIvBGaQ/s320/Edward+Frederick+Brewtnall+-+The+three+ravens.jpg" width="193" /></a></div><span style="font-size: medium;">Rav said, “Once a piece of meat was out of sight, it is prohibited – perhaps a raven switched it  with a non-kosher piece.”<br />
<br />
But previously we learned that one is allowed to buy meat from non-Jewish resellers!? Rav will answer that perhaps the reseller never lost sight of the meat. Nevertheless, it was Rav's own stringency.<br />
<br />
Rav was once going to the house of his son-in-law and saw a ferry coming toward him. He said, “It is an omen that there will be a festival where I stay.” When everyone came to great him, he himself kept watching the meat. Then he said to the butchers, “If not for me, you would have fed prohibited meat to my family!”<br />
<br />
After all, Rav himself did not eat that meat. Not because it was not watched – for he watched it, and not because he used ferry for divination, but because it was a wedding of a daughter of a Sage to an unlearned man, and a Torah scholar like Rav is prohibited to eat at a feast that is not by itself a mitzvah.<br />
<br />
Art: Edward Frederick Brewtnall - The three ravens<br />
</span>

---

### content/chullin/96.txt
<a id="src-00396"></a>

**Source file:** `content/chullin/96.txt`

Chullin 96 – How Much of the Sciatic Sinew?
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;">
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEi1lmyOHO-GyHySsVyTUwErG5AgYk5sXprcDCAhe70c4g9euunPoZHCoUV_sqzM9p9x6wq-RM-3LCJnuVubjvQSkcHlvZC1CHd7EUpOmfZxRJJ0tlastM4tRaj7sOAKc_WNgfQMgXW4vms/s1600/Pietro+Longhi+-+Vendor+of+Roast+Meat.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEi1lmyOHO-GyHySsVyTUwErG5AgYk5sXprcDCAhe70c4g9euunPoZHCoUV_sqzM9p9x6wq-RM-3LCJnuVubjvQSkcHlvZC1CHd7EUpOmfZxRJJ0tlastM4tRaj7sOAKc_WNgfQMgXW4vms/s320/Pietro+Longhi+-+Vendor+of+Roast+Meat.jpg" width="237" /></a></div>
<span style="font-size: medium;">One who removes the sciatic sinew from the thigh meat must remove it entirely. He must dig deep into the thigh and extract it from wherever it is embedded in the meat. This is the presumed opinion of Rabbi Meir, because anonymous ruling are usually his. Rabbi Yehudah says that he needs only remove enough for the mitzvah, leveling it off the surface of the rounded flesh. Both agree that the Torah required only the removal of the external part of the sinew, but Rabbi Meir opines that the Sages extended this prohibition to within the thigh, and Rabbi Yehudah says that they did not enact any additional prohibitions.<br />
<br />
Bar Piyuli was excising a sciatic sinew from a piece of thigh meat, doing this in front of Shmuel, and he was cutting it flush at the surface. Shmuel said, “Cut deeper! Had I not seen you, you would have fed me something forbidden.” Bar Piyuli became frighntened, and the knife fell from his hand. “Do not be afraid,” – said Shmuel, – “for you did nothing wrong. The one who taught you did it according to Rabbi Yehudah, but the law follows Rabbi Meir.”
<br /><br />
Art: Pietro Longhi - Vendor of Roast Meat</span>

---

### content/chullin/97.txt
<a id="src-00397"></a>

**Source file:** `content/chullin/97.txt`

Chullin 97 – One-In-Sixty
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;">
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiwjEgxlHwgCbe_gYRxPjUKGkCYjmaeGMcL3j87jQk63KTX5pF8snRIPY6MuHOZ_tCaJtoHxHRU8cNGfFgS4O97CSWlyqSykcbBqFcmkKkwwHrlWNLg5N4-J96sQLes25RvTHwra5n9Tlo/s1600/Jozef+Israels+-+The+Frugal+Meal.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="204" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEiwjEgxlHwgCbe_gYRxPjUKGkCYjmaeGMcL3j87jQk63KTX5pF8snRIPY6MuHOZ_tCaJtoHxHRU8cNGfFgS4O97CSWlyqSykcbBqFcmkKkwwHrlWNLg5N4-J96sQLes25RvTHwra5n9Tlo/s320/Jozef+Israels+-+The+Frugal+Meal.jpg" width="320" /></a></div>
<span style="font-size: medium;">If one neglected to remove the sciatic sinew and cooked the thigh together with the sinew in it, then if the thigh is small enough, so that the sinew imparts a flavor to it, the complete thigh is forbidden to be eaten. However, how do we differentiate between the two meaty tastes? We imagine that the sinew is made of meat, and the meat is turnip, and estimate whether this amount of meat will impart taste to the turnip.
<br /> <br />
If a sciatic sinew was cooked with other, permitted sinews, and afterward one recognized the sciatic sinew and removed it, then the whole mixture is forbidden only if the forbidden sinew imparts its flavor to it. Later Sages estimated to be the volume of one-in-sixty. However, if one does not recognize the prohibited sinew, then the entire mixture of forbidden, because any piece might be the forbidden one. In any case the soup is prohibited if there is forbidden taste in it. The same law holds true if a slice of non-kosher meat or non-kosher fish was cooked together with kosher slices.
<br /><br />
Art: Jozef Israels - The Frugal Meal
</span>

---

### content/chullin/98.txt
<a id="src-00398"></a>

**Source file:** `content/chullin/98.txt`

Chullin 98 – It Wasn't Always One-In-Sixty
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;">
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjvxIkzoWT7ztl20xLCD998093uqI2_OxlOgFQc70UD9VIK7EBMOmi33qFMmy9YMMF5pqVSP6NINXAX2cooGNdfr_bVILCe-fyRtjctGXWGGqBrn_9M46MlVdl9sOHk9BXDG3aINy01eTw/s1600/Antoine+Vollon+-+Brass+Cooking+Vessel.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="223" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjvxIkzoWT7ztl20xLCD998093uqI2_OxlOgFQc70UD9VIK7EBMOmi33qFMmy9YMMF5pqVSP6NINXAX2cooGNdfr_bVILCe-fyRtjctGXWGGqBrn_9M46MlVdl9sOHk9BXDG3aINy01eTw/s320/Antoine+Vollon+-+Brass+Cooking+Vessel.jpg" width="320" /></a></div>
<span style="font-size: medium;">There was a case of a half an olive volume of prohibited fat that fell into a pot of meat. Mar bar Rav Ashi considered measuring the pot and nullifying the prohibited fat in the proportion of one-in-thirty. His father Rav Ashi told him, “You think that you can use the rule of treating the laws of the Sages leniently. Further, you think that half an olive volume is not even considered eating. However, that is wrong. Eating <a href="http://bible.ort.org/books/pentd2.asp?ACTION=displaypage&amp;BOOK=3&amp;CHAPTER=7#P2900">any amount of prohibited food is still prohibited by the Torah</a>, just that one does not get lashes for it, the taste of the prohibited food is considered as the food itself, and the correct proportion is always one-in-sixty.”
<br /><br />
Rabbi Chiya bar Abba said in the name of Bar Kappara that all prohibited substances nullify one-in-sixty, but Rav Assi said in the name of the same teachers that it is one-in-a-hundred. Both derived their opinion from the case of a <a href="http://bible.ort.org/books/pentd2.asp?ACTION=displaypage&amp;BOOK=4&amp;CHAPTER=6#P3840">cooked foreleg of a ram offering</a>, but one included the bones in the estimate, while the other one didn't.
<br /><br />
Art: Antoine Vollon - Brass Cooking Vessel
</span>

---

### content/chullin/99.txt
<a id="src-00399"></a>

**Source file:** `content/chullin/99.txt`

Chullin 99 – Why One-In-Sixty and not the Majority?
<div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;">
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEi4MfzUdyURw9_RrKJ6NVm7nW7a0Vh_hWELiZ_josn4COaclloj_N9YodfBPCWhNEumpzmDdwZLPldD9r5cPIiOi09LKsXeaux4L9syXkvL_tH6AKUOqAtmsAljzd1Zv9EVQXzmyvyXyAM/s1600/Cornelis+Jacobsz+Delff+-+Still-Life+of+Kitchen+Utensils.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="206" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEi4MfzUdyURw9_RrKJ6NVm7nW7a0Vh_hWELiZ_josn4COaclloj_N9YodfBPCWhNEumpzmDdwZLPldD9r5cPIiOi09LKsXeaux4L9syXkvL_tH6AKUOqAtmsAljzd1Zv9EVQXzmyvyXyAM/s320/Cornelis+Jacobsz+Delff+-+Still-Life+of+Kitchen+Utensils.jpg" width="320" /></a></div>
<span style="font-size: medium;">The Torah said, “<a href="http://bible.ort.org/books/pentd2.asp?ACTION=displaypage&amp;BOOK=2&amp;CHAPTER=23#P2144">You should follow the majority</a>.” Accordingly, any substance should be nullified in a majority, that is, if a forbidden piece became confused with two or more permitted pieces, and you cannot tell which piece is which, then the forbidden piece becomes nullified, and all three pieces are permitted. Why did we say then <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2011/10/chulin-97-it-wasnt-always-one-in-sixty.html">that a forbidden foreleg becomes nullified in the proportion of one-in-sixty</a>, and according to some, even one-in-hundred?
<br /><br />
The rule of the majority is only applicable to dry pieces that became intermingled. The cooking process, however, leads to mixing of all of the particles, and its law has a special stringency. Then let's derive all other cases from it and negate the law of majority!? – No, we cannot do this, because the law of a cooked foreleg is a novelty, and we don't derive general rules from novel cases.
<br /><br />
Still, the apparent discrepancy between the laws of dry and cooked foods leads some to believe that the whole law of one-in-sixty is only a Rabbinical stringency. What about the Torah phrase that seems to indicate otherwise? – It is only a hint that the Sages found for their law.
<br /><br />
Art: Cornelis Jacobsz Delff - Still-Life of Kitchen Utensils</span>

---

### content/eruvin/10.txt
<a id="src-00400"></a>

**Source file:** `content/eruvin/10.txt`

Eruvin 10 – Post
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEi7qJh8YmoR8wTyBEMaEppG_kYhCmB-uZPAmlVSbcREs4ui5iW4XSuRyIEQujuup4KGNj_OluxGXywiYROkAPain8wZn-H4h2CrKEYB6t9DYC8jyGea3uuC7o99-sQaYNGGkmR18ljIe-Wx/s1600/Jose+Benlliure+Y+Gil+-+Uncle+Jose.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEi7qJh8YmoR8wTyBEMaEppG_kYhCmB-uZPAmlVSbcREs4ui5iW4XSuRyIEQujuup4KGNj_OluxGXywiYROkAPain8wZn-H4h2CrKEYB6t9DYC8jyGea3uuC7o99-sQaYNGGkmR18ljIe-Wx/s320/Jose+Benlliure+Y+Gil+-+Uncle+Jose.jpg" width="268" /></a>Up until now we discussed one way of making carrying permitted in an alley – by placing a crossbeam over the top of its entrance. There is another way, however: a post. This post is placed next to the alley's exit, and it serves the same purpose: either it reminds the residents of alley's courtyards that the alley is different from the street, or it serves as the beginning of the fourth wall, separating the alley from the street.
<br />
<br />
Ordinarily, this post is places partially in the alley and partially in the street, so that it is visible both from the inside and outside the alley. However, what if one placed it completely outside the alley? The people inside then won't think that it is a reminder, for it looks to them as the continuation of the alley's wall. Still, does this post help, since at least it works for the people outside?
<br />
<br />
The Talmud finds a proof that it helps, then a disproof, and then concludes that it helps. How could it be – we just found a disproof!? – Since Rabbi Chiya was the one who offered a proof, and his explanations are based on the teaching of his uncle, Rabbi Yehudah the Prince, who wrote down all of the rules, then he is more trustworthy.
<br />
<br />
Art: Jose Benlliure Y Gil - Uncle Jose

### content/eruvin/11.txt
<a id="src-00407"></a>

**Source file:** `content/eruvin/11.txt`

Eruvin 11 – Shape of a door
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgRYX3Ka5oqWObgOpPzPYGxxCB4YsnJ5BH60TlGFf-3GQ_EEUTZT5oCJoPV36MZlxIVj67n_EepAjO5VrkIoktpXT96Hoe7R84ZQ71DOvP0dJhz1k4mASpB4ozHPfMf0APxJ4NH_csW0dEx/s1600/Otto+Piltz+-+A+young+Maid+in+a+Doorway.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgRYX3Ka5oqWObgOpPzPYGxxCB4YsnJ5BH60TlGFf-3GQ_EEUTZT5oCJoPV36MZlxIVj67n_EepAjO5VrkIoktpXT96Hoe7R84ZQ71DOvP0dJhz1k4mASpB4ozHPfMf0APxJ4NH_csW0dEx/s320/Otto+Piltz+-+A+young+Maid+in+a+Doorway.jpg" width="256" /></a>A shape of a door is constructed of two side posts and a bar or a rope across the top. Although it does not have practical utility, it helps for many laws. For example, an alley with an entrance wider than ten amot (20 feet) cannot be adjusted with a crossbeam on top of it, but the shape of a door here helps to permit carrying on Shabbat in such an alley. It also helps if the doors of the alley are too high for the crossbeam to be noticed.
<br />
<br />
A man from the valley of Beit Chortan took this idea to the extreme. He surrounded his field with the shapes of a door on all four sides as follows: he thrust four poles at the four corners on his field and stretched a vine across. His question now was, is that a valid separation? The matter came before the Sages, and they said that this indeed was a separation for planting. Normally, one should not plant wheat next to a vineyard. However, with the shape of a door serving as separation, it was allowed. Although the roots of the plants were next two each other and mixing, the shape of a door legally separated them into two distinct domains, and planting of wheat next the vineyard was allowed.
<br />
<br />
Resh Lakish said that just as the shape of a door was effective for planting, so too it worked for Shabbat, and the man was allowed to carry in his field. However, Rabbi Yochanan said that there was no comparison, and the laws of Shabbat were stricter. In discussing this, the Talmud considers many possibilities of how exactly his door shapes were constructed.
<br />
<br />
Art: Otto Piltz - A young Maid in a Doorway

---

### content/eruvin/12.txt
<a id="src-00408"></a>

**Source file:** `content/eruvin/12.txt`

Eruvin 12 – Crossbar and – or a post?
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEj5nzMK5PSAqHDIzVoRXOaOG-914BcRwZtq0PG5ORy8Z2ZOyjx5DFpWiLzC2YGPZ7st2yob7UPFX6n8L6qYGNJZ6cTPNlxT53bjxK_C7M3z-gSpZalpysTwFHyc9HXJMDumE5C9rfBfHyFc/s1600/John+Singer+Sargent+-+White+Walls+in+Sunlight+Morocco.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="241" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEj5nzMK5PSAqHDIzVoRXOaOG-914BcRwZtq0PG5ORy8Z2ZOyjx5DFpWiLzC2YGPZ7st2yob7UPFX6n8L6qYGNJZ6cTPNlxT53bjxK_C7M3z-gSpZalpysTwFHyc9HXJMDumE5C9rfBfHyFc/s320/John+Singer+Sargent+-+White+Walls+in+Sunlight+Morocco.jpg" width="320" /></a>In order to carry in his alleyway on Shabbat, one needs to adjust it by putting up a crossbeam on top or a post on the side, as we have seen multiple times before. This, however, is the opinion of Beit Hillel. By contrast, Beit Shammai require more: both a crossbeam and a side-post.
<br />
<br />
What is the reason for their disagreement, and what can we deduce from here about their basic points of view? Shall we say that Beit Shammai consider an area private only if it is surrounded by four walls, and that is why for  a three-walled alley they require an additional quasi-wall made of a crossbeam and a side post? – No! You cannot deduce this with certainty. It could be that in Beit Shammai's view three walls already create a private domain, so much so that one who throws an object from the street into an alley will already be liable for Shabbat violation. However, the Sages safeguarded the Shabbat by requiring further adjustment to the alley.
<br />
<br />
On the other hand, Beit Hillel require a beam in place of the fourth wall – is it clear to them that the third wall surely cannot be substituted by a beam, which means that three walls are a minimum to make a private domain? Again, not necessarily. It could be that Beit Hillel consider two walls sufficient, and will in fact make one liable for throwing an object into a two-walled partition. However, to permit carrying inside an alley they require a third wall and also a beam in place of the fourth.
<br />
<br />
Thus, we remain without definitive conclusions about their points of view.
<br />
<br />
Art: John Singer Sargent - White Walls in Sunlight Morocco

---

### content/eruvin/13.txt
<a id="src-00409"></a>

**Source file:** `content/eruvin/13.txt`

Eruvin 13 – The illumination of Rabbi Meir
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjGuXLQeFePCPQoyrcXZuUzvVjCN1G-vr8ZyQ6owadxClN_llqXT7-T67r3XLslQFpvVFAZUa91ExzQQpYzJ_R-Or8Yb2tEZmBHQpzdVV3nMrJ4TLc8dUlMa-pJ8mgYr13sZq3RGLe8mA-5/s1600/B.+Werner+-+Rabbis+in+a+debate.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="263" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjGuXLQeFePCPQoyrcXZuUzvVjCN1G-vr8ZyQ6owadxClN_llqXT7-T67r3XLslQFpvVFAZUa91ExzQQpYzJ_R-Or8Yb2tEZmBHQpzdVV3nMrJ4TLc8dUlMa-pJ8mgYr13sZq3RGLe8mA-5/s320/B.+Werner+-+Rabbis+in+a+debate.jpg" width="320" /></a>In reporting the <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2013/03/eruvin-12-crossbar-and-or-post.html">opinions of Beit Shammai and Beit Hillel</a>, the Talmud mentions Rabbi Meir, and continues with his story. Rabbi Meir initially came to study with Rabbi Akiva, but since Rabbi Akiva was a masterful logician, Rabbi Meir could never understand if his teacher was arguing a true point of view or just showing the logic of the opposite one. Therefore, Rabbi Meir went to Rabbi Ishmael, to get the facts straight, and then returned to Rabbi Akiva, and again learned the logic.
<br />
<br />
Rabbi Meir was a scribe, and to prevent the possibility of accidental erasure in the Torah – which could lead to great confusion, such as erasing the letter dalet slightly, making appear it is a resh, which would then spell not “God is one” but “another God” – he used indelible ink. His teacher told him to always use erasable ink, since there is a portion in the Torah, intended for a suspected wife, which one should erase in water, in preparing the test to remove suspicion.
<br />
<br />
Eventually Rabbi Meir himself became the leading Sage of his generation and now the other Sages could never ascertain whether he was arguing a true point of view, or a false one, just as convincingly. Since they could never fully understand him, they never established the law based on his opinion. Nevertheless, they benefited greatly from it, as he illuminated their eyes and minds with his reasoning. The student of Rabbi Meir, Sumchos, could present forty-eight reasons why a <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2012/07/niddah-56-creepy-crawly-in-alley.html">rat should be ritually impure</a> and forty-eight reasons why it should be otherwise. Ravina attempted one, by comparing to a snake, but was disproved.
<br />
<br />
Art: B. Werner - Rabbis in a debate

---

### content/eruvin/14.txt
<a id="src-00410"></a>

**Source file:** `content/eruvin/14.txt`

Eruvin 14 – The crossbeam has to be real
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEisVljLfP6CNGvER7HmkhDDbxB8nicPOpDdCDbYrh0zjG1-b7Q85TzWgOTs1StaWFISXWMFxffd70yfGnX0DQtTRy875lxLs5uIgh0pHNLlfxhcOp4NltNGHFFpcmcJw7zcjLBvkJefEmJ5/s1600/Vasily+Perov+-+Three+Apprentice+Workmen+Carrying+Water.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="235" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEisVljLfP6CNGvER7HmkhDDbxB8nicPOpDdCDbYrh0zjG1-b7Q85TzWgOTs1StaWFISXWMFxffd70yfGnX0DQtTRy875lxLs5uIgh0pHNLlfxhcOp4NltNGHFFpcmcJw7zcjLBvkJefEmJ5/s320/Vasily+Perov+-+Three+Apprentice+Workmen+Carrying+Water.jpg" width="320" /></a>The crossbeam that fixes an alley for carrying on Shabbat – and which was the subject of many a discussion hithertofore – has to be real: it needs to be able to support at least a half of a standard brick, which amounts to a hand-breadth; Rabbi Yehudah says that it only has to look right, not to be strong. What is the source for their disagreement? – The first teacher considers the crossbeam to be a reminder, thus, it has to be somewhat serious; Rabbi Yehudah says it is a symbolic fourth wall, and only has to look right.
<br />
<br />
By contrast, if one uses a side-post to delineate where the alley ends and the street begins – that side-post only has to be ten hand-breadths high, but it can be as thin as a thread. A side-post is more unusual than a crossbeam, and thus serves its purpose, whether as a symbolic wall or as a reminder.
<br />
<br />
Art: Vasily Perov - Three Apprentice Workmen Carrying Water

---

### content/eruvin/15.txt
<a id="src-00411"></a>

**Source file:** `content/eruvin/15.txt`

Eruvin 15 - Abaye wins
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjljjHD7V_LVsmOEQ7ql_aJGgaaDlOOrB7ugDdDnAP4ogm0AstsVyJhxwTUQWY1lrYZoo4JXTJz5kl63VWDFnJW20_gSGTscYKeYepgpljv4gSPbUVZQMOwQGtPxcuz43aa-oVMoRCfC_Hb/s1600/Caspar+David+Friedrich+-+Landscape+with+Grave,+Coffin+and+Owl.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEjljjHD7V_LVsmOEQ7ql_aJGgaaDlOOrB7ugDdDnAP4ogm0AstsVyJhxwTUQWY1lrYZoo4JXTJz5kl63VWDFnJW20_gSGTscYKeYepgpljv4gSPbUVZQMOwQGtPxcuz43aa-oVMoRCfC_Hb/s320/Caspar+David+Friedrich+-+Landscape+with+Grave,+Coffin+and+Owl.jpg" width="316" /></a>If a side-post was not erected specifically for observing Shabbat laws, but just happened to be there, will it work to permit carrying in the valley? Abaye says that it will – if they relied on it at the beginning of Sabbath – after all, they relied on it! However, Rava says that it does not help, since it was not made expressly for this purpose from the beginning. The Talmud lists a number of possible arguments pro and con, but Rava and Abaye remain unconvinced. The law, however, uncharacteristically follows Abaye – the side-post helps – and this is the "L" in the six cases abbreviated&nbsp;<a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2009/05/bava-metzia-21-lost-objects-that-finder.html">Y</a>&nbsp;<a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2010/03/sanhedrin-27-from-what-time-is-refuted.html">A</a>&nbsp;<a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2013/04/eruvin-15-abaye-wins.html">L</a>&nbsp;<a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2008/11/kiddushin-51-should-betrothal-allow.html">K</a>&nbsp;G&nbsp;<a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2010/03/sanhedrin-27-from-what-time-is-refuted.html">M</a>&nbsp;where the law follows Abaye against Rava.<br />
<br />
The side-post can be made of any material, and it can even be an animal. Here, however, Rabbi Meir disagrees – since anything that is alive cannot serve as a partition, according to him. Correspondingly, the Sages will say that an animal that is used as a coffin cover will become ritually impure, and Rabbi Meir will say that it won't. Tangentially, one can write a divorce document on an animal – but Rabbi Yose does not allow this. What are their reasons? Rabbi Yose says that the divorce document, or Get, is called in the Torah “The book (sefer) of separation.” Just as a book is not alive and does not eat – so must be the material for the divorce document. And the Sages? They understand the word “sefer” as “story,” which can be written on anything.
<br />
<br />
Art:  Caspar David Friedrich - Landscape with Grave, Coffin and Owl

---

### content/eruvin/16.txt
<a id="src-00412"></a>

**Source file:** `content/eruvin/16.txt`

Eruvin 16 – Shabbat in a caravan in the desert
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg2sxyKy5DvvuHqQH162nCOb3uG4Ma98Ww-Q59cSSBJs_SziYBvvRC-tGpz6hmaMCuVgGzlEf7SaJBGwTd_eu_C_fyF7MceuwrqaHnMsJfCXbCOQWKgqfNYeiPUnDiLxlA71t2yJ9Aqof6X/s1600/Edwin+Lord+Weeks+-+Arrival+Of+A+Caravan.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="192" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEg2sxyKy5DvvuHqQH162nCOb3uG4Ma98Ww-Q59cSSBJs_SziYBvvRC-tGpz6hmaMCuVgGzlEf7SaJBGwTd_eu_C_fyF7MceuwrqaHnMsJfCXbCOQWKgqfNYeiPUnDiLxlA71t2yJ9Aqof6X/s320/Edwin+Lord+Weeks+-+Arrival+Of+A+Caravan.jpg" width="320" /></a>If a caravan encamps in an open field, one cannot carry inside the caravan's area on Shabbat. Since this area lacks partitions, the Sages gave it the status of “<a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2012/10/shabbat-7-special-area-called-karmelit.html">karmelit</a>”, which is neither private nor public, but still one cannot carry there. Therefore, they may decide to make a fence&nbsp;around&nbsp;the caravan. Then the following rules apply.
<br />
<br />
If they surrounded their encampment with saddles, saddlebags, and the like, then they can carry there – provided that the height of the partition is at least ten hand-breadths, that the gaps between the saddles are not larger than the total length of their fence. In addition, each individual gap should not be larger than ten amot (about 20 feet), since such a gap is considered a door. More than this is considered an opening, and then one cannot carry there.
<br />
<br />
What if the length of the gaps is exactly equal to the total length of the closed fence? Is such partition valid or not? The Talmud spends a page trying to find a proof. In the end, since&nbsp;the verbiage of our ruling above is most easily understood if we assume that gaps equal to fence are valid, this become the law.<br />
<br />
Art: Edwin Lord Weeks - Arrival Of A Caravan

---

### content/eruvin/17.txt
<a id="src-00413"></a>

**Source file:** `content/eruvin/17.txt`

Eruvin 17 – Fence of ropes
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgs6VjUTf_33Af2geZwi-j8FGYsTMrNALijjTfPG27yF918iQqbLPJhOK2_hsWYyh136JFzG4p0LDC21wvpk2RtO_w6V_Wpl6W49Yl_v9n7B0e0ofNdjHucsSJQADsk-HjOAb56kjn8SXU2/s1600/Francesco+Peluso+-+An+Algerian+Caravan+At+Rest.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="152" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEgs6VjUTf_33Af2geZwi-j8FGYsTMrNALijjTfPG27yF918iQqbLPJhOK2_hsWYyh136JFzG4p0LDC21wvpk2RtO_w6V_Wpl6W49Yl_v9n7B0e0ofNdjHucsSJQADsk-HjOAb56kjn8SXU2/s320/Francesco+Peluso+-+An+Algerian+Caravan+At+Rest.jpg" width="320" /></a>Another possibility to spend <a href="http://mkerzner.blogspot.com/2013/04/eruvin-16-shabbat-in-caravan-in-desert.html">Shabbat in a caravan in a desert</a> is to surround it with ropes: they can stretch three ropes at a distance of three hand-breadths from each other. If the thickness of the ropes together adds up to a hand-breadth, then they have a valid fence ten hand-breadths high. They could also surround their camp with vertical poles, ten hand-breadths high, and place them at three hand-breadths from each other.
<br />
<br />
How does this work? It relies on the principles of “Closing”, “Lavud” in Hebrew, which states that a gap of three hand-breadths can be considered closed for the purposes of Shabbat, ritual purity, and other similar laws where partitions are involved. 
<br />
<br />
However, there are those who disagree. Rabbi Yehudah limits the partition of ropes only for a caravan of three or more people. His son Rabbi Yose is even more strict: he says that any partition that does not have criss-cross elements is not a partition. The Sages, however, say that a partition can be either vertical or horizontal.
<br />
<br />
Wait a minute! The Sages are repeating themselves!? – This is another group of Sages, and they differ with the first one in permitting such partition even for an individual at home, not in a desert.
<br />
<br />
Art: Francesco Peluso - An Algerian Caravan At Rest

---

### content/eruvin/2.txt
<a id="src-00416"></a>

**Source file:** `content/eruvin/2.txt`

Eruvin 2 - Houses, courtyard, alley
<a href="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhchCvr3OKvWGZ_Td-AWPfFj_rClgNn-LGDvb2OmdLNGFblF26HRr2tdcB9Q3KxRA4uK4JwTRxxuJlRTqXii_25_UPWsZFUYUB98ObCwxR18eMmxspBz_6itxpIdIgRQ9xU-MUII0-N5PcJ/s1600/Gillis+van+Tilborgh+-+An+Elegant+Company+Eating,+Drinking+And+Smoking+In+The+Courtyard.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"><img border="0" height="320" src="https://blogger.googleusercontent.com/img/b/R29vZ2xl/AVvXsEhchCvr3OKvWGZ_Td-AWPfFj_rClgNn-LGDvb2OmdLNGFblF26HRr2tdcB9Q3KxRA4uK4JwTRxxuJlRTqXii_25_UPWsZFUYUB98ObCwxR18eMmxspBz_6itxpIdIgRQ9xU-MUII0-N5PcJ/s320/Gillis+van+Tilborgh+-+An+Elegant+Company+Eating,+Drinking+And+Smoking+In+The+Courtyard.jpg" width="317" /></a>The Talmud assumes the following organization of houses.<br />
<br />
Several houses open into a courtyard, and several courtyards open into an alley. Usually the alley has one of its ends closed, so strictly speaking all of these areas are private domains, and one should be allowed to carry from any house to any house, in the courtyard and in the alley.<br />
<br />
However, since these structures are similar to public areas, like a street, and since one can confuse the two and come to carry in the street, the Sages prohibited carrying between the houses through the courtyard and between the courtyard through the alley - unless some preparations have been made. A symbolic fourth wall has to be created, even if it just a beam across, and common food has to be stored, making all residents as if one family.<br />
<br />
A beam that is placed across the entrance into an alley must not be higher than twenty amot (about 40 feet). If it is higher, it must be placed lower. The Talmud immediately asks: we will learn that a <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sukkah">sukkah</a> must not be higher than twenty amot, and if it is higher than that, it is invalid. Why "invalid" for sukkah but "placed lower" for an alley? The answer: since the sukkah requirement is dictated by the Torah, then the Sages just tell you the law, "invalid." The beam over an alley, however, is dictated by the Sages themselves, and as they explain it, they can also tell you how to fix it.<br />
<br />
Or, if you want, I can give you another explanation. Since the laws of the sukkah are numerous (shade, sun, walls, etc.) it is easier to just say "invalid" and let you find a way to fix it. The laws of an alley are relatively simpler, and the Sages can start teaching them right away by saying "place it lower."<br />
<br />
<br />
Art: Gillis van Tilborgh - An Elegant Company Eating, Drinking And Smoking In The Courtyard

---

### content/eruvin/24.txt
